Rejected because it forces a yaml-vs-toml-vs-json file-format decision, a `.reviewbot/` vs `.warden/` location decision, and a `noise.always` / `noise.never` / `knownDebt` schema decision under noise-filter time pressure. Each of those is its own design surface; collapsing them produces undergrilled choices.

- _Tiny CLI flag escape hatch (`--noise-never=path/`)._ Skip the yaml overlay entirely; ship `--noise-never` and `--noise-always` flags. Rejected because per-invocation flags don't survive across runs (the user has to remember to pass them every `warden review`), and the failure mode of ADR-0022 (zero-config posture) is exactly "tools that need configuration on every invocation are tools that don't get used." A persistent file-based override surface is the right shape; M10 builds it properly.

- _Keep directory-concentration heuristic as profile-miss fallback._ Profile runs first; heuristic fires when no profile match was found. Rejected because the heuristic produces real false positives on legitimate large refactors (1K-file rename inside `packages/api/`); without overlay, false positives have no remediation. Profile-only loses the project-specific-dump coverage but gains zero false positives. Net trade favors profile-only in M9.

- _Build the tree from `git diff --raw` via a CLI-side capture._ CLI invokes `git diff --raw` and passes raw output to core alongside unified diff. Rejected because it doubles `ReviewInput`'s surface for one consumer (the noise filter) and makes future bot wrappers (`apps/github-bot/`) require a raw-diff source they don't otherwise need. Deriving counts from `parseUnifiedDiff()`'s output avoids the new field entirely.

- _Keep the (added, modified, deleted) triplet on tree nodes._ Rejected — no current consumer reads anything other than file count. Add the triplet when a downstream consumer (M10 directory-level deadcode, M11+ tree-aware diff analyzer) actually needs it. Same "build the seam, don't fill it" rejection ADR-0018 / ADR-0019 / ADR-0021 / ADR-0023 each made.

- _Put lockfiles in `alwaysNoise.files`._ The first-draft profile listed `package-lock.json` / `pnpm-lock.yaml` / `yarn.lock`. Rejected because lockfile presence in the diff is _signal_ — vuln runs independently, ESLint and TSC filter by extension, and the synthesizer prompt benefits from the "dep-bump PR" context. Pruning them costs context without benefit.

- _Keep schema versioning (`version: 1` in profile JSON)._ YAGNI for one profile in v0; reintroduce when profile schema actually evolves and a migration is real.

- _Fold Tier-1 baseline into the JS profile._ Rejected — `.DS_Store`, `.git/`, `.vscode/.history/` are OS / editor noise unrelated to JS. A future Python profile would redeclare them. Language-agnostic floor in the loader scales; profile-embedded does not.

- _Ship full ADR-0022 design as written._ Multi-ecosystem detector + 7 profiles + overlay loader + structural fallback in one milestone. Rejected as a milestone-and-a-half of work that violates the single-architectural-commit pattern. ADR-0022 read like a single direction; ADR-0025 disambiguates it into one v0 commit + several M10+ follow-ups, each its own milestone.

**Caveats.**

- _Caveat — narrows ADR-0022; does not retract it._ ADR-0022's architectural shape (single seam, ecosystem-driven, profile-loaded, depth-limited tree, one degraded entry per pruned subtree, override via overlay) all hold. ADR-0025 narrows the _v0 coverage_ (one profile, no overlay, no fallback) without weakening any architectural commitment. Future M10 work realizes the deferred commitments without redesigning the architecture.

- _Caveat — overlay is the named M10 milestone, not a vague "later."_ M10 is sized to: yaml parser dep, file-format decision, schema (`knownDebt` + `noise.always` + `noise.never` at minimum), location (likely `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` per ADR-0008's existing reference, but the location debate is M10's not M9's), loader integration with diff prune. ADR-0008's reference to the overlay is honored _retroactively_ by M10's shipping; the dangling reference between M3 (when `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` first got named) and M10 is acknowledged technical debt.

- _Caveat — multi-ecosystem detector is the named M11+ milestone._ Detector rewrite is bigger than overlay: marker-file precedence rules, monorepo per-subtree detection, priority on conflicting markers, `EcosystemId[]` shape, profile-union semantics. M11+ takes it up with its own ADR. M9 → M10 → M11+ is the implied sequence; sequence may shuffle if dogfood demands it.

- _Caveat — false positives during the M9 → M10 overlay gap are accepted._ If a user has a project-specific generated directory the JS profile doesn't list, M9 doesn't prune it, runners process it normally, and the catastrophic-case smoke fixture's wall-clock target (< 5s) may fail on that one repo. The user can fix `.gitignore` to address it (the same workaround that exists today). The honest framing is "M9 closes the JS-`node_modules/` catastrophic case decisively; project-specific noise dumps wait for M10's overlay."

- _Caveat — degraded `topic: "noise-filter"` is permanent vocabulary._ ADR-0022 introduced the topic name; ADR-0025 keeps it. Listed alongside the conventional topic list (`context`, `osv`, `gitignore`, `committability`, `scalability`, `deadcode`, `consistency`, `embeddings`, `schema`, `llm`, `vuln`).

- _Caveat — `committability.ts` cleanup is part of M9._ Removing the directory-concentration heuristic and the duplicated Tier-1 hard-skip list from `committability.ts` is part of M9's diff. The committability sub-agent continues to function, just without its noise-filtering responsibility (which the diff loader now owns universally).

- _Caveat — m9-plan.md's "open design questions" §1–§7 are answered by this ADR._ §1 (per-subtree ecosystem) — moot under JS-only. §2 (ecosystem coverage) — JS only. §3 (profile schema) — alwaysNoise.{directories, extensions} only. §4 (α vs β interface) — already locked by ADR-0023 §5; β stays. §5 (structural heuristics) — dropped. §6 (caching) — no. §7 (degraded-entry verbosity) — one entry per pruned subtree, default mode shows actionable kind, no collapse (per-subtree visibility is a trust feature, especially under JS-only where 1–2 entries is the common case).

- _Caveat — design is locked; implementation specifics live in m9-plan.md._ ADR-0025 is the design commit; the rewritten m9-plan.md is the implementation brief. Future agents read both; ADR-0025 is the authority on design questions, m9-plan.md on file-by-file scope.

**Status.** Direction. Grilling pass complete (Q1 → Q6 + ADR-shape). Implementation tracked in the rewritten `m9-plan.md`.

---

## ADR-0026 — M11: tool-augmented formatter + API claim verifier via `.d.ts` lookup

**Decision.** M11 picks exactly one item from ADR-0019's M10+ deferral list — cross-repo / `node_modules` / `.d.ts` retrieval — and narrows it to the smallest credible cut that earns its rent: **`.d.ts` lookup, lookup-on-demand cache, tool-augmented formatter as the producer, API claim verifier as the post-pass consumer.** The architectural keystone framing is that this single item unblocks two named M10+ deferrals — the `leverage` review category (memory: `project_warden_leverage_category.md`) and the API claim verifier (memory: `project_warden_verify_api_claims.md`) — both of which extend ADR-0008's citation thesis to library API claims. M11 ships the _verifier_ half of that pair; the `leverage` category waits for its own M12+ ADR. The keystone narrows along five axes against the broader bag the deferral list named: (1) `.d.ts` only, no `node_modules/<pkg>/src` chunking. (2) Lookup-on-demand cache, not bulk indexing — no Voyage call for type definitions. (3) Tool-augmented formatter as producer (extends the existing M4/M8 formatter via AI SDK tool use), not a new `leverage` sub-agent. (4) No sibling repos — that's its own deferred concept per CONTEXT.md §8. (5) No `warden index export/import` CLI verbs, no daemon `JobRunner`, no cloud-hosted index, no BYOEmbedder, no mid-stream key handling, no retrieval refinements — each stays in the M10+ basket for its own future ADR. The architectural commitments from ADR-0019 — content-addressed cache, model-versioning discipline, single-consumer posture, smallest-credible-cut — all hold; the _scope_ narrows to what one verifier needs.

The full surface:

1. **Single deferred item, no bundle.** ADR-0019's M10+ list collectively names eight separable deferrals (BYOEmbedder, cross-repo retrieval, SAST worker, export/import CLI, daemon JobRunner, cloud-hosted index, mid-stream keys, retrieval refinements) plus three rooted in other memory (self-aware boss, leverage category, API claim verifier). M11 schedules exactly one — `.d.ts` retrieval + its verifier consumer — to preserve the single-architectural-commit discipline established by ADR-0018 / ADR-0019 / ADR-0021 / ADR-0023 / ADR-0025. The other ten deferrals stay deferred until they earn their own milestone.

2. **`.d.ts` only; no source chunking, no sibling repos.** ADR-0019's M10+ entry phrased the retrieval scope as "cross-repo / `node_modules` / `.d.ts` retrieval" — three orthogonal directions bundled into one name. The named follow-on consumers (leverage, API claim verifier) both treat the library's `.d.ts` as the source of truth for "does this symbol exist / what's its shape." Neither needs the package's source code. Indexing `node_modules/<pkg>/src` (~100s of MB per dep-heavy repo) spikes Voyage cost and `.warden/cache.sqlite` size for capability neither M11 consumer requires. Sibling repos are a separately-named deferred concept (CONTEXT.md §8) with their own change-detection surface, security model, and `--sibling-repo` UX — they earn their own future ADR if and when scheduled.

3. **Lookup-on-demand cache, not bulk indexing.** The keystone framing originally implied "extend the M6 Voyage path to `.d.ts`." A second look says the verifier's only need is _exact symbol lookup_ — `lookupTypeDef('drizzle-orm', 'with')` — not semantic retrieval. Eager bulk indexing (~500 packages × ~50 top-level symbols × ~500 bytes/row ≈ 25–50 MB per repo) stores rows the LLM will never query; cache size grows with repo size, not with usage. Lookup-on-demand inverts that: cache only what the LLM actually asks about (typically a handful of symbols per review); storage stays <1 MB per repo; `warden init` is not extended (its three phases stay walk → chunk → embed for the M6 source-code index). Cache invalidation is automatic via `(package, version)` mismatch — `npm install`-driven version bumps produce new cache rows; old rows become unreachable. ADR-0016's content-addressed discipline survives — the cache key is `(package, version, symbol)`, content-addressed in the sense that re-resolving the same triple in the same install state is idempotent. **Voyage is not invoked for `.d.ts` in M11.** The "cross-repo retrieval" keystone narrows from "retrieval" to "lookup" to match the consumer.

4. **Tool-augmented formatter as the producer; defer `leverage` sub-agent.** The verifier post-pass is a no-op without a producer emitting `api_def` sources. Four producer shapes were considered (Q3): (a) tool-augmented formatter; (b) new `leverage` Haiku sub-agent; (c) pre-emit deterministic detector; (d) both. M11 picks (a) — extend the existing M4/M8 formatter LLM with a `lookupTypeDef({ package, symbol })` tool via AI SDK v6's `tool()` primitive. Tool results become `api_def` sources on revised `Comment.sources[]`. Verifier post-pass validates those sources structurally. The `leverage` category as a priority-order slot (per ADR-0020) is left for M12+ with its own grilling — leverage adds a `CategoryEnum` entry, a prompt slot, per-category confidence tuning, and probably its own Haiku sub-agent; bundling it into M11 doubles the surface and forces both bets at once. Memory `project_warden_verify_api_claims.md` allows this framing — its "Will likely require boss/worker orchestration" caveat is satisfied by M8's spine (the formatter is the boss; the tool is one shape of worker).

5. **Tool return shape: discriminated union, not all-optional bag.** `LookupTypeDefResult` is a discriminated union on `found: true | false`. The `found: true` variant carries `{ package, version, symbol, signature, kind, jsdoc: string | null, dts_file, line_start, line_end }`; the `found: false` variant carries `{ package, symbol, reason: "package_not_installed" | "no_types" | "symbol_not_found" | "lookup_error" }`. The `reason` enum lets the LLM treat system-level failures (`package_not_installed` → degrade silently) differently from semantic failures (`symbol_not_found` → genuine "no such API" claim). `lookup_error` is the fallback for unexpected parser crashes; the LLM treats it like `package_not_installed`. `jsdoc: string | null` (not optional) — explicit "looked, none present" vs the structural absence the union already encodes via `found: false`.

6. **LLM-decided mid-synthesis tool calls + 4-trigger prompt rule + cap=8 calls per review.** AI SDK v6's native tool-use loop (`streamText({ tools, stopWhen: stepCountIs(8) })`) hosts the tool calls. The LLM decides when to call based on four concrete triggers articulated in the system prompt: (i) a TSC diagnostic mentions a library type/method/property and the formatter wants to refine or contradict the diagnostic; (ii) the formatter is about to assert that a library has (or lacks) a specific method/field/type/parameter/behavior; (iii) the formatter is about to recommend refactoring toward a library primitive; (iv) the formatter is about to contradict the user's library usage. The cap (`stepCountIs(8)`) is a guardrail against pathological spirals; based on dogfood evidence it tunes up or down in M12+, but lives in code (not env) for v0. **Pre-resolving all imported symbols upfront was rejected** — it's the over-eager version that pays for verification the formatter mostly doesn't need; the four triggers encode the "look up when something feels off" instinct, not "look up everything."

7. **Discipline: tool-required for library claims via prompt; verifier validates structurally; uncited claims slip through (accepted).** The prompt addition forbids library claims without first calling `lookupTypeDef`; the verifier post-pass validates `api_def` sources structurally (substring-match `signature` against `dts_file:line_start..line_end`). The two layers combine into defense-in-depth: prompt makes citation the natural path; verifier catches cited-but-wrong cases. A library claim _without_ an `api_def` source — i.e., the LLM violated the prompt and asserted without citing — does not get caught by the structural verifier. This gap is real and accepted. It is the same epistemic floor as the rest of the citation-discipline system: the prompt prevents un-cited claims; the verifier catches cited-but-wrong claims; the combined coverage is "best-effort + structurally-verified." Self-tagging via a `Comment.api_claims[]` field (which would close the gap structurally) was rejected as too ambitious — self-tagging adds a new failure mode (under-tagging) on top of the existing one (under-citing); it doesn't earn its surface.

8. **Verifier post-pass extends M10's substring-verifier on the same algorithm.** ADR-0021 §3 + M10's `verify-citations.ts` already substring-checks `{path, line, snippet}` triples against the cited file at `line ± DRIFT` (currently `line ± 5`). The `api_def` source maps onto the same triple: `path = dts_file`, `line = line_start`, `snippet = signature`. M11's verifier extension is the **same algorithm**, applied to a source variant where the `path` lives in `node_modules/` instead of the repo root. Re-uses M10's whitespace normalization, the same drop semantics (failed source dropped; if all sources on a Comment drop, the Comment drops), and the same `degradedWorkers` surfacing (`kind: "info", topic: "llm"`) plus a new topic `"api-claim-verifier"` for forensic distinction. **No new verifier file; extend `verify-citations.ts`.**

9. **Schema: reuse `SourceSchema`'s existing M10 triple; add `'api_def'` to `SourceTypeEnum`.** `SourceSchema` already carries `{ type, url?, id?, title?, retrievedAt, path?, line?, snippet? }` with the all-or-nothing refinement on the M10 triple. The `api_def` source variant reuses every existing field: `type: 'api_def'`, `path = dts_file`, `line = line_start`, `snippet = signature`, `id = '${package}@${version}#${symbol}'`, `title = '${kind} ${symbol}'`, `retrievedAt = ISO timestamp`. No new schema fields. Single-line enum change. `lineEnd` is intentionally lost — multi-line signatures still substring-match against `line ± DRIFT`; if dogfood reveals signatures regularly exceed the drift window, bump DRIFT in `verify-citations.ts` rather than denormalize the schema.

10. **Failure surfacing: silent per-symbol; one `degradedWorkers` entry on missing `node_modules/`.** Per-symbol misses (`symbol_not_found`, `no_types`) return the discriminated-union result; the LLM drops the claim cleanly. No `degradedWorkers` entry per miss — that path is _normal operation_. A _system-level_ failure (the `node_modules/` directory doesn't exist at all — likely scenario: someone running `warden review` on a fresh-cloned PR before `npm install`) surfaces exactly one `degradedWorkers` entry per review with `kind: "actionable", topic: "api-claim-verifier"` and the message "no `node_modules/` directory — library API verification unavailable; run `npm install` to enable." Detection: `fs.existsSync(repoRoot + '/node_modules')` once at first tool-call time, cached for the rest of the review. Per-package misses are _not_ collapsed into entries — that's the verbosity middle ground (Q8 option C) rejected as still-noisy on big diffs. Mirrors M9's noise-filter philosophy ("loud about subtrees, quiet about individual files").

11. **Package boundaries: `tool` re-exports from `@warden/ai`; tool descriptor lives in `@warden/core/src/llm/tools/`.** `@warden/ai` already re-exports `streamText`, `generateText`, `Output` from `ai` (per `packages/ai/src/index.ts`) — the precedent for "AI SDK primitives flow through `@warden/ai`." Adding `tool` to the re-exports is one line. The tool descriptor (`lookupTypeDef` wrapped via `tool({ inputSchema, execute })`) lives in `packages/core/src/llm/tools/lookup-type-def.ts`; the resolver function (the actual `.d.ts` walking + caching) lives in `packages/core/src/api/lookup-type-def.ts`. CLAUDE.md's package-boundary table is honored unchanged — `@warden/core` consumes `@warden/ai` (allowed); `@warden/ai` does not consume `@warden/core`. **No new `WardenTool` interface abstraction.** The existing re-export pattern is sufficient; an abstraction would be a premature commitment to a multi-call-site shape the M11 surface doesn't justify.

12. **Cascade integration: tools threaded into `streamText`; `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)`; cache key gains `dependenciesHash`.** `callWithCascade()` in `packages/core/src/llm/cascade.ts` accepts an optional `tools` argument (typed `Record<string, Tool>`) and forwards it into the `streamText({ ... tools, stopWhen })` call. Tool calls flow through the existing ai-retry path — fallback (Anthropic → retry → Google per ADR-0017) applies to tool-using calls identically; transient failures retry the whole step, including any prior tool calls (AI SDK's tool-use loop is a step-level construct). The M4 LLM cache (`computeCacheKey` in `packages/core/src/llm/cache.ts`) keys on `(modelId, systemPromptHash, userTemplateHash, inputCommentIds, diffHash)`. Tool-using calls add a new input: `node_modules/` state. M11 extends the cache key with `dependenciesHash` (sha256 of `package-lock.json` / `pnpm-lock.yaml` / `yarn.lock` content — first one found at `repoRoot`; empty string if none). When no tools are used (legacy code paths, no library claims made), the cache key still matches because `dependenciesHash` is appended uniformly to all keys; existing M4 cache entries miss exactly once on the first M11 review and refill on the next.

13. **Tool exposed to formatter only in M11; committability sub-agent and future sub-agents stay tool-less until their own ADR.** The committability sub-agent (M7 close-out) has its own prompt + Haiku-tier model selection + grilling pass; it doesn't make library claims, doesn't need `lookupTypeDef`. Broadening the tool exposure surface to all sub-agents is reversible but premature — each sub-agent's tool budget, prompt impact, and verifier exposure deserves its own grilling. M11 ships the formatter integration only; future sub-agents bind the tool through the same `tools: {}` argument when their ADR explicitly schedules it.

14. **Forward compatibility for `leverage`: additive `type_def_embeddings` table, no rewrite.** When `leverage` ships (M12+), it likely wants semantic search over `.d.ts` ("find Drizzle's join-related primitives") in addition to exact lookup. The M11 `type_def_cache` table stores per-symbol records; embeddings layer atop them as a separate `type_def_embeddings` table keyed on `(package, version, symbol, model_id, model_version)`. Same content-addressed discipline as M6's `embeddings` table. Symbol-table-only is a _strict subset_ of what an embedding-augmented lookup offers; the M11 cache stays useful as the exact-match fast path even after embeddings exist.

**Why.**

- _The single-deferred-item discipline._ Same posture as ADR-0018 / ADR-0019 / ADR-0021 / ADR-0023 / ADR-0025. ADR-0019's M10+ list is a _bag_, not a milestone schedule; M11 picks one item with the biggest downstream dependency cascade and ships the narrowest credible cut. Picking three (e.g., `.d.ts` + BYOEmbedder + export/import CLI) would conflate three architectural commits in one milestone; if dogfood reveals quality issues, attribution is muddled. One milestone = one architectural commit.

- _Architectural keystone framing._ The Q1 grilling framed M11's pick-criterion as "biggest downstream dependency cascade." Cross-repo retrieval was the only M10+ item that _gates two named follow-on M10+ items_ (leverage category, API claim verifier) — every other deferral is either standalone (BYOEmbedder, daemon JobRunner, export/import CLI) or speculative without evidence (retrieval refinements, mid-stream keys). Shipping the keystone first makes M12 and M13 small; shipping anything else first leaves the keystone deferred and both follow-ons stuck. Honors ADR-0001's single-user-built-right posture: dogfooding pacing favors unblocking-the-most-things over architectural ambition.

- _Lookup-on-demand over bulk indexing._ The grilling pass (Q4) surfaced the table-bloat concern explicitly. Eager bulk indexing stores ~25–50 MB of rows the LLM mostly won't query; lookup-on-demand stores <1 MB scaling with usage. The trade-off is first-query latency (parse `.d.ts`, walk re-exports — tens of ms typical, hundreds for `@types/node`-sized type files) for a 25–50× storage reduction. The latency cost is paid inside an LLM call already running 10s+; storage cost is paid forever. Storage wins.

- _Tool-augmented formatter as producer, defer leverage category._ Q3 framing: a sub-agent (`leverage`) adds enum entry + prompt slot + per-category confidence + new Haiku tier model selection. The formatter (extended with one tool) makes library claims natively when the four triggers fire. Same epistemic floor (citation-discipline-via-prompt + structural verifier) at a fraction of the engineering surface. `leverage` as a _category_ deserves its own grilling; M11 is "the verifier earns rent against the existing producer," not "the leverage category ships."

- _Four triggers, not laundry list._ Q7's compress-to-2-trigger alternative would fold (i) and (iii) into "library API claim" — but the four triggers cover distinct _scenarios_: refining a TSC diagnostic, asserting library shape, recommending a refactor, contradicting user code. Explicit is better than collapsed when the prompt is small; the formatter system prompt is currently ~6KB, four triggers add ~400 bytes. The cost-to-clarity ratio favors explicit.

- _Mid-synthesis tool calls, not pre-resolved._ Q7 alternative C (pre-resolve every imported symbol upfront) does extra work that 90% of the time isn't queried by the formatter. AI SDK's native tool-use loop is the path of least engineering — `streamText({ tools, stopWhen })` is one config block, not a separate symbol-extraction pipeline. The cap=8 keeps it self-limiting.

- _Verifier symmetry with M10's substring-verifier._ The M10 `{path, line, snippet}` triple invariant on `SourceSchema` was designed to be "the architectural primitive future producers inherit verification through." `api_def` is the first such producer, and proves the design works: zero new verifier file, zero new substring algorithm, just one extension to `verify-citations.ts`'s source-walking. The M10 grilling's promised architectural dividend pays out in M11.

- _Reuse SourceSchema, not new fields._ Adding 5+ optional fields to `SourceSchema` for the `api_def` variant would bloat the schema. Reusing `path` / `line` / `snippet` / `id` / `title` for the type-def metadata keeps the schema lean and the verifier's source walk algorithm shared. The schema is now richer in _meaning_ (one `type` variant) without being richer in _fields_; same posture as ADR-0021 §3's M10 triple addition.

- _Failure surfacing matches M9's noise-filter philosophy._ "Loud about system-level issues, quiet about per-item normal-operation results." Missing `node_modules/` is system-level (the user can act: `npm install`). Per-symbol misses are normal-operation results the LLM handles cleanly via the discriminated union. The middle-ground "one entry per missed package" was rejected as still-noisy on big diffs.

- _`@warden/ai` re-exports `tool` (precedent)._ The existing `streamText` / `generateText` / `Output` re-exports already established the pattern: AI SDK primitives flow through `@warden/ai`. Adding `tool` is a one-line change; building a `WardenTool` abstraction would prematurely commit to a multi-call-site shape M11 doesn't have.

- _Cache key gains `dependenciesHash`._ Tool-using calls produce results that depend on `node_modules/` state; the M4 cache key without it would over-hit (cached comments include claims about a now-removed library symbol). Lockfile hash is the canonical proxy for "what packages and versions are installed" — single read at the top of `formatReview()`. Old M4 cache entries miss once on the first M11 review (the new field shifts all keys); refill on the next; not a regression.

**Alternatives considered and rejected.**

- _Pick a different M10+ item._ BYOEmbedder (engine-maturity), daemon JobRunner (skip-init UX), custom-code SAST worker (capability gap), self-aware boss (security boundary), `warden index export/import` (productize). Each has merit; none has the same "unblocks two named M10+ items" dependency cascade. The keystone framing (Q1) explicitly favored cascade over the other three signals (dogfood pain, engine maturity, capability gap). Rejecting alternatives preserves the M12+ menu for whichever signal becomes loudest after M11 dogfood.

- _Cross-repo retrieval at full scope (`.d.ts` + `node_modules/<pkg>/src` + sibling repos)._ Maximum cascade per milestone. Rejected because (a) `node_modules/<pkg>/src` is 10–100× the volume of `.d.ts` and ADR-0019's caveat explicitly named the cost spike on dep-heavy repos; (b) sibling repos have a different change-detection surface (each sibling needs its own merkle + file_state), a different security model (indexing code outside the working directory), and their own `--sibling-repo` UX — all are M12+ grilling material on their own. Full-scope is a milestone-and-a-half. Narrow-scope earns rent and informs the next slice.

- _Bulk-index `.d.ts` upfront via M6's Voyage path._ Reuse the existing `chunks` + `embeddings` tables. Rejected because (a) `voyage-code-3` is trained for source code, not type signatures — the embedding quality on `.d.ts` is unproven; (b) the M11 consumer (verifier) needs exact lookup, not semantic retrieval; (c) embedding `.d.ts` for ~500 packages at typical repo scale costs $0.20–$0.50 per repo for capability we don't ship in M11. Defer embedding to when `leverage` (the consumer that _would_ use semantic retrieval) actually ships.

- _Per-symbol bulk indexing into a new `type_defs` table (eager but no Voyage)._ Stores all top-level exports + class/interface members at `init` time, no embeddings. Storage ~25–50 MB per repo. Rejected (Q4) because _most rows are dead weight_ — the LLM queries a handful of symbols per review, not the whole `node_modules/`. Lookup-on-demand stores only what's queried (<1 MB) with the same lookup latency for cached symbols and acceptable first-query latency for novel ones.

- _Hybrid metadata-only pre-index._ Pre-index `package.json#types` pointers at `init`; resolve symbols lazily. Saves a parse step per query. Rejected (Q4) — the parse step is fast enough to not earn the metadata table; storage minimization principle dominates.

- _Bundle `leverage` sub-agent in M11 (Q3 option D)._ Ship API claim verifier _and_ leverage category together. Rejected because `leverage` is a category-shaped commitment — new `CategoryEnum` entry, new `PRIORITY_ORDER` placement (ADR-0020), new per-category prompt slot, new Haiku sub-agent prompt with its own grilling, new per-category confidence threshold. Bundling doubles the surface and forces two architectural bets at once; M11 ships verifier proof, M12+ ships leverage category with its own ADR.

- _Pre-emit deterministic detector (Q3 option C)._ Walk the diff for library-symbol references deterministically; check `.d.ts`; emit findings without LLM. Rejected because the _interesting_ leverage cases are LLM-reasoned (refactor recommendations, contextual fitness), not symbol-grep-able. A detector here is limited to "symbol doesn't exist in installed version" — narrow, but the LLM does this case better with broader context. Detector-only forecloses the broader case for a narrow win.

- _Self-tagging via `Comment.api_claims[]` (Q6 option C)._ LLM self-tags library references; verifier checks each tag has a source. Closes the gap structurally — but introduces a new failure mode (under-tagging) on top of the existing one (under-citing). Schema bloat. Rejected as too ambitious; the gap (uncited claims slip through) is accepted at the same epistemic floor as the rest of the system.

- _Pre-resolve every imported symbol upfront (Q7 option C)._ Pipeline extracts `(package, symbol)` pairs from imports + TSC findings, looks them all up before the formatter runs. Formatter sees facts; no tool calls. Predictable cost. Rejected as the over-eager version — does extra work for 90% of imports the formatter doesn't make claims about, and replaces AI-SDK-native tool use with a custom symbol-extraction pipeline.

- _Hybrid: pre-resolve TSC-mentioned symbols + ad-hoc tool (Q7 option D)._ Balances eagerness with selectivity. Rejected because it adds pipeline complexity (a second resolver path) for a marginal gain over the four-trigger LLM-decided path. Defer hybrid until dogfood reveals a specific gap.

- _Voyage `voyage-code-3` for `.d.ts` retrieval._ Same as bulk-index alternative above; rejected for the same reasons. Re-rejected to make the "no Voyage for `.d.ts`" decision explicit — M11 ships _cross-repo lookup_, not _cross-repo retrieval_ in the M6 sense.

- _User-global cache at `~/.warden/cache.sqlite`._ Cross-repo sharing — `drizzle-orm@0.30.0` types are identical across every repo. Theoretically reduces wasted re-resolution. Rejected because ADR-0007 fixes the cache at the per-repo `.warden/cache.sqlite` location and decentralized caching avoids version-resolution conflicts between repos pinning different `drizzle-orm` versions. Revisit if dogfood shows the per-repo duplication is a real storage problem; it isn't at <1 MB per repo.

- _Webfetch fallback for uninstalled packages._ When `lookupTypeDef('drizzle-orm', 'with')` returns `package_not_installed`, fetch from the npm registry or unpkg.com instead. Captured in memory `project_warden_verify_api_claims.md` as the "long-tail fallback." Rejected for M11 because it (a) introduces network I/O at LLM-call time inside `@warden/core` (currently I/O-pure for HTTP); (b) needs caching policy decisions (CDN ETags, retention TTL); (c) opens supply-chain attack vectors (untrusted CDN content flowing into LLM context). Future milestone if a real consumer earns rent. M11 surfaces the missing-package case via the single `degradedWorkers` entry; the user runs `npm install` to enable verification.

- _Expose the tool to all sub-agents._ Lets committability and future sub-agents call `lookupTypeDef`. Rejected for M11 — committability has its own prompt + grilling pass; expanding its tool surface deserves its own grilling. Tool exposure broadens reversibly when a sub-agent earns the addition.

- _Cap=4 or cap=16 tool calls per review._ Cap=8 is a guess. Rejected the alternatives because no dogfood evidence favors either bound. Cap is a code constant in M11; tunable in M12+ if dogfood shows the bound is wrong. Code-not-env to keep the tuning visible in commits.

- _Build `WardenTool` interface in `@warden/core`; adapt to `ai.tool()` in `@warden/ai`._ Mirror-image of `getBossModel()`'s indirection. Rejected because `@warden/ai` already re-exports AI SDK primitives directly (`streamText`, `Output`); adding `tool` to the re-export list is one line. The abstraction would commit to a multi-call-site shape M11 doesn't have. Revisit if a second tool emerges and the call sites diverge.

**Caveats.**

- _Caveat — the structural-verifier gap is accepted._ The verifier validates `api_def` sources that _exist_ on a Comment. A library claim _without_ an `api_def` source (the LLM violated the prompt and asserted without citing) is not caught structurally. This is the same epistemic floor as the rest of the citation-discipline system (the formatter is told not to invent assertions; nothing structurally enforces the absence). M11 honors that floor; closing it requires self-tagging or post-pass NLP, both rejected in Q6. If dogfood evidence shows uncited library claims slip through frequently enough to hurt, M12+ revisits with the self-tagging shape its own grilling considers.

- _Caveat — cap=8 is a guess; tune in M12+._ The cap exists to bound pathological spirals (LLM in a loop calling the tool). Dogfood may show 8 is too tight (cuts off useful verification chains) or too loose (LLM still spirals on edge cases). Code constant in `cascade.ts`; one-line bump when dogfood says so. Not an env var in v0 — keeping it in code makes the tuning visible in commits.

- _Caveat — `.d.ts` resolution edge cases are real engineering._ Re-exports (`export * from 'sub'`), conditional exports (`package.json#exports`'s ESM/CJS map), default exports (`export default class X`), namespace exports (`Drizzle.with` vs `with`), dual-package hazards (`drizzle-orm`'s `.d.ts` vs `.d.mts`), `@types/*` fallback when `package.json` lacks `types`. The resolver's correctness on real-world packages is the implementation risk. Mitigation: the smoke harness fixtures (`smoke-m11-lookup.mts`) include `drizzle-orm`, `react`, `@types/node`, and one conditional-exports case (`zod` or similar). Real-world edge cases that surface in dogfood become smoke-fixture additions.

- _Caveat — per-repo cache, not user-global._ `drizzle-orm@0.30.0` types are identical across every repo using that version; M11 re-resolves per-repo. Theoretically wasteful at scale. ADR-0007's single-file-per-repo cache invariant holds; user-global cache is its own decision (cross-repo concurrent access, namespace resolution between repos pinning different versions). Revisit if storage pain materializes — at <1 MB per repo, it doesn't, yet.

- _Caveat — Voyage is not invoked for `.d.ts`._ The keystone framing originally implied "extend the M6 Voyage path to `.d.ts`." M11 narrows to "extend to `.d.ts` _lookup_, not retrieval." This means the M6 storage layer (`chunks`, `embeddings`, `merkle`, `index_meta`) is untouched by M11; the new `type_def_cache` table sits alongside, not inside, the M6 architecture. When `leverage` ships in M12+ and _does_ want semantic retrieval over `.d.ts`, embedding-based retrieval re-enters the picture as the additive `type_def_embeddings` table — same content-addressed discipline as ADR-0016.

- _Caveat — the verifier surface for non-`api_def` sources is unchanged._ M10's substring-verifier handles `{path, line, snippet}` triples in repo-rooted files. M11 adds `api_def` handling (path in `node_modules/`); other source types (`cve`, `advisory`, `changelog`, `documentation`, `web`, `tool`, `repo_convention`) are unchanged. The verifier walk is "for each Comment, for each source, dispatch on `type`" — the dispatch gains one new branch.

- _Caveat — first-Voyage-SKU-bump is unaffected._ M6's locked-model concept (ADR-0019 #6) governs the source-code index. `.d.ts` lookup doesn't use embeddings, so Voyage SKU bumps don't trigger any `.d.ts` re-resolution. The `--rebuild` semantics in M6 stay scoped to the embedding index; M11 introduces no parallel rebuild verb.

- _Caveat — package version resolution is shallow._ `lookupTypeDef` reads `node_modules/<pkg>/package.json#version` for the cache key. It does not resolve pnpm's flat-by-default `node_modules` symlinks, peer-dependency hoisting conflicts, or monorepo workspace cross-references. v0 assumes the resolved package at `node_modules/<pkg>/` is the canonical one; this matches `node_modules` consumer expectations (Node's own `require.resolve` algorithm). pnpm workspace packages with internal `.d.ts` (resolvable from the consumer) work transparently because pnpm symlinks them into `node_modules/`. Edge cases that fail v0 surface as `package_not_installed` (graceful) rather than wrong-version cache hits (silent).

- _Caveat — design is locked; implementation specifics live in m11-plan.md._ ADR-0026 is the design commit; `m11-plan.md` is the implementation brief. Future agents read both; ADR-0026 is the authority on design questions, m11-plan.md on file-by-file scope.

- _Caveat — does not close ADR-0019's other M10+ deferrals._ BYOEmbedder, daemon JobRunner, custom-code SAST worker, `warden index export/import` CLI, cloud-hosted index, mid-stream key handling, retrieval refinements all stay deferred after M11. Each earns its own ADR + milestone when scheduled. The `leverage` review category (rooted in memory, not ADR-0019) also stays deferred for its own grilling.

**Pre-implementation refinements (added 2026-05-12).** Three loopholes surfaced during a pre-implementation review of `m11-plan.md`; all are additive to the ADR shape, not structural changes:

- _Subpath imports are first-class._ §3 originally said the resolver walks `package.json#types` / `#typings` / `#exports['.']['types']`. Real-world claims overwhelmingly target subpath imports (`drizzle-orm/sqlite-core`, `next/server`, `@radix-ui/react-dialog`). The tool's `package` field accepts the **literal import path**; the resolver splits `(packageName, subpath)` internally, reads `node_modules/<packageName>/package.json#version`, and resolves the `.d.ts` via `exports['./<subpath>']` → `typesVersions[*][<subpath>]` → direct `<subpath>.d.ts` / `<subpath>/index.d.ts` → `@types/<packageName>/<subpath>.d.ts` fallback chain. The cache key `(package, version, symbol)` uses the **literal `pkg`** so `drizzle-orm` and `drizzle-orm/sqlite-core` stay independent rows. Implementation details in `m11-plan.md` §3.

- _Multi-line signatures verified via concat-then-match._ §8 + §9 originally implied the verifier re-uses M10's per-line substring match. That fails on `.d.ts` signatures, which routinely span 10+ lines (generics, JSDoc, overload sets). The verifier dispatches on `source.type`: `api_def` sources widen the drift window to `API_DEF_DRIFT = 30`, concatenate `lines[line ± 30]`, normalize whitespace once, then `.includes()` the normalized signature. Non-`api_def` sources keep M10's per-line semantics unchanged. The resolver stores `signature` already-normalized-to-one-line, so the snippet field is a clean substring of the normalized window. Picked over the considered alternative ("match prefix-only against any line") because concat-then-match verifies the full signature is present (semantically stronger than "the symbol appears nearby") without the "how many prefix chars" tuning knob the prefix-match alternative requires.

- _Tool result carries a pre-shaped `suggestedSource` object._ §9 of the ADR alludes to "the LLM constructs `Source` from the result fields." That construction is the single biggest LLM-side failure mode under the current schema: `SourceSchema.refine()` rejects partial `{path, line, snippet}` triples at parse time → entire `LlmOutput` fails Zod → cascade throws → ai-retry retries → eventual hard fail. The `found: true` variant of `LookupTypeDefResult` now carries a `suggestedSource: SuggestedApiDefSource` field — fully-formed Source object with `type`, `id`, `title`, `path`, `line`, `snippet`, `retrievedAt`. The prompt instructs the LLM to copy it **verbatim** into `Comment.sources[]`. Converts the failure mode from "Zod-parse cliff that fails the whole review" to "the LLM ignored the instruction and emits no source," which the existing verifier-discipline floor handles cleanly (uncited claim → accepted gap per §7).

**Status.** Direction. M11 grilling pass complete (Q1 → Q8); design locked. Pre-implementation refinements above (2026-05-12) add subpath / multi-line / `suggestedSource` shape without altering the ADR's structural choices. Implementation tracked in `m11-plan.md`.

---

## ADR-0027 — M12: `leverage` review category — bounded stdlib detector + Haiku sub-agent (cashes the M11 keystone)

**Decision.** M12 ships the **`leverage` review category** — the second half of ADR-0026's architectural keystone framing. ADR-0026 narrowed cross-repo retrieval to `.d.ts` lookup + the API claim _verifier_ half of the dependency cascade; ADR-0027 ships the _producer_ half: a sixth `CategoryEnum` slot for "this hand-rolled code duplicates a library or stdlib primitive," realised as **two runners under one category** — a deterministic bounded-pattern detector for JS stdlib idiom misses, and a cheap-tier Haiku sub-agent for library-specific substitution suggestions that cites verified `api_def` sources via M11's `lookupTypeDef`. The two runners share the `leverage` category slot in `PRIORITY_ORDER` but emit structurally different comments — detector → `kind: "assertion"` + `type: "tool"` AST evidence; sub-agent → `kind: "question"` + `type: "api_def"` sources verified by M10/M11's substring + concat-then-match verifier. Both runners ride the M8 `Runner` contract from day 1 (no new debt on the "remaining inline runners" list). The category enum extends by one value, and the internal runner mapping learns `ToolFinding.source = "leverage"`; no new `SourceType`, no new SQLite tables, no `lookupTypeDef` cap change, no new model tier. Slots into `PRIORITY_ORDER` as `... → style → leverage → dedup → tests` — leverage before dedup because a library swap can dissolve a downstream dedup finding entirely (rewriting `arr.filter(p).length > 0` away makes a sibling `hasItems` helper unnecessary).

The full surface:

1. **Two runners under one category — clean structural split, not a bundle.** ADR-0008's citation thesis + CONTEXT.md §5's detector-vs-sub-agent rule combine into a clean fork: a bounded anti-pattern set with reliable structural detection earns a detector; an open-ended set or one that's reliable in principle but unreliable across ecosystems earns a sub-agent. Leverage has _both_ — stdlib idiom misses (e.g., `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))`) are AST-bounded and ecosystem-independent; library-specific suggestions (e.g., manual JOIN vs. Drizzle relational) are open-ended and dependency-gated. Bundling them under one runner would either (a) force the LLM through stdlib patterns the detector handles deterministically (token waste, lower precision) or (b) force the detector to encode library knowledge it can't represent reliably (the M7 committability trap). The runners share _only_ the `leverage` category slot; they're independent files (`packages/core/src/runners/leverage.ts` for the detector, `packages/core/src/runners/leverage-libraries.ts` for the sub-agent — naming finalised in `m12-plan.md`), independent inputs (detector reads parsed AST; sub-agent reads diff + `package.json` deps preamble), and independent verification paths (detector findings are tool-grounded by their own AST trace; sub-agent comments survive only if `verify-citations.ts` substring-matches the `api_def` triple). The "Both" Q1 answer earns its rent precisely because the citation shapes are different — same category, different epistemic grounding.

2. **Detector v0 pattern set: three high-precision stdlib substitutions.** The detector ships exactly three AST patterns in v0, all modern JS stdlib idioms, all single-call replacements, all with zero overlap against M7's scalability detector and ADR-0021 dedup runner. The set: (a) `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))` → `structuredClone(x)`; (b) `arr.indexOf(x) !== -1` / `arr.indexOf(x) > -1` / `arr.indexOf(x) >= 0` → `arr.includes(x)`; (c) `arr.filter(p).length > 0` / `arr.find(p) !== undefined` / `arr.find(p) != null` → `arr.some(p)`. Rejected from v0: `Array.from(new Set(arr))` (idiomatic; not a leverage miss); `Object.keys(o).map(k => [k, o[k]])` → `Object.entries(o)` (rare in modern code); lodash-style substitutions (gate on installed `lodash` — pushes into sub-agent territory); `Promise.all` collapse for sequential awaits (already owned by `scalability.ts`). Each pattern is a separate AST visitor function in `packages/core/src/runners/leverage.ts`; each emits a `ToolFinding` with `source: "leverage"` and optional `(path, line, snippet)` evidence pointing at the matched call expression. No type-aware narrowing in v0 — even though these substitutions have legitimate semantic edges (`structuredClone` runtime support / `toJSON` / JSON-stripping, `includes` and `NaN`, `find` on nullish elements), the v0 detector emits conditional wording uniformly; dogfood evidence drives any narrowing (per §9).

3. **Sub-agent: Haiku via `getWorkerCheapModel()`, prompt at `packages/core/src/llm/prompts/leverage-system.md`.** The sub-agent mirrors M7's committability sub-agent harness: cheap-tier (Haiku) via `getWorkerCheapModel()` from `@warden/ai`, own system prompt under `packages/core/src/llm/prompts/leverage-system.md` (per ADR-0015's prompts-as-files discipline), gated to `review` mode only (no LLM call in `check`, where the deterministic synthesizer runs instead). The prompt is **library-agnostic with four canonical examples** + a dependency preamble: the prompt body explains the leverage concept and lists four representative cases (Drizzle relational `with:` over manual JOIN; Elysia `.guard()` over per-route `{ auth: true }`; AI SDK `Output.array(...)` over manual JSON parse; Drizzle `onConflictDoNothing()` over `INSERT-check-INSERT`), and the runner injects an "Installed libraries:" preamble built from `repoRoot/package.json` plus the nearest touched package manifests (top-level `dependencies` + `devDependencies` + `peerDependencies` keys, no version resolution). The preamble gates suggestions to libraries the user has actually installed, including pnpm workspace packages whose dependencies live under `packages/*/package.json`; the four examples anchor the LLM's idiom-recognition without committing to a closed library table. The sub-agent has access to M11's `lookupTypeDef` tool (via the same `tools: { lookupTypeDef }` argument passed to `streamText`); every emitted question that asserts a library API must carry a matching `api_def` source. The runner drops any LLM finding with no `api_def` source before it becomes a `Comment`, because the global verifier intentionally passes comments that never had snippet-bearing sources. The M10/M11 verifier post-pass enforces the remaining citations — comments whose `api_def` source fails the concat-then-match check are dropped silently, leaving uncited claims at the same epistemic floor as ADR-0026 §7 ("best-effort + structurally-verified").

4. **Sub-agent emission: `kind: "question"` not `"assertion"`.** Leverage substitution claims are _suggestions_ — "library Y has primitive Z that matches what you wrote" — not assertions of broken behaviour. Even when `lookupTypeDef` returns a verified signature, the _substitution_ itself has unstated tradeoffs (bundle size, ergonomics, perf characteristics, opt-in feature flags) the LLM can't fully assess. `kind: "question"` invites the developer to decide; `kind: "assertion"` would overclaim. Committability is the precedent: it cites `repo_convention` / `documentation` sources and still emits questions, because its claims ("you probably didn't mean to commit this") are intent-driven. Leverage's claims are similarly intent-adjacent ("you probably wanted Drizzle's relational query"). The detector half emits `kind: "assertion"` because its claims are mechanically present in the AST — `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))` either _is_ the pattern or _isn't_; there's no intent layer. The split is clean: detector = assertion (deterministic, mechanically grounded); sub-agent = question (LLM-synthesised, structurally cited but not behaviourally proven).

5. **Priority slot: `... → style → leverage → dedup → tests`.** ADR-0020 extended ADR-0012's order with `scalability`, `consistency`, `deadcode`, `committability` inserted between correctness and clarity. M12 inserts `leverage` between `style` and `dedup`. Order = action precedence: dedup ("extract this shared helper") presumes the code stays; leverage ("use the library primitive") deletes the code entirely. If both fire on the same diff, leverage first because acting on it dissolves the dedup finding. Adjacent placement keeps the "use what exists elsewhere" cluster together — leverage (external library) + dedup (internal utility) read as a coherent pair. Rejected alternatives: (a) after `dedup` ("between dedup and tests") — the original framing in `project_warden_leverage_category.md`, pre-M7 era; downgraded because it treats library evidence as lower-confidence than repo-internal duplication, which inverts the actual tool-grounding (`api_def` verifier > jscpd structural similarity); (b) right before `clarity` — treats leverage as near-correctness, too aggressive when the LLM is still synthesising the substitution. The before-dedup slot is the action-precedence-preserving choice.

6. **Schema: one-line `CategoryEnum` extension; no new `SourceType`, no new SQLite tables.** `SourceTypeEnum` already carries every source variant M12 needs — detector emits `type: "tool"` (existing); sub-agent emits `type: "api_def"` (ADR-0026 extension). No new persisted state — sub-agent reads M11's `type_def_cache` transparently via `lookupTypeDef`'s existing cache layer; no `type_def_embeddings` table (semantic retrieval is M13+ if dogfood shows the exact-match path misses; see §10). `CategoryEnum` in `packages/core/src/schema.ts` gains `'leverage'`; `PRIORITY_ORDER` in `packages/core/src/index.ts` gains a slot between `'style'` and `'dedup'`; `ToolFinding.source` in `packages/core/src/runners/types.ts` gains `'leverage'`; `packages/core/src/runners/to-comment.ts` maps it to `{ category: "leverage", tier: 2 }` and copies optional snippet evidence into the existing `SourceSchema` triple. No new confidence-threshold subsystem ships in M12 — leverage uses the existing `confidence` field, priority sort, and tier-3 verbose gate. The schema lean-ness is the ADR-0026 dividend cashing — M11 designed `api_def` to be the first of a family of producer integrations; M12 is the second producer (after the M11 formatter integration), and it slots in without public schema work.

7. **Runner contract: both runners ride M8's `Runner` interface from day 1.** ADR-0023 shipped the orchestration spine and committed scalability + committability through the `Runner` contract; the remaining 6 runners (TSC, ESLint, jscpd, vuln, deadcode, consistency) stay inline as accepted debt. M12's two new runners land on the contract — they're new, the contract is well-tested at this point (M8 → M11 spans four milestones), and pattern-matching the existing migrated runners (scalability for the detector; committability for the sub-agent) keeps the spine homogeneous on the new code. The detector's `Runner.run(input)` returns `RunnerOutput` with `findings[]` + `degraded[]`; the sub-agent's returns `RunnerOutput` with `questions[]` + `degraded[]`. Both register with `dispatch()` in `packages/core/src/orchestration/dispatch.ts`; the synthesizer reads both runners' outputs from the scratchpad transparently. No new orchestration primitives, no contract changes — the contract earns rent by absorbing two new runners with zero structural friction.

8. **Mode gating: detector in `check` + `review`, sub-agent in `review` only.** The detector is deterministic (no LLM call); it runs in both verbs uniformly, same as scalability/deadcode/consistency. The sub-agent makes an LLM call (Haiku via `getWorkerCheapModel()`); per ADR-0011, `warden check` is the fast deterministic-only verb (pre-commit / CI gating), so it skips all sub-agents. M12 honours this — the sub-agent is registered conditionally on `mode === "review"` at dispatch construction. The skipping is silent (no `degradedWorkers` entry) because the user explicitly chose the fast verb; emitting "leverage suggestions unavailable in `check`" every time would be the noise pattern ADR-0025 rejected.

9. **FP handling: dogfood-tune the patterns; no escape hatch.** The three detector patterns each have known semantic edges: `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))` for deep-strip / `toJSON` / runtime-availability cases; `arr.indexOf(x) !== -1` for `NaN`-sensitive code paths (where `includes` uses SameValueZero); `arr.find(p) !== undefined` / `arr.find(p) != null` when the matched array element itself can be nullish. M12 ships no escape hatch — no inline `// warden-ignore-leverage` marker (would force every detector to respect the parser surface — a wide commitment for an unscheduled need); no per-category overlay (the `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` surface from ADR-0008 is still deferred per ADR-0025); no LLM downgrade pass (synthesizer doesn't know which leverage findings have intentional uses). If dogfood evidence shows specific patterns producing false positives, the right fix is _tightening the detector_ (e.g., AST-time check that the `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))` input's static type contains only JSON-safe shapes), not adding a suppression layer. Mirrors the M7-committability → M9 cleanup philosophy: ship the honest detection; the right escape hatch (if any) emerges from dogfood evidence, not speculative API surface.

10. **Forward compatibility: semantic retrieval over `.d.ts` stays deferred (ADR-0026 §14).** ADR-0026 §14 pre-anticipated that `leverage` might want semantic search over `.d.ts` ("find Drizzle's join-related primitives") and committed the additive `type_def_embeddings` table as the swap-point. M12 _does not_ schedule that path. The sub-agent's prompt + `lookupTypeDef`'s exact-match lookup is sufficient for the four canonical examples (the LLM names the library + symbol from memory, then verifies via lookup). Semantic retrieval earns rent only when the LLM's library-symbol recall starts to limit useful suggestions — i.e., when "I know Drizzle has a function for this but I don't know its name" becomes the bottleneck. Dogfood the exact-match path first; if recall is the gap, M13+ adds the embedding layer with its own ADR. The keystone framing pays out one more time: ADR-0026's schema is already shaped to absorb semantic retrieval additively when the consumer earns it.

**Why.**

- _Cashes the M11 keystone._ ADR-0026's opening frame was "this single milestone unblocks two named M10+ items — the `leverage` review category and the API claim verifier." M11 shipped the verifier; the leverage category is the named successor. The keystone was the unlock; M12 is the dividend. Deferring leverage another milestone leaves M11 looking like infrastructure-for-its-own-sake; shipping leverage now closes the framing.

- _Cheap-detector + cheap-LLM is the right shape, not formatter integration._ ADR-0026 §4 considered (and explicitly deferred) "leverage as a sub-agent" framing. The verifier consumes `api_def` sources from any producer; the producer choice is independent. M12's two-runner shape (detector for stdlib; sub-agent for library) lets the cheap path (deterministic AST) handle the cheap patterns and the expensive path (Haiku LLM + lookupTypeDef) handle the expensive ones. Folding both into the synthesizer (the M11 path) would route stdlib patterns through Sonnet, wasting tokens on AST-decidable cases. Folding both into a single sub-agent would force the Haiku to re-derive stdlib idiom checks the AST does for free. Two runners, two cost tiers, one category — the orthogonality earns rent.

- _Bounded stdlib patterns are the M7 committability trap's safe sibling._ M7's committability detector half was parked because "dirname conventions and dev-script naming look bounded but break across ecosystems." Leverage's three patterns are _language-stdlib_, not ecosystem-specific — `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify)` / `Array.prototype.indexOf` / `Array.prototype.some` are ES specification primitives, identical across every JS ecosystem (Node, browser, Bun, Deno). The committability trap was ecosystem variance; the leverage detector sidesteps it by scoping to spec-defined idioms. The honest test: each pattern's "wrong" version and "right" version have identical observable behaviour modulo perf or rare edge cases (NaN, Map/Set strip) — that's the bounded-set criterion CONTEXT.md §5 demands.

- _Library-agnostic prompt + package.json preamble inverts the curated-table maintenance burden._ The rejected curated-library-table approach (Q4 option B / C) requires updating per-library snippet maps for every version bump that changes idiomatic usage. Library-agnostic + preamble inverts the relationship: the LLM names libraries from its training data; the preamble gates suggestions to installed packages; `lookupTypeDef` verifies the API surface; the verifier drops hallucinations. The maintenance cost moves from "Warden's prompt table" to "the LLM's training cutoff" — and the LLM updates faster than any per-library snippet table Warden could maintain by hand.

- _Priority order = action precedence._ Q3 surfaced three candidate slots (before dedup, after dedup, before clarity). Before-dedup wins because leverage substitutions delete code that dedup might extract — the action ordering implied by reading top-down is "consider library swap; if not applicable, then consider dedup." After-dedup forces the user to mentally undo a dedup suggestion when leverage applies. Before-clarity is too aggressive — leverage isn't near-correctness, it's near-style. The `... → style → leverage → dedup → tests` ordering reads as "suggestions about your code" → "suggestions about replacing your code" → "suggestions about its tests," which matches the user's mental model.

- _Schema lean = M11 dividend cashing._ ADR-0026 §13–14 designed `api_def` source variant + `type_def_cache` table as the architectural primitive future producers inherit. M12 is the first new producer (after the M11 formatter integration); zero new schema additions confirms the dividend. The bar for "new milestone earns its rent" is now "fits inside the existing schema" — M12 clears it.

- _No FP escape hatch matches M7 → M9._ M7 committability shipped a directory-concentration heuristic placeholder; M9 deleted it when the diff-level noise filter superseded it. M12 ships honest patterns; M13+ deletes any that produce false positives by narrowing detection (not by adding an opt-out layer). The pattern is "loud about real signal; quiet about misses; tighten signal when dogfood reveals noise" — ADR-0025's "loud about subtrees, quiet about individual files" philosophy generalised.

- _Verifier symmetry preserved._ ADR-0021 §3 designed the verifier as `walk(comment.sources, dispatch on type)`; M10 added the per-line algorithm; M11 added the `api_def` concat-then-match branch. M12 _invokes_ the verifier without extending it — the sub-agent's emitted `api_def` sources flow through the same dispatch the M11 formatter's `api_def` sources flow through. Zero verifier changes. The verifier's architectural primitive role (per ADR-0021 §3's framing) keeps paying out.

**Alternatives considered and rejected.**

- _Detector-only._ Ship the three bounded patterns; defer the sub-agent to M13+ when dogfood reveals which library substitutions matter most. Rejected because the M11 keystone explicitly framed leverage as the sub-agent half — shipping detector-only would leave M11's `lookupTypeDef` tool under-used (the formatter rarely needs it for library-substitution claims because the formatter's job is triage, not idiom-recognition). The sub-agent earns its rent precisely _because_ it cashes M11's tool surface.

- _Sub-agent-only._ Ship the Haiku sub-agent; defer the detector to M13+. Rejected because the three patterns are genuinely AST-bounded and shipping them through Haiku wastes tokens on cases an AST visitor decides in microseconds. The Q1 answer ("Both") was a substantive choice, not a hedge — both halves earn their rent, and the cost-tier orthogonality argument (cheap detector for cheap patterns; cheap LLM for expensive patterns) requires both.

- _Larger detector set (5–8 patterns)._ Add `Object.entries`/`Object.fromEntries` substitutions, optional chaining replacements, etc. Rejected for v0 — more patterns = more FP risk + more AST surface; v0 should prove the pattern shape with three patterns proven not to overlap with scalability/dedup. M13+ adds patterns when dogfood reveals which ones the LLM consistently misses (signal: every leverage suggestion the sub-agent makes that _should_ have been a detector hit becomes a candidate pattern).

- _Curated library table in the prompt (Q4 option B)._ Hardcoded `(library → idiom_snippets[])` table in the prompt. Rejected because library version bumps invalidate the table (e.g., Drizzle's relational query syntax changed between versions); maintenance burden grows with library count; closed set caps coverage. Library-agnostic + `package.json` preamble achieves the same gating (only suggest installed libraries) without the table.

- _package.json-gated curated table (Q4 option C)._ Per-library snippets injected into the prompt only when the library is in `node_modules`. Rejected as the hybrid that earns neither benefit cleanly — still requires the per-library snippet maintenance, just gated by installation; coverage still capped at the table; the gating logic adds prompt-construction complexity for marginal precision gains. The library-agnostic + preamble path is structurally simpler and similarly precise after verifier filtering.

- _Library-agnostic prompt with retrieved context (Q4 option D)._ Same as the chosen option A, but additionally pass the M5/M6 selector's retrieved context (same-folder neighbours, semantic candidates) to the sub-agent. Rejected for v0 — the sub-agent's job is library-substitution suggestion, which is diff-local (the call site of the hand-rolled code). Retrieved context adds tokens without clearly improving suggestion quality; the M5/M6 retrieval shape was designed for _correctness_ claims that need adjacent-code grounding, not idiom suggestions. Revisit in M13+ if dogfood shows the sub-agent missing substitutions that retrieved context would surface.

- _Detector-emits-`question` (uniform comment kind across both runners)._ Both runners emit `kind: "question"` so the category-level discipline reads uniformly. Rejected because the detector's findings are mechanically present in the AST — calling them questions overclaims the LLM-synthesis layer that wasn't involved. Mixing assertion + question kinds within a single category is fine; ADR-0021's vulnerability detector + committability sub-agent already establish the precedent (vulnerabilities are assertions; committability is questions; both feed different `category` slots — leverage feeding both kinds into one category is a half-step from there).

- _Inline `// warden-ignore-leverage` marker (Q5 option B)._ Per-line suppression. Rejected because once one detector respects the marker, every detector must (TSC, ESLint, scalability, deadcode, consistency, leverage detector — the surface area is wide); the marker also pollutes the source tree with Warden-specific metadata, breaking the M9 noise-filter philosophy ("Warden is loud about subtrees, quiet about individual files"). If marker-based suppression becomes necessary, it deserves its own ADR scoped to all detectors uniformly, not a leverage-specific shortcut.

- _Per-category `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` (Q5 alternative)._ Per ADR-0008's "known debt" surface — but the overlay loader is `[deferred]` and ADR-0025 explicitly pushed it to M10's own ADR (still unscheduled). Rejected because committing to the overlay shape for leverage would commit M12 to the overlay loader implementation; that's a separate milestone. Revisit when overlay loader ships.

- _Priority slot after `dedup` (Q3 option B)._ Memory's pre-M7 framing. Rejected because it inverts the action ordering — leverage swaps delete code that dedup might extract; users reading top-down should see leverage first.

- _Priority slot before `clarity` (Q3 option C)._ Treats leverage as near-correctness. Rejected as too aggressive — leverage suggestions are still LLM-synthesised substitutions; clarity (readability) and style (formatting) are higher in the priority order because they're stylistic, not substantive. Leverage sits between style (cosmetic) and dedup (structural) — it's structural but optional; close to dedup's neighbourhood.

- _Add `type_def_embeddings` table now for semantic retrieval over `.d.ts`._ Pre-build the embedding index in M12 to enable "find Drizzle's join-related primitives" semantic queries. Rejected (per §10) because the four canonical examples in the prompt + `lookupTypeDef`'s exact-match lookup is sufficient for v0; semantic retrieval earns rent only when dogfood reveals the LLM hits recall limits ("I know Drizzle has a function for this but can't name it"). Schema absorbs this additively when scheduled — ADR-0026 §14 designed for it.

- _Expose `lookupTypeDef` to the leverage detector._ Let the detector look up library types when its AST pattern matches a call site (e.g., `lodash.cloneDeep` → check if `structuredClone` is the suggested replacement). Rejected because the leverage detector's three v0 patterns are stdlib-only — they don't suggest library substitutions, only stdlib substitutions. If a future detector pattern _does_ span library boundaries (M13+), it gets the tool then; v0's detector stays tool-less.

- _Promote the bounded detector half to a "leverage stdlib" sub-category (`leverage-stdlib` + `leverage-libraries`)._ Two `CategoryEnum` slots, two priority order entries, two confidence thresholds. Rejected because the category split is over-engineered for a category that hasn't shipped yet — the user-facing distinction is "this code could be more idiomatic," and the source of truth (stdlib vs. library) is already encoded in `Source.type` (`tool` vs. `api_def`). A reader who cares about the split can filter on source type; a reader who doesn't sees a unified "leverage" category. Split if dogfood reveals users want different confidence thresholds per source-type half — not before.

- _Bundle the M8 contract migration for the remaining 6 runners into M12._ Re-platform TSC, ESLint, jscpd, vuln, deadcode, consistency through `Runner` while leverage rides the contract. Rejected because the migration is its own architectural commitment (per ADR-0023's deferred list) and M12 should ship a category, not a refactor. The two new runners land on the contract; the inline 6 stay inline until their own scheduled milestone (likely tied to the noise-filter pass touching the same surface, per ADR-0023's note).

**Caveats.**

- _Caveat — the three detector patterns are honest-tightenable._ `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(x))` over a value containing `Map`/`Set`/`Date`/functions has semantic differences `structuredClone` doesn't reproduce — `structuredClone` _preserves_ them, the JSON roundtrip _strips_ them; it also differs for custom `toJSON`, cycles, and runtimes without `structuredClone`. The v0 detector emits uniformly with conditional wording; if dogfood shows enough FPs from intentional-strip uses, the right fix is type-aware narrowing at AST time (check if the call's input type contains stripping-relevant types via the TS Compiler API). Similarly: `indexOf !== -1` and `includes` differ on `NaN`; if dogfood shows NaN-sensitive code paths producing FPs, narrow to "input type is `unknown` or contains `number`" before suggesting. `find(...) !== undefined` / `find(...) != null` and `some(...)` differ when the matched array element itself can be nullish; if that fires in dogfood, narrow against nullish element types before suggesting. Tightening is honest engineering; the pattern set survives the dogfood-tune philosophy.

- _Caveat — the sub-agent does not share the formatter's `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)` cap._ M11 set the formatter cap at 8 per ADR-0026 §6. The leverage sub-agent makes its own `streamText` call and gets its own 8-call budget for `lookupTypeDef` invocations. Sharing the cap across runners (one budget for the whole review) was considered and rejected — per-runner budgets are easier to reason about and the M11 cap is generous for a single runner's needs. If both LLM call sites spiral on the same review, the total tool-call budget hits 16 — bounded; M12 doesn't centralise this.

- _Caveat — dependency preamble is shallow but workspace-aware._ The sub-agent reads `dependencies` + `devDependencies` + `peerDependencies` top-level keys from `repoRoot/package.json` and the nearest touched package manifests under the repo. It does not resolve version ranges, peer-dependency conflicts, yarn berry portal-style resolutions, or transitive dependencies. The preamble is a soft gate (the LLM may still suggest a library not in the preamble; the verifier will catch the hallucination at `lookupTypeDef` time via `package_not_installed`). M12 also hardens the type lookup path enough to try those touched package roots' `node_modules` directories before declaring a package missing; this is package-resolution correctness, not `node_modules/<pkg>/src` retrieval. v0 accepts this shallow read; M13+ deepens resolution if dogfood evidence shows the soft-gate path produces noise.

- _Caveat — detector + sub-agent don't double-fire on the same site, by category invariant._ The detector emits findings on stdlib AST patterns (`JSON.parse(JSON.stringify)` etc.); the sub-agent emits questions on library-substitution opportunities (Drizzle, Elysia, AI SDK, etc.). These are disjoint anti-pattern sets — the detector's patterns are stdlib-only, the sub-agent's prompt narrows it to installed libraries. The risk of double-fire is structurally low; the verification path (different `Source.type` values: `tool` vs. `api_def`) makes accidental double-citation impossible.

- _Caveat — leverage isn't tier-prescriptive at category level._ Comments emitted by both runners carry the standard `tier` field (1 / 2 / 3); the runner emitters assign tier per-finding. The detector defaults to Tier 2 (should-fix) — these are real-but-optional improvements. The sub-agent's tier defaults to Tier 2 by default but Tier 3 (informational) when the substitution is purely stylistic. No category-level tier override and no new confidence gate in M12; the existing priority sort, confidence tie-breaker, and tier-3 verbose gate apply unchanged.

- _Caveat — sub-agent skip in `check` mode is silent._ `warden check` is the deterministic-only fast verb (pre-commit / CI gating per ADR-0011). The leverage detector runs in `check`; the sub-agent doesn't. The skip is silent — no `degradedWorkers` entry. Surfacing it ("leverage suggestions unavailable in check mode; run `warden review` for the full pass") was considered and rejected as the verbosity ADR-0025 §10 explicitly mirrors: loud about system-level issues, quiet about per-verb normal-operation skips. The user chose the fast verb; they know what it excludes.

- _Caveat — semantic retrieval over `.d.ts` stays deferred (per §10 + ADR-0026 §14)._ If the LLM's library-symbol recall becomes the bottleneck for useful suggestions ("I know Drizzle has a join-flavoured function but can't name it"), M13+ adds the `type_def_embeddings` table additively. The schema is shaped for it; the runtime path is not. Don't pre-build the index in M12 — gates on dogfood evidence the consumer needs it.

- _Caveat — design is locked; implementation specifics live in `m12-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0026 → `m11-plan.md`. ADR-0027 is the design commit; `m12-plan.md` is the file-by-file implementation brief. Future agents read both; ADR-0027 is the authority on design questions, `m12-plan.md` on implementation scope.

**Status.** Direction. M12 grilling pass complete (Q1 → Q5); design locked 2026-05-14. Implementation tracked in `m12-plan.md`. Closes the second half of ADR-0026's keystone framing.

---

## ADR-0028 — M13: custom-code SAST default-review producers — ESLint security floor + Haiku triage sub-agent with DeepSec-borrowed prompt structure

**Decision.** M13 fills the long-empty `'security'` `CategoryEnum` slot with **two default-review producers** under one category — pattern-matching M12's leverage shape exactly. The `'security'` slot has lived in the enum + `PRIORITY_ORDER` since v0 (between `'correctness'` and `'vulnerability'`) without a producer; ADR-0008 deferred the custom-code SAST worker; ADR-0015 committed to borrowing DeepSec's pipeline while rejecting its grounding model; and the user's own `project_warden_security_depth_tiers.md` memory named the three security tiers (always-on fast + default review + on-demand deep) over 6 months ago. M13 ships the default-review tier. The on-demand-deep tier (`warden security` verb + Sonnet specialist worker + dedicated orchestration harness — the _first vision-tier worker proper_ per CONTEXT.md §3) is deferred to M14 with its own ADR. The split is load-bearing: bundling worker + verb + harness + default-review producers into one milestone would force a single ADR to commit on every architectural surface at once; splitting lets M14 grill its design tree afresh with M13 dogfood evidence in hand. M13 uses the existing M8 review spine without introducing a second harness: the Haiku sub-agent registers through `orchestrationRunners`, while the ESLint security detector stays in the inline deterministic runner lane and records into the scratchpad like the existing ESLint result. M14 introduces a separate harness alongside per the two-harness vision (vision.md §3, Ronit's agent-orch framing). The schema is unchanged — `'security'` already in `CategoryEnum`; both producers emit existing `type: "tool"` sources; the substring-verifier dispatches on `type` as today with zero new branches. The architectural lift is concentrated in one new piece: the **per-category confidence-threshold subsystem** (CONTEXT.md §7 `[deferred]` since M4) earns its rent in M13 because security is the first category whose Haiku output is inherently noisy without volume control.

The full surface:

1. **Two producers under one category — clean structural split, not a bundle.** ADR-0008's citation thesis + CONTEXT.md §5's detector-vs-sub-agent rule combine the same way they did for leverage. ESLint security plugins are bounded-pattern detectors with reliable structural detection (the `detect-eval-with-expression` regex on `eval(req.body)` is a fact, not a judgment) — they earn the detector slot. The Haiku sub-agent handles the open-ended residue: cross-tenant ID leakage, missing auth on route handlers, parameter-pollution bypasses, SSRF, path-traversal in non-canonical sinks, secret-in-log, auth-bypass via encoded characters — patterns whose detection is open-ended and requires LLM reasoning rather than AST matching. Same shape, different epistemic grounding: detector → `kind: "assertion"` with mechanically-verified `tool` sources (the ESLint rule's diagnostic); sub-agent → `kind: "question"` with LLM-synthesised but substring-verified `tool` sources (the source line + sink line). The "Both" answer earns its rent precisely because the citation shapes are different — same category, different epistemic floor.

2. **Detector: same ESLint runner module, separate Warden-owned invocation.** The detector half is implemented in `packages/core/src/runners/eslint.ts` as `runEslintSecurity()`, a second ESLint invocation that uses Warden's own pinned `eslint`, `eslint-plugin-security`, and `eslint-plugin-no-secrets` dependencies plus a Warden-managed flat config. It is not gated on the target repo having an ESLint config; it only needs JS/TS changed files. Rule-prefix mapping in `packages/core/src/runners/to-comment.ts` routes rule IDs matching `security/*` or `no-secrets/*` to `{ category: "security", tier: 1 }`. No new runner file, no new dispatch registration. `eslint-plugin-no-unsanitized` and `@microsoft/eslint-plugin-sdl` are explicitly deferred to dogfood evidence — adding a plugin is a config change, not a milestone. The existing ESLint runner's TypeScript-only constraint (ADR-0008) is inherited unchanged; multi-language security detection is an M14+ concern tied to the multi-ecosystem detector rewrite.

3. **Haiku security sub-agent — cheap-tier triage in default review.** New runner at `packages/core/src/runners/security.ts` (name finalised in `m13-plan.md`). Mirrors M12's leverage sub-agent harness: Haiku via `getWorkerCheapModel()` from `@warden/ai` (graceful when env keys missing — one info-level `degradedWorkers` entry, no hard fail), own system prompt under `packages/core/src/llm/prompts/security-system.md` (per ADR-0015's prompts-as-files discipline), gated to `review` mode only. Has access to M11's `lookupTypeDef` tool (third consumer after the M11 formatter and the M12 leverage sub-agent) with its own `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)` budget — library API security claims (e.g., "does this `validator.escape(x)` actually escape correctly?") get the same `api_def` citation discipline as leverage's library-substitution claims. The sub-agent emits `Comment[]` of `kind: "question"` carrying source-line + sink-line `tool` sources, each verified by the existing M10 substring-verifier; the runner drops any LLM finding with no `tool` source before it becomes a `Comment`.

4. **DeepSec prompt borrow set — pipeline structure adopted, grounding model rejected.** Per ADR-0015 ("borrow DeepSec's pipeline, reject its grounding model"), M13 cashes the borrow on the prompt structure specifically.
