The Haiku system prompt is a ~120-line structural mirror of DeepSec's `packages/processor/src/prompt/core.ts` (~94 lines, read at `~/Developer/oss/deepsec/` 2026-05-15) with five Warden adaptations: (a) the severity classification table (`CRITICAL=RCE/auth-bypass/SQLi`, `HIGH=XSS/SSRF/secrets/insecure-deserialization`, `MEDIUM=open-redirect/weak-crypto/race-conditions`) maps explicitly to Warden's `tier` 1/2/3 schema; (b) DeepSec's 26-slug vocabulary is narrowed to **10 v0 slugs** covering the OWASP-ish core (`auth-bypass`, `missing-auth`, `rce`, `sql-injection`, `ssrf`, `path-traversal`, `secrets-exposure`, `insecure-crypto`, `xss`, `open-redirect`); (c) DeepSec's "false positive guidance" section (check for mitigations _before_ flagging — sanitization, middleware that wraps the handler directly, allowlists) is preserved verbatim because it pre-empts upstream the failure mode DeepSec's second-agent revalidation tries to fix downstream; (d) DeepSec's "auth bypass patterns to look for" section (parameter pollution, encoded characters, OAuth callback manipulation, cross-tenant ID, negated permission checks) is preserved because it's concrete subtle-pattern guidance the LLM benefits from beyond its training prior; (e) every reference DeepSec makes to free-form `description` / `recommendation` fields is replaced with citation-discipline language ("cite source line + sink line via `tool` sources; the substring-verifier post-pass verifies"). The 5 canonical worked examples from the M13 grilling (command injection, SQL injection, hardcoded secrets, weak crypto, missing auth on route handler) land as the prompt's "Worked Examples" section, demonstrating the citation shape on each slug.

5. **Confidence threshold subsystem — first user is `security`, future categories opt in.** CONTEXT.md §7's `[deferred]` ships in M13 because the Haiku sub-agent's output is inherently noisier than M12's leverage sub-agent (which is package-installed-gated and library-API-verified) or M7's committability sub-agent (which is added-files-gated and small-scope). Implementation: `Record<Category, number>` map (likely co-located with `PRIORITY_ORDER` in `packages/core/src/index.ts` or a new sibling `confidence.ts`). v0 values: `{ security: 0.8 }`; other categories implicit floor of 0 (no filtering). Applied as a new filter step in `applyHardRules` _before_ the priority sort, alongside the existing Tier-3 verbose gate. **Tier-1 findings bypass the gate unconditionally** — a clear-cut Tier-1 security finding (`eval(req.body)`) surfaces regardless of confidence, preserving the critical-finding short-circuit from the security-depth-tiers memory. One info-level `degradedWorkers` entry per drop batch; the message prints the effective floor after env override, not always the static default. Env override: `WARDEN_SECURITY_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR` validated in `@warden/env` (numeric, 0.0–1.0); per-category env vars added on demand when future categories ship with non-zero floors. No flag, no config file, no per-comment threshold (rejected as overengineering — `[M14+]` if a real consumer earns it).

6. **Disjointness — prompt-level scoping, not pipeline-level dedup.** The Haiku prompt's slug list explicitly notes which slugs ESLint already handles deterministically (`rce` partial via `detect-eval-with-expression` + `detect-child-process`, `insecure-crypto` partial via `detect-pseudoRandomBytes`, `secrets-exposure` partial via `eslint-plugin-no-secrets`) and instructs the LLM to focus on subtler subtypes the detector cannot catch — cross-tenant ID, missing-auth on route handlers, auth-bypass via parameter manipulation, SSRF, path-traversal in non-canonical sinks, secret-in-log, OAuth callback manipulation. Disjoint by prompt convention, not by code. Pattern-matches M12 leverage's scoping-by-example. If dogfood reveals consistent double-fire on specific slugs, the prompt is the right place to tighten — not adding a post-pass dedup at `(path, line)` ranges (considered as Q11B; rejected as pipeline complexity that pre-empts a problem dogfood hasn't surfaced).

7. **Schema, category, citation type — zero changes.** `'security'` already in `CategoryEnum` (`packages/core/src/schema.ts:34`); already slotted in `PRIORITY_ORDER` between `'correctness'` and `'vulnerability'` (`packages/core/src/index.ts:578`). Both producers emit existing `type: "tool"` sources. The detector keeps the ESLint diagnostic as the tool source and, for the Warden-managed security pass, also populates `ToolFinding.evidence` with the cited source line so the current M10 substring-verifier can validate it. The sub-agent cites source line + sink line (two sources per Comment when the flow spans lines). The substring-verifier walks each snippet-bearing `tool` source with the existing per-line `LINE_DRIFT = 5` algorithm; no new dispatch branch. The third milestone in a row (M11/M12/M13) where the citation infrastructure absorbs a new producer with zero schema work. ADR-0026 §13's "first of a family of producer integrations" framing pays out one more time.

8. **Runner contract — only the sub-agent rides M8; the detector remains inline.** ADR-0023 shipped the orchestration spine and committed M7's scalability + committability through the `Runner` contract; M12 added leverage's detector + sub-agent. M13 adds the security sub-agent as a new runner registering through `dispatch()` in `packages/core/src/index.ts` `orchestrationRunners`. The detector is an inline deterministic ESLint pass, recorded into the scratchpad next to the existing user-config ESLint result. The remaining inline runners (TSC, ESLint config-level, jscpd, vuln, deadcode, consistency, and now ESLint security) stay inline as accepted debt — M13 explicitly does not re-platform them.

9. **Mode gating — detector in `check` + `review`; sub-agent in `review` only.** Detector is deterministic and uses a Warden-owned ESLint security invocation, so it runs in both verbs whenever the pruned diff contains JS/TS files; it does not depend on the target repo's ESLint config existing or passing. Sub-agent makes an LLM call; per ADR-0011, `warden check` is the fast deterministic-only verb (pre-commit / CI gating), so it skips all sub-agents. The skip is silent (no `degradedWorkers` entry) — the user explicitly chose the fast verb; emitting "security suggestions unavailable in check mode; run `warden review` for the full pass" every time would be the noise pattern ADR-0025 rejected and ADR-0027 §8 reinforced.

10. **No teaser for M14 in M13's output.** The "consider `warden security` for deeper analysis" hint considered during grilling (Q12) was rejected: `warden security` does not exist in M13, so teasing a future verb pre-commits a discoverability surface before the verb's shape is settled. M14 introduces the verb and owns its discoverability via docs + `--help`. M13's output is self-contained — Haiku findings stand on their own value; users learn `warden security` exists when M14 releases.

11. **Forward compatibility — M14 introduces a dedicated security orchestration harness; M13's existing-harness use is on purpose.** Per the user's two-harness vision (M13 grilling pass): `warden review` keeps its single M8 harness; `warden security` (M14) gets a **separate** orchestration spine — own dispatch, own scratchpad, own synthesizer, own Sonnet specialist worker, multi-step pipeline (DeepSec-shaped scan → reason → cite with substring-verifier replacing LLM-judges-LLM revalidation). M13 deliberately stays in the existing harness because the harness split is M14's design decision; pre-committing to it in M13 would either (a) ship a refactor without a consumer or (b) constrain M14's harness shape unnecessarily. The Haiku sub-agent registering in `orchestrationRunners` alongside committability + leverage is the right v0 placement.

12. **FP handling — confidence floor is the only volume control; no escape hatch.** No inline `// warden-ignore-security` marker (every detector would have to respect it — wide commitment for unscheduled need), no per-category `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` (overlay is its own deferred milestone per ADR-0025), no LLM downgrade pass. The confidence floor handles volume; the DeepSec-borrowed FP guidance section in the prompt handles upstream FP suppression; the substring-verifier handles citation invalidity downstream. Three layers, deterministic outcome. Mirrors M7→M9 and M12 (ADR-0027 §9): tighten the detection or the prompt; the right escape hatch (if any) emerges from dogfood evidence, not speculative API surface.

**Why.**

- _Fills the longest-empty slot in the enum._ `'security'` has been in `CategoryEnum` + `PRIORITY_ORDER` since v0 (ADR-0012's tier-mapping rule explicitly named it). Every milestone since has shipped producers for other categories; security has been waiting on the worker-vs-deferred decision. M13 fills the default-review tier; M14 fills the deep tier. Splitting unblocks both.

- _The security-depth-tiers memory is finally implementable._ `project_warden_security_depth_tiers.md` named three tiers (always-on fast + default review + on-demand deep) over 6 months ago. M13 + M14 together cash the memory's framing exactly: detector + Haiku in default review (existing fast tier unchanged); Sonnet specialist in on-demand deep mode. The critical-finding short-circuit (Tier-1 bypasses the confidence gate) is the "critical findings short-circuit through the gate regardless of mode" line from the memory implemented as one policy rule.

- _DeepSec's prompt structure is mature prior art and replaceable in exactly the place ADR-0015 named._ ADR-0015 committed to borrowing DeepSec's pipeline and rejecting its grounding model. The prompt structure (severity, slug vocabulary, FP guidance, auth-bypass subtleties) is pure pipeline value-add; the grounding model (free-form `description`, second-agent revalidation) is the replaceable layer. M13 borrows the structure and replaces the grounding with citation discipline (every quoted snippet substring-verified). The borrow-vs-reject division ADR-0015 sketched in May 2026 cashes here.

- _Cheap-pass triage + on-demand-deep is the right cost shape._ Sonnet on every `warden review` for a category that fires on a small fraction of diffs is the wrong cost curve — Haiku is competent at the triage question ("is there anything here worth a deeper look?") and the confidence floor + substring-verifier suppress its noise floor. Sonnet earns its rent in M14's `warden security` precisely because the user opts in to the deeper pass. vision.md §3's "security: Sonnet-class" promise is honoured at the deep tier; M13's Haiku is the gate that decides when the deep tier is worth invoking (when the user reads M13's findings and runs the deep mode for more).

- _Confidence threshold subsystem earns its rent now._ §7 has been `[deferred]` since M4; v0 didn't need it because the existing five categories were tightly bounded by deterministic producers or scoped LLM tasks. Security is the first category whose default-review LLM output is inherently noisier than the substring-verifier alone suppresses — sub-agent surface is broad (10 slugs spanning injection/auth/crypto/secrets), and Haiku's confidence on subtler subtypes is variable. Shipping the subsystem in M13 unblocks future categories that need volume control (style is the obvious next candidate per CONTEXT.md §7's note).

- _Schema lean = M11 + M12 dividend repeating._ Four milestones in a row where the citation infrastructure absorbs a new producer with zero schema work. ADR-0026 §13 framed `api_def` as "the first of a family of producer integrations"; M12 was the second producer (leverage sub-agent); M13 is the third (Haiku via `lookupTypeDef` for library-API security claims). The bar for "new milestone earns its rent" is now "fits inside the existing schema and verifier" — M13 clears it without touching either.

- _Split protects M14's design space._ M14 is the worker tier ADR — the _first vision-tier worker_ (CONTEXT.md §3 reserves the term "worker" for specialist-LLM-in-multi-call-pipeline). Bundling M13 + M14 would force a single ADR to commit on the worker harness shape, the verb shape, the multi-step pipeline structure, AND the default-review producers in one shot. Splitting lets M14 enter its grilling pass with M13 dogfood evidence in hand (which slugs the Haiku consistently misses; which FPs the floor doesn't suppress; whether `lookupTypeDef` recall is the bottleneck).

- _No teaser is the honest answer to a deferred verb._ Q12's teaser options pre-committed to the discoverability surface for a verb that doesn't exist. The cleaner answer is "M14 owns its own discoverability." When the verb ships, the teaser concept can be re-evaluated against actual usage data, not speculation.

**Alternatives considered and rejected.**

- _AST taint-tracer for command injection (Q2/Q5 earlier answer, reversed during grilling)._ Ship an intra-procedural taint analyser at `packages/core/src/runners/taint.ts` covering command-injection sinks (`child_process.exec/execSync/spawn-with-shell`) with framework-aware source detection (Express, Hono, Bun, Next.js, Elysia). Rejected because: (a) framework-aware source detection means a curated framework adapter table, which the M12 library-table rejection (ADR-0027 §3 alternatives) already named as a maintenance anti-pattern — same trap; (b) intra-procedural dataflow analysis is ~700–1000 LOC of TS-Compiler-API-specific code that doesn't generalize to the multi-language future the user named during grilling ("backend might be in a different language than the frontend"); (c) the LLM does framework-recognition + flow-reasoning for free, language-agnostic, with substring-verified citations — the same trade ADR-0027 made for leverage's library-agnostic prompt. The taint-tracer might still earn rent in M14+ if dogfood reveals the LLM's flow recall has gaps the AST trace closes, but it's not v0.

- _Sonnet sub-agent in M13 (collapse M13 + M14)._ Use Sonnet from day 1 in the default-review path. Rejected because every `warden review` would pay Sonnet cost on a category that mostly fires on a small fraction of diffs; the on-demand-deep tier from the security-depth-tiers memory is precisely the right framing — Sonnet earns its rent when the user opts in, not on every review. The Haiku-then-Sonnet split also lets M14's worker grilling pass benefit from M13 dogfood evidence on which slugs need deep reasoning.

- _Detectors-only M13 (drop the Haiku sub-agent)._ Ship just the ESLint security plugins; defer all LLM analysis to M14's worker. Rejected because ESLint plugins alone catch a thin slice (eval, child_process, weak randomness, hardcoded secrets via entropy) — the dogfood feedback loop on "is security useful in Warden" would be too narrow to validate M14's worker design. The Haiku triage gives M13 enough signal breadth to inform M14's grilling.

- _Bundle M14 into M13._ Ship the worker + verb + dedicated harness + default-review producers in one milestone. Rejected because M14 is its own architectural commit (worker tier introduction, dedicated harness, verb shape, multi-step pipeline) that deserves a separate grilling pass; M13 is already substantial (confidence-threshold subsystem + DeepSec-borrowed prompt + two producers); splitting lets M13 ship in ~1.5 weeks vs M14's ~3 weeks, getting dogfood evidence sooner.

- _Teaser at end of `warden review` output (Q12 option A)._ Emit a `degradedWorkers` info entry pointing at `warden security`. Rejected because the verb being teased doesn't exist in M13. Cleaner to introduce discoverability with M14.

- _Per-category overlay for FP suppression._ The `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` surface from ADR-0008. Rejected per ADR-0025 (overlay is its own milestone, still unscheduled) and per ADR-0027 §9 (tighten detection; the right escape hatch emerges from dogfood evidence, not speculative API surface).

- _Larger initial slug set (DeepSec's 26)._ Ship all 26 DeepSec slugs from day 1. Rejected because v0 slug surface needs to be small enough that dogfood reveals which slugs earn their rent. 10 slugs covers the OWASP-ish core; M14+ adds slugs based on what dogfood shows the Haiku consistently misses (signal: every security suggestion the M14 worker makes that _should_ have been a triage hit becomes a candidate slug expansion).

- _Custom `@warden/eslint-plugin-security` package with Warden-specific rules._ Write our own rules. Rejected because off-the-shelf plugins (`eslint-plugin-security` + `eslint-plugin-no-secrets`) cover the bounded surface well; maintaining a custom plugin is the curated-library-table anti-pattern again, just applied to rules. Revisit if dogfood shows a specific gap.

- _Detector emits `kind: "question"` like the sub-agent (uniform comment kind)._ Both producers emit `kind: "question"` so the category-level discipline reads uniformly. Rejected because ESLint rules are mechanically present in the AST — calling them questions overclaims the LLM-synthesis layer that didn't run. Mixing assertion + question kinds within a single category is fine; ADR-0021's vulnerability detector + committability sub-agent already established the precedent and ADR-0027 §4 reinforced it.

- _Post-pass dedup at file+line range (Q11 option B)._ Drop Haiku findings whose `(path, line)` overlaps a detector finding within ±3 lines. Rejected as pipeline complexity that pre-empts a problem dogfood hasn't surfaced — if double-fire happens on specific slugs, the prompt is the right place to tighten, not a synthesizer-stage dedup.

- _Per-comment LLM-emitted threshold (Q8 option C)._ Let the LLM emit a per-comment `floor`. Rejected as overengineering — no current consumer needs it; map + env override is sufficient v0.

- _Pre-committing M14's harness shape in M13._ Sketch the dedicated security harness in ADR-0028 so M14 can pattern-match it. Rejected because the harness shape depends on the worker tier's contract (what does a `SpecialistWorker` look like? multi-step or single-step? streaming or batch?) — questions M14's grilling is supposed to answer. M13's ADR notes M14's harness as forward compat (§11) without constraining its shape.

**Caveats.**

- _Caveat — Haiku at the triage layer is a deliberate tradeoff._ vision.md §3 says "security: Sonnet-class … too important to skimp on." M13 deliberately uses Haiku for the triage half because: (a) the deep pass in M14 is Sonnet, so security gets Sonnet eventually; (b) Haiku at the triage layer answers "is there anything here worth a deeper look?" — a classification task Haiku is competent at; (c) the confidence floor (0.8) drops low-confidence Haiku output before render, so noise is suppressed at the gate; (d) the substring-verifier drops uncited claims downstream. If dogfood reveals Haiku's recall is too low even with these gates, the v0 fix is upgrading the sub-agent's model via a single-line change to `getWorkerCheapModel()` → `getWorkerStrongModel()`; the prompt + harness + threshold + verifier all stay unchanged.

- _Caveat — `lookupTypeDef` is exposed to the Haiku._ Third consumer of M11's tool (after the M11 formatter and the M12 leverage sub-agent). Library API security claims (e.g., "this `validator.escape(x)` actually escapes correctly") get the same `api_def` citation discipline as leverage's library-substitution claims. The tool's `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)` budget is per-call-site, so the security sub-agent has its own 8-call budget separate from the formatter's and leverage's. Total per-review tool budget is now 24 calls across three LLM call sites (formatter + leverage sub-agent + security sub-agent) — still bounded; M13 doesn't centralise this.

- _Caveat — confidence threshold subsystem's first user is security; future categories opt in via the map._ The map is open for expansion. v0 leaves all other categories implicit at floor 0 (no filtering). If dogfood reveals another category that needs volume control (style is the natural candidate per CONTEXT.md §7's note: "style/readability higher (very conservative on nits)"), add a key to the map and (optionally) a corresponding env var.

- _Caveat — ESLint plugin choice is dogfood-tunable._ v0 ships `eslint-plugin-security` + `eslint-plugin-no-secrets`. Other candidates (`eslint-plugin-no-unsanitized` for DOM XSS, `@microsoft/eslint-plugin-sdl` for broader SDL coverage) defer to dogfood evidence. The integration surface is one config entry per plugin in the existing ESLint runner; adding a plugin is hours, not days.

- _Caveat — disjointness is prompt-level, not pipeline-level._ If the Haiku ignores the prompt instruction and emits a finding ESLint already caught, double-fire happens. Per Q11A's rationale: we accept some duplicate signal as the cost of doing business when the alternative is more pipeline complexity. ADR-0025's "loud about subtrees, quiet about individual files" philosophy generalises: tighten the prompt when dogfood reveals consistent double-fire on specific slugs; don't add a dedup pass.

- _Caveat — M14 will introduce a dedicated security orchestration harness; M13's existing-harness use is on purpose._ The two-harness vision from M13 grilling (Ronit's agent-orch framing, also vision.md §3's inspiration) means M13's Haiku sub-agent registers in `orchestrationRunners` alongside committability + leverage in the existing M8 spine; M14 introduces a separate harness for `warden security`. M13's choice to stay in the existing harness is what makes M14's harness split a clean greenfield decision rather than a refactor.

- _Caveat — env-key graceful failure mirrors M12 leverage._ When `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is unset (or the Anthropic → Google cascade exhausts), `getWorkerCheapModel()` returns null and the sub-agent silently skips — emits one `degradedWorkers` entry (`{ kind: "info", topic: "security", message: "Security sub-agent skipped — no model available" }`) and returns empty findings. Mirrors M12 leverage's behaviour exactly; same path used by committability since M7.

- _Caveat — Tier-1 bypass is a policy decision, not a schema field._ The confidence-threshold filter inspects `comment.tier === 1` and short-circuits before checking the floor. No schema field, no LLM-emitted "I'm critical" signal — the policy reads structurally what the existing tier mapping already encodes. If the LLM emits a Tier-1 security finding with 0.6 confidence, it surfaces; if it emits Tier-2 at 0.6, it drops. The Haiku prompt is instructed to reserve Tier-1 for clear-cut patterns; substring-verification still applies.

- _Caveat — M13 inherits the ESLint runner's TS-only constraint (ADR-0008)._ The detector half is TS/JS only; the sub-agent half is in principle language-agnostic (the LLM analyses whatever diff content arrives), but Warden's ecosystem detection layer is currently TS-only, so v0 review only invokes the sub-agent on TS/JS files anyway. Multi-language security detection is an M14+ concern tied to the multi-ecosystem detector rewrite.

- _Caveat — design is locked; implementation specifics live in `m13-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0027 → `m12-plan.md`. ADR-0028 is the design commit; `m13-plan.md` is the file-by-file implementation brief. Future agents read both; ADR-0028 is the authority on design questions, `m13-plan.md` on implementation scope (exact runner naming, exact map location, exact plugin config shape, smoke harness scope).

**Status.** Done. M13 grilling pass complete (Q1 → Q12); design locked 2026-05-15; implementation landed the same day. Shipped surface: `security` category filled with Warden-owned ESLint security detector + Haiku triage sub-agent under the existing M8 spine (per ADR-0028 §8 + §11) + confidence-threshold subsystem (`packages/core/src/confidence.ts`, env override via `WARDEN_SECURITY_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR`) + DeepSec-borrowed system prompt (`packages/core/src/llm/prompts/security-system.md`) + rule-prefix routing in `to-comment.ts` (`security/*` + `no-secrets/*` → `{ category: "security", tier: 1 }`) + three smoke scripts (`pnpm smoke:m13`). Detector v0 rule set narrowed to the plan's eight conservative entries; noisy rules (`detect-unsafe-regex`, `detect-object-injection`, `detect-possible-timing-attacks`, `detect-non-literal-require`) deliberately off per dogfood evidence on the M13 diff itself. Opens the architectural arc that ADR-0029 will close with the M14 worker tier + dedicated security orchestration harness + `warden security` verb + Sonnet specialist multi-step pipeline.

---

## ADR-0029 — M14: dedicated security harness — Opus apex boss + per-file Sonnet investigators + Haiku classifiers + deterministic triage gate

**Decision.** M14 ships the on-demand deep tier of `project_warden_security_depth_tiers.md` and closes the architectural arc ADR-0028 opened. The shape is a **dedicated security orchestration harness** living alongside the M8 review spine (per ADR-0028 §11's two-harness vision) — not a refactor of M8, not a synthesizer swap, not a reuse of M8's dispatch. The harness runs a **six-phase pipeline** with a deterministic triage gate between det priors and LLM work: **Det Priors → Triage Gate → Boss Plan → Worker Fan-Out → Boss Synth → Citation Verify**. The boss seat upgrades to a new apex tier (Opus 4.7) that v0 sites have never used; the worker tier — `[deferred]` since vision.md §3 was sketched and explicitly named as still-deferred in ADR-0023 — finally ships, in the shape of **per-file Sonnet investigators with boss-picked slug subsets, plus Haiku classifiers for cheap subtasks** the boss spawns ad-hoc. ADR-0028 §11 predicted "Sonnet specialist worker" at the boss seat; the M14 grilling pass upgraded the framing to Opus-boss + Sonnet-workers + Haiku-classifiers, which earns its rent precisely because the deep tier is opt-in: the user explicitly invokes `warden security` (or `warden review --deep`) and signals "no holes barred, run the strongest available tier." Two CLI shapes ship, with **different semantics, not aliases**: `warden security` is a focused SAST verb that runs only the new harness; `warden review --deep` is a flag on `warden review` that runs the M8 spine (minus the M13 Haiku security sub-agent, which is superseded for this invocation) plus the M14 harness, and unions their outputs. Schema impact is zero — the `'security'` category was already in `CategoryEnum` since v0, both producers (workers + boss synthesis) emit existing `tool` / `api_def` source types, the substring-verifier dispatches on `type` as today, and `CommentSet` shape is unchanged. The architectural lift concentrates in three new pieces: the apex model tier in `@warden/ai`, the dedicated harness module in `@warden/core`, and the `security_runs` SQLite table that records per-invocation cost (the foundation a future M15+ ADR builds the weekly USD cap on).

The full surface:

1. **Six-phase pipeline — Det Priors → Triage Gate → Boss Plan → Worker Fan-Out → Boss Synth → Citation Verify.** Phase 1 (Det Priors) runs the security-relevant deterministic runners — M13's ESLint security detector + `npm audit` + OSV — and writes findings into a dedicated `SecurityScratchpad` (own type, own instance; not shared with the M8 scratchpad). Phase 1.5 (Triage Gate, no LLM) reads the scratchpad + the diff and decides whether the deep tier should engage at all. Phase 2 (Boss Plan, Opus 4.7, 1 call) generates a structured `Plan` — `subtasks[]` carrying `worker: 'sonnet' | 'haiku'`, `files: string[]`, `slugs: SecuritySlug[]`, optional `retrievedContext` excerpt — driven by diff + det priors + M5/M6 context selector output. Phase 3 (Worker Fan-Out) dispatches each subtask in parallel via `Promise.all` to a Sonnet investigator or Haiku classifier; workers are AI SDK `streamText` tool-use loops capped at `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)` and emit `SecurityFinding[]` with source-line + sink-line `tool` sources (or `api_def` sources when a finding hinges on a library API claim). Phase 4 (Boss Synth, Opus, 1 call) reads the scratchpad's accumulated worker outputs + det priors and synthesizes the final `CommentSet` for the `security` category — resolving cross-worker duplicates, picking highest-confidence framings, merging citations. Phase 5 (Citation Verify, no LLM) runs the existing M10/M11 substring-verifier unchanged; comments whose sources fail substring-match drop silently. The six-phase shape is the M14 contribution; the M8 spine collapses to four phases (no Plan, no Synth — det runners write directly to scratchpad and a single Sonnet synthesizer call emits the `CommentSet`).

2. **Dedicated harness — own dispatch, own scratchpad, own synthesizer — not a refactor of M8.** Per ADR-0028 §11's two-harness vision (Ronit's agent-orch framing): `warden review` keeps its M8 spine unchanged; `warden security` (and the `--deep` flag) invoke the new harness greenfield. Module location: `packages/core/src/security/` (sibling to `packages/core/src/orchestration/`, not nested inside it). Files: `harness.ts` (top-level entry, six-phase orchestration), `triage-gate.ts` (Phase 1.5 deterministic gate), `plan.ts` (Phase 2 Opus call + Plan schema), `worker.ts` (Phase 3 investigator + classifier shapes + tool wiring), `synth.ts` (Phase 4 Opus synthesis), `scratchpad.ts` (new `SecurityScratchpad` class — different shape from M8's `Scratchpad` because it carries Plan + worker outputs, not generic `RunnerOutput[]`). The dedicated harness is the architectural rent ADR-0028 §11 promised; M14 cashes it.

3. **Two CLI shapes — `warden security` (focused SAST verb) + `warden review --deep` (review + SAST flag).** Different semantics, not aliases: `warden security` invokes only the M14 harness — Phase 1 re-runs the security-relevant det runners (ESLint security + vuln/OSV) into the `SecurityScratchpad`, Phases 1.5–5 follow, and the output is a security-only `CommentSet`. `warden review --deep` invokes the M8 spine (minus M13's Haiku security sub-agent — see §6) and then the M14 harness in sequence; the M14 harness's Phase 1 reads the M8 scratchpad's already-populated ESLint security + vuln/OSV entries as priors rather than re-running them; outputs union at `CommentSet` level (no overlap by category — M8 owns everything _except_ `security` when `--deep`, M14 owns `security`). `warden check` is unaffected: it remains the fast deterministic-only verb (ADR-0011), and `--deep` does not exist on `warden check`. Both new entry points share the same `--base` / `--stdin` / `--json` / `--verbose` flag surface as `warden review` for consistency. The CLI verb registers in `packages/cli/src/index.ts` next to `review`/`check`/`init`.

4. **Apex model tier — `getApexModel()` → Opus 4.7; `getApexFallbackModel()` → Gemini 2.5 Pro.** New `@warden/ai/src/models.ts` entries alongside the existing boss/worker-strong/worker-cheap helpers. Two-step cascade per ADR-0017's existing fallback shape: Anthropic `claude-opus-4-7` → 1× retry with backoff → Google `gemini-2.5-pro` → hard fail. The existing `getBossModel()` stays `claude-sonnet-4-6` unchanged; M8's synthesizer + the M4 formatter call site continue to use Sonnet at the boss seat (zero impact on `warden review` cost). The apex tier is used by exactly two call sites in M14 — Phase 2 (Plan) and Phase 4 (Synth) — and only when the user invoked `warden security` or `warden review --deep`. Workers stay on `getWorkerStrongModel()` (Sonnet 4.6) and `getWorkerCheapModel()` (Haiku 4.5); no model changes downstream.

5. **Worker axis — per-file Sonnet investigators with boss-picked slug subsets + Haiku classifiers for cheap subtasks.** Each `Plan.subtasks[]` entry carries `worker: 'sonnet' | 'haiku'`, `files: string[]` (typically one file; boss can batch tightly-coupled files when warranted), `slugs: SecuritySlug[]` (subset of the M13 10-slug vocabulary the worker should focus on), and an optional `retrievedContext` excerpt sourced from the M5/M6 selector. Sonnet investigators do deep multi-turn investigation of their file(s) for their slug subset; Haiku classifiers do cheap one-shot classification of borderline cases (e.g., "is line 42 in `src/log.ts` `secrets-exposure` or `log-injection`?"). The boss decides the axis per-diff: trivial diffs may produce zero subtasks (boss-decided skip even after the triage gate proceeded); large diffs cluster cohesive files. Workers naturally parallelize via `Promise.all`; the M8 `Runner` contract is **not** reused — M14 workers have a different input shape (`SecurityWorkerInput`: `files`, `slugs`, `retrievedContext`, `repoRoot`, `tools`) and output shape (`SecurityWorkerOutput`: `findings: SecurityFinding[]`, `durationMs`, `error?`) because they're scoped to a slug subset + carry tool access the M8 contract doesn't model. The split is honest: the contract earned its rent for the existing M8 runners; M14's worker tier is a different shape and lives in its own file.

6. **`--deep` composition — M14 owns `security`, M8 spine skips M13 Haiku sub-agent.** When `--deep` is set, M8's dispatch gates the M13 Haiku security sub-agent on `!deep` and skips it; M8 still runs every other runner (TSC, ESLint config-level, ESLint security detector, vuln/OSV, jscpd, scalability, deadcode, consistency, committability, leverage, leverage-libraries). The M8 synthesizer emits its `CommentSet` covering all non-`security` categories. The M14 harness then runs and emits the `security`-category `CommentSet`. Outputs union at the CLI rendering layer; no dedup needed because the two harnesses own disjoint categories under `--deep`. The skip of M13's Haiku is silent for the `--deep` invocation (no `degradedWorkers` entry — the user opted into the deeper tier; emitting "Haiku skipped, Opus engaged" every time would be the noise pattern ADR-0025 §10 and ADR-0027 §8 rejected). The det runners (ESLint security + vuln/OSV) run exactly once per invocation — under `--deep`, the M14 harness reads M8's already-populated scratchpad rather than re-executing them.

7. **Phase 1.5 — deterministic Triage Gate skips Phase 2–5 when no security signal.** Cheap-skip behavior addressing the "tiny diff or non-security diff shouldn't pay deep-tier cost" concern. After Phase 1 (Det Priors) completes, the gate evaluates two deterministic signals: **(a)** any det prior emitted a finding/candidate (ESLint security rule hit, vuln/OSV match); **(b)** the diff touches a path matching `SECURITY_SENSITIVE_PATTERNS` — a hardcoded glob list in `packages/core/src/security/triage-gate.ts` covering `**/{auth,login,signin,signup,session,oauth}/**`, `**/api/**`, `**/routes/**`, `**/middleware/**`, `**/crypto/**`, `**/encrypt/**`, `**/db/**`, `**/queries/**`, `**/migrations/**`, `*.sql`, lockfiles (`package-lock.json`, `pnpm-lock.yaml`, `yarn.lock`), and `*.env*`. If **both** signals are negative, the gate emits a single info-level `degradedWorkers` entry (`{ kind: "info", topic: "security", message: "Deep security analysis skipped — diff has no security-relevant content (no det findings; no path matches)" }`), produces an empty `security`-category `CommentSet`, and returns. Phases 2–5 never run. If **either** signal is positive, the gate proceeds to Phase 2; the boss can still emit `subtasks: []` if it judges the trigger noise (e.g., a `package.json` bump that adds a dev-dep with no transitive vuln), so the gate is conservative-permissive: it filters the obvious-skip cases, the boss filters the borderline cases. The pattern list is intentionally hardcoded in v0 (not user-configurable) to keep the gate fast and predictable; user override + per-repo extension lands in the M15+ init-time security inventory ADR alongside the richer scan-driven gate. The Tier-1 critical-finding short-circuit from `project_warden_security_depth_tiers.md` still applies upstream: M13's ESLint security detector flags Tier-1 findings on `eval(req.body)` etc., and those surface via the M8 spine in default `warden review` regardless of whether the user invokes `--deep`. The Triage Gate skip-case never suppresses a Tier-1 finding because M14 never reaches a Tier-1 finding the M8 path doesn't already surface.

8. **Worker tools — `lookupTypeDef` + `readFile` (repo-scoped) + `grepRepo` (bounded), exposed only to workers.** Sonnet investigators and Haiku classifiers receive three tools via AI SDK v6's `tool()` primitive: **(a)** `lookupTypeDef` — M11's existing tool (third consumer after the M11 formatter and the M12/M13 sub-agents); same `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)` budget per worker — total per-review tool-call budget is bounded by (8 × number of workers), not centralized. **(b)** `readFile` — new tool at `packages/core/src/security/tools/read-file.ts`. Inputs: `path` (repo-relative), `startLine?`, `endLine?`. Constraints: path-traversal check (resolved path must stay under `repoRoot`), default-deny list for `.env*` / `*.pem` / `*.key` / `*.p12` / `*.pfx` / `.git/**` / files matching common-secret regex (`API_KEY=`, `PRIVATE_KEY`, etc. — implementation reuses M13's `no-secrets` plugin entropy detection where practical), gitignore-honored (skips files Git ignores), 1000-line-per-call cap (truncates with explicit `…` marker if exceeded). **(c)** `grepRepo` — new tool at `packages/core/src/security/tools/grep-repo.ts`. Inputs: `pattern` (literal substring in v0, regex deferred to dogfood evidence), optional `glob` filter. Constraints: max 200 results (truncates with count), repo-scoped paths, same secret-file deny list as `readFile`, gitignore-honored. Tool errors swallowed inside `execute()` so the cascade retry path is unaffected (matches M11's tool wrapper pattern). The **boss has no tools** — Phase 2 (Plan) and Phase 4 (Synth) are single-shot calls; the boss reasons from diff + det priors + retrieved context + worker outputs without tool access, on the principle that the boss's job is planning/synthesis and the workers' job is investigation. If a boss-side claim mis-cites, the M10/M11 substring-verifier drops the source post-hoc, same as today. Bash/exec is a hard no in v0 — would violate ADR-0013's I/O-pure spirit and opens supply-chain attack vectors via LLM-generated commands.

9. **Cost story — no estimate, no default cap, env knob, post-hoc cost line + `security_runs` table.** The M14 deep tier is opt-in by the verb's name (`warden security`) or by an explicit flag (`--deep`); the user has signalled they accept the cost. M14 does **not** print a pre-flight estimate (estimation requires per-model cost tables Warden doesn't currently maintain and per-Plan token-count estimation is too inaccurate to be load-bearing), does **not** prompt for confirmation, and does **not** impose a default worker cap. The single knob the user has is `WARDEN_SECURITY_WORKER_BUDGET` (`@warden/env`, optional positive integer; unset = unbounded); when set, the boss is told the cap in its planning prompt and decides which N files earn workers when the diff exceeds the cap (boss can batch tightly-coupled files into one worker). The end-of-run CLI output prints a cost line (`Cost: $0.34 — Opus: $0.18 · Sonnet x8: $0.14 · Haiku x3: $0.02`) computed from the AI SDK's `usage` objects + a static per-model `$/1M tokens` table in `packages/core/src/security/cost.ts` (input + output rates current as of M14 ship date, updated when Anthropic/Google bump pricing). Every invocation writes a row to a new SQLite table `security_runs` in `@warden/db` carrying `(id, timestamp, model_boss, model_worker_strong, model_worker_cheap, input_tokens, output_tokens, cost_usd, comments_emitted, mode)` where `mode ∈ {'security', 'review-deep'}`. This table is the foundation a future M15+ ADR builds the weekly USD cap + `--max-cost <usd>` flag on; v0 records but does not enforce.

10. **Confidence floor carve-out — M14 output bypasses `applyConfidenceFloor()`.** M13's `CATEGORY_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR: { security: 0.8 }` and `applyConfidenceFloor()` in `packages/core/src/confidence.ts` were designed to suppress Haiku triage noise in the M8 default-review path. M14's epistemic structure is materially different: Opus boss does planning + synthesis, Sonnet workers investigate with tools, the M10/M11 substring-verifier drops every uncited claim, and the DeepSec-borrowed FP-guidance section in the worker prompt pre-empts FPs upstream. Applying the 0.8 floor to M14 output would drop Opus-vetted, citation-verified findings the user explicitly opted into the deep tier to surface — undermines the "no holes barred" framing. M14's `applyHardRules()` call site gains a harness-context discriminator: `applyHardRules(comments, { harness: 'm8-review' | 'm14-security' })`. The `m14-security` branch skips the confidence-floor step entirely; the substring-verifier remains the sole gate. M13's floor stays in place for the M8 path unchanged. Tier-1 bypass (which already short-circuits the floor in M13's path) continues to apply on both paths.

11. **Schema, output, and CommentSet shape — zero changes.** `'security'` already in `CategoryEnum` since v0; `PRIORITY_ORDER` slot unchanged; `Source.type ∈ { 'tool', 'api_def', ... }` unchanged. Workers emit `SecurityFinding[]` internally, but `Boss Synth` maps each surviving finding into a standard `Comment` of `kind: 'question' | 'assertion'` (boss decides per-finding) carrying the existing `tool`/`api_def` source variants — there is no new `Comment` field for "taint flow visualization" or "data-flow path" in v0, and no new `Source.type` discriminant. The substring-verifier walks `comment.sources` and dispatches on `type` exactly as in M11/M12/M13; M14 adds no verifier branch. The output a user sees is structurally indistinguishable from `warden review` output — same `Comment` schema, same priority ordering, same JSON shape under `--json`. This is the fourth milestone in a row (M11/M12/M13/M14) where the citation infrastructure absorbs a new producer with zero schema work; ADR-0026 §13's "first of a family of producer integrations" framing keeps paying out.

12. **Forward compatibility — what M14 explicitly does not ship.** **(a)** Weekly USD cap + `--max-cost <usd>` flag + per-model cost table maintenance: M15+ ADR, gated on having a week of M14 dogfood data to size the cap honestly. The `security_runs` table M14 ships is the foundation. **(b)** Slug expansion beyond the M13 10-slug set: M15+ ADR, driven by dogfood evidence on which subtler slugs the v0 surface misses. **(c)** Init-time security inventory (`.warden/security-inventory.json` populated by a new `warden init` scan phase, consumed by a richer Phase 1.5 gate + Phase 2 Plan): M15+ ADR; addresses recall limits the path-glob gate has. The Phase 1.5 v0 shape is intentionally cheap-and-narrow so the inventory upgrade is purely additive (gate gains a third signal, no API changes). **(d)** AST candidate-scanner expansion of Phase 1 (DeepSec-style ~26 matchers): M15+; gated on dogfood showing the boss has trouble noticing patterns ESLint security misses. **(e)** Per-worker output caching keyed on `(file_sha, slugs, worker_prompt_version, model_id)`: M15+; gated on dogfood evidence that re-runs of the same files are common enough to earn the table. **(f)** Repo-wide audit mode (`warden security --all`): M15+; the diff-scoped v0 default keeps cost bounded and matches existing UX. **(g)** Boss-side tool access: M15+ if dogfood reveals the boss needs to verify library API claims directly during synthesis (today, the substring-verifier catches mis-cites post-hoc, which is the same epistemic floor M11 set). **(h)** Multi-language security detection beyond TS/JS: tied to the multi-ecosystem detector rewrite (ADR-0008 backlog). **(i)** `warden security` in a non-git working directory: errors loudly in v0 (no diff source); M15+ may add `--all` for repo-wide audit independent of git state. **(j)** Hosted-mode deep-tier execution: M15+ alongside ADR-0019's cloud-hosted index work.

**Why.**

- _Two-harness vision cashes the rent ADR-0028 §11 promised._ M13 deliberately stayed inside the M8 spine so M14's harness split could be a clean greenfield decision rather than a refactor. M14 cashes that decision: the new harness has its own dispatch, scratchpad, synthesizer, and lives in a sibling module (`packages/core/src/security/`), preserving the M8 spine for `warden review` invocations and avoiding the architectural tax a synthesizer-swap or scratchpad-share would have imposed.

- _Six-phase pipeline absorbs both prior arts honestly._ Ronit's agent-orch blog contributes the Route → Execute → Synthesize → Grade shape (M14 collapses Grade into the citation verifier per ADR-0015's borrow/reject division). DeepSec contributes the per-file investigation pattern + tool-access-for-context + concurrency-aware fan-out. Neither is sufficient alone for Warden's context (diff-scoped, citation-disciplined, AI-SDK-only); the synthesis is the M14 design contribution. Phase 1.5's deterministic triage gate is original to M14 — neither source has it; both would have benefited from it.

- _Per-file workers with boss-picked slug subsets is the only axis that uses every tier._ Pure per-slug (10 fixed workers) wastes tokens on slugs the diff doesn't touch. Pure per-file (DeepSec-style, no slug subset) wastes tokens on slugs each file doesn't have. Per (file, slug) explodes worker count. Per-concern (4 fixed buckets) is arbitrary. Per-file-with-boss-picked-slugs makes the boss earn its rent (planning is a real decision, not a static rule) and parallelizes naturally — the only axis where every tier's work matches its tier's reasoning capability.

- _Phase 1.5 closes the "wasted deep-tier on a typo diff" gap._ Without a gate, `warden review --deep` on a README typo would pay full Opus + worker cost for guaranteed-zero return. The deterministic gate (path globs + det priors) skips Phases 2–5 in those cases, costs sub-millisecond, and emits an honest "skipped" info entry. The gate is intentionally cheap and dumb in v0; the M15+ init-time inventory makes it precise once dogfood reveals what the globs miss.

- _Opus apex tier is the marginal upgrade that earns its rent only at the opt-in tier._ `warden review` runs on every PR; using Opus globally would inflate cost on a category most diffs don't trigger. `warden security` and `warden review --deep` are explicit opt-ins; the user has signalled they accept the apex tier's cost. Sonnet at workers (vision.md §3 "security: Sonnet-class … too important to skimp on") + Opus at boss seats (planning + synthesis only) bracket the cost-quality curve at the deep tier without inflating the default tier.

- _Citation verifier replaces grading cleanly._ Vision.md §3 specifies a Grade step as separate from Synthesis; ADR-0015 already rejected the LLM-judges-LLM grading model in favor of substring verification. M14 honors that rejection: the substring-verifier IS the grader. The boss synthesizes (resolves duplicates, picks framings); the verifier grades (drops uncited claims). Two distinct cognitive tasks done by tools that match their reasoning surface — synthesis is fuzzy (LLM); grading is mechanical (verifier).

- _Worker tool kit gives DeepSec's capability without DeepSec's lock-in._ DeepSec uses Claude Agent SDK to give its investigator file-system access; that locks them to Anthropic. Warden's `readFile` + `grepRepo` (via AI SDK v6's native `tool()` primitive) gives workers the same dataflow-tracing capability while preserving ADR-0005's AI-SDK-only invariant. The original ADR-0029 assumption that tool-using workers could inherit ADR-0017's Gemini fallback is superseded by ADR-0017's 2026-05-17 amendment: `tools[] + Output.object()` call sites are Anthropic-only until ADR-0033 settles worker fallback.

- _Zero schema changes is the architectural rent on M11's keystone._ ADR-0026 §13 framed `api_def` as "the first of a family of producer integrations." M12 was the second producer (leverage sub-agent), M13 was the third (security Haiku sub-agent), M14 is the fourth (security workers + boss synthesis). The schema absorbs each new producer without modification; the verifier dispatches on `type` unchanged. The bar for "new milestone earns its rent" is now "fits inside the existing schema" — M14 clears it.

- _Confidence-floor carve-out is honest, not lazy._ M13's floor was designed for Haiku's noise floor in the default-review path. M14's Opus-boss-led pipeline + worker citation discipline + substring-verifier is a materially different epistemic structure. Applying the same floor to both would be cargo-culting M13's tuning to M14's surface. The carve-out preserves the floor where it earns its rent (M8 path) and removes it where it would drop signal (M14 path).

- _Cost-table-but-no-cap defers the policy decision to data._ The user's stated intent ("no holes barred unless user sets cap") + the unknowns around weekly-vs-per-run-vs-per-turn semantics + the precision of per-model cost tables all point toward shipping the recording infrastructure now (`security_runs` table + post-hoc cost line) and deferring the enforcement policy to M15+ once a week of dogfood data is available to size defaults. The `WARDEN_SECURITY_WORKER_BUDGET` knob is the only escape valve in v0; that's deliberate.

- _Different semantics for verb vs flag earns rent._ `warden security` as an alias of `warden review --deep` would have collapsed the two surfaces to one shape; the different-semantics framing makes each path's identity clear — verb is "focused security pass"; flag is "everything plus deep security." Future users grepping for the verb find a verb that does what its name implies (no implicit `review` work); future CI configs using the flag get the full review they expect.

- _Worker contract divergence from M8 is honest._ M14's workers take slug subsets + tool access + retrieved context; M8's `Runner` contract has none of these. Forcing the new shape through the old contract would have required additive optional fields that mostly read `undefined` on the existing M8 runners — false abstraction. The M14 worker shape lives in its own file, has its own contract, and shares only the type union of `CommentSet` with M8 at the output boundary.

**Alternatives considered and rejected.**

- _Reuse M8 spine with synthesizer swap._ When `--deep`, replace M8's Sonnet synthesizer with M14's Opus-led pipeline; share the scratchpad. Rejected because (a) M14's scratchpad has Plan + worker outputs, not generic `RunnerOutput[]` — the schema would need a discriminated union M8 doesn't have; (b) the M13 Haiku sub-agent skip becomes a configuration on M8's dispatch rather than a clean two-harness separation; (c) it undermines ADR-0028 §11's deliberate "M14 introduces a separate harness" commitment. The two-harness shape is the architectural primitive M14 is supposed to introduce.

- _Claude Agent SDK as the worker primitive._ Adopt `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` (DeepSec's choice) for workers; gives unfettered file-system + bash access + native Task subagent dispatch. Rejected because (a) it violates ADR-0005's single-SDK invariant; (b) it locks the security mode to Anthropic, breaking ADR-0017's cross-provider cascade; (c) `readFile` + `grepRepo` via AI SDK's native `tool()` covers the dataflow-tracing capability that motivates Agent SDK without the lock-in. Revisit only if dogfood reveals AI SDK's tool-use loop is insufficient for the investigation depth M14 wants.

- _Single Opus agent loop, no worker tier._ One Opus session with tools investigates the whole diff iteratively; no Sonnet or Haiku sub-calls. Simplest code, single model bill. Rejected because (a) it makes the cheap tier (Haiku) illusory — the user's stated intent named both Sonnet and Haiku as delegation targets; (b) it forfeits parallelism on bigger diffs (a 20-file diff serially investigated is slow); (c) it inflates Opus token spend on tasks Sonnet would handle adequately. Worker fan-out is the cost-quality optimization the apex tier earns its rent against.

- _Hybrid: manual boss dispatch with agentic workers (each worker is a tool-use loop)._ Same as the chosen design — except this is no longer rejected; M14 ships the hybrid. Recording here for clarity: the "boss = single-shot calls; worker = tool-use loops" shape is the M14 design, not an alternative. The genuine alternative was "boss = tool-use loop too," which is rejected per §8 (the boss has no tools).

- _Per-slug fixed workers (10 workers regardless of diff)._ Each slug gets its own Sonnet worker scanning the whole diff. Rejected because (a) wastes tokens on slugs no file in the diff would trigger; (b) per-slug specialization is achieved more cheaply via slug-subset hints in a generic worker prompt; (c) the cost ceiling is 10× the per-file cost on small diffs where most slugs are irrelevant. Per-file with boss-picked slug subset uses every tier's capability honestly.

- _Per-concern bucket workers (taint-flow / auth / crypto-secrets / web-injection)._ Four fixed workers; each takes the whole diff. Rejected because the bucket boundaries are arbitrary (where does `secrets-exposure` live — crypto-secrets or with `xss` under web?), and per-bucket prompts duplicate context that's shared across slugs. Per-file with slug subset earns the same precision without the bucket-mapping ceremony.

- _Per (file, slug) Cartesian product._ Boss generates one worker per (file × applicable-slug) pair. Maximum precision per worker (each has the tightest possible scope), but cost blows up on bigger diffs (5 files × 5 plausible slugs = 25 workers per review). Token-efficient only when every pair has a real finding; in practice most pairs would produce nothing. Per-file with boss-picked slug subset trades per-worker scope for cost predictability.

- _Bash/exec as a worker tool._ Give workers `bashExec` so they can run `ast-grep`, custom matchers, project scripts. Most powerful tool surface; mirrors DeepSec's Agent SDK capability. Rejected because (a) it violates ADR-0013's I/O-pure core spirit (the core would shell out to arbitrary LLM-generated commands); (b) opens supply-chain attack vectors (LLM-generated commands execute against the user's working directory); (c) `readFile` + `grepRepo` covers the legitimate use cases workers need without the blast radius. Hard no for v0.

- _Pre-flight cost estimate + `--max-cost <usd>` flag._ Before Phase 3 fans out, print "Est: $0.34, ~45s; proceed?" and accept `--max-cost` to abort. Considered seriously and rejected (per the M14 grilling): estimation requires per-model cost tables maintained by Warden (real maintenance burden as Anthropic/Google bump pricing), Plan token-count estimation is too inaccurate to be load-bearing for the gate decision, and the verb name itself is the warning. M15+ revisits with the weekly USD cap shape once dogfood evidence supports the policy decision.

- _Default worker cap (e.g. 20)._ Cap worker count by default; user sets the env var to lift. Rejected because (a) "no holes barred unless user sets cap" was the user's stated intent — the default is unbounded; (b) the M9 noise filter already prunes pathological diffs upstream; (c) the user's escape valve is the env var, which sets a per-run cap when the user wants one. Belt-and-suspenders cap is over-engineering for v0.

- _Apply the M13 `security: 0.8` confidence floor to M14 output too._ Consistent treatment across both harnesses. Rejected because M14's pipeline has structurally different epistemic ground (Opus + Sonnet + verifier + boss synthesis); applying the Haiku-tuned floor would drop Opus-vetted, verified findings the user explicitly opted in to see. The carve-out preserves the floor where it earns its rent and removes it where it would suppress signal.

- _Three-step apex cascade (Opus → Sonnet → Gemini Pro)._ Survives Opus rate-limits without leaving Anthropic. Rejected because Sonnet at the boss seat undermines the entire `--deep` framing — the user opted into the apex tier; silently downgrading to the boss-tier model defeats the opt-in. Better to hard-fail loudly than silently downgrade. Two-step cascade (Anthropic Opus → Google Gemini Pro → hard fail) preserves the apex tier across providers.

- _Hard-fail M14 if Opus unavailable; no Google fallback._ Simplest cascade. Rejected because it hard-couples M14 to Anthropic Opus's availability; transient Anthropic outages break `warden security` entirely. ADR-0017's existing cross-provider fallback shape applies cleanly to the apex tier.

- _Per-call BYO model override (`--apex-model <id>`)._ Most flexible; lets the user pick Gemini Pro or local models at invocation. Rejected because BYOLLM is the deferred ADR-0006 milestone; bringing it forward for M14 alone forces every other tier to gain the same surface for symmetry.

- _DeepSec-style AST candidate scanner as Phase 1 expansion._ Add a Warden-owned AST scanner emitting 20+ slug candidates per file before workers fan out. Rejected for M14 v0 because (a) Warden's diff is already small (typical PR ≤50 files post-noise-filter); the candidate scan space is narrow; the boss can reason from file content directly; (b) M13 deliberately rejected `@warden/eslint-plugin-security` for the same reason — off-the-shelf is sufficient; (c) the candidate scanner is real new code that's its own grilling pass. M15+ ADR if dogfood shows the boss has trouble noticing things ESLint security misses.

- _Slug expansion beyond M13's 10 slugs._ DeepSec ships 26 slugs; M14 could match. Rejected per ADR-0028's existing M14+ gating ("M14+ adds slugs based on what dogfood shows the Haiku consistently misses") — the M13 ship date is the same day as this grilling pass, so there's no dogfood evidence yet. Expansion is M15+.

- _Init-time security inventory now._ Add a scan phase to `warden init` that catalogues security-sensitive call sites repo-wide; Phase 1.5 gate consults it. Rejected because (a) it's real new code in `warden init` with its own incremental-maintenance concerns; (b) the v0 path-glob gate is sufficient for the "skip on README typo" case the user surfaced; (c) the inventory upgrades the gate's precision additively when M15+ schedules it.

- _Per-worker output caching._ Cache `worker_output` keyed on `(file_sha, slugs, worker_prompt_version, model_id)` so re-runs reuse work. Rejected for v0 because `warden security` re-runs are likely rare (user opts in deliberately; diff content shifts between runs); the cache would mostly read-miss. Defer to M15+ if dogfood reveals re-run patterns that earn the table.

- _Repo-wide audit mode (`warden security --all`)._ Investigate the whole repo, not just the diff. Powerful; matches DeepSec's default. Rejected for v0 because (a) it's a different cost shape (1000s of workers possible); (b) `--all` deserves its own UX grilling (does it audit every file, or sample? does it batch heavily? does it require `warden init`?); (c) the diff-scoped default matches existing `warden review` UX and is the cheaper-to-reason-about v0.

- _Boss tool access (Phases 2 + 4)._ Give the boss `lookupTypeDef` + `readFile` so it can verify library API claims during planning/synthesis. Rejected because (a) workers already have the tools — boss delegates the lookup; (b) tool calls inside the boss prompt inflate token spend on every Plan/Synth invocation; (c) the substring-verifier catches boss mis-cites post-hoc, same epistemic floor as M11+. Revisit M15+ if dogfood reveals boss-side library claims slipping past the verifier.

- _New `Source.type` for taint flows or data-flow paths._ Workers emit findings with a structured `flow: { sourceLine, sinkLine, path[] }` source. Visualizes the data flow. Rejected for v0 — workers emit `tool` sources (source-line + sink-line as two separate sources) which the existing M10 verifier handles unchanged. A structured flow type is a presentation feature, not a verification feature; ship it M15+ if the CLI rendering or future GitHub bot consumes it.

**Caveats.**

- _Caveat — design depends on M13 having shipped clean._ M14 reads M8's scratchpad under `--deep` (Phase 1 priors); the M13 ESLint security detector + vuln/OSV runner are the populated entries. Both shipped 2026-05-15 and are in the scratchpad already. Standalone `warden security` re-runs them; the implementation must keep the runners callable in both contexts.

- _Caveat — apex cost is real._ Opus 4.7 input ≈ $15/M, output ≈ $75/M (current Anthropic pricing). A typical `warden review --deep` with 5 worker subtasks costs ~$0.30–$0.80 per invocation depending on file size and tool-use depth. The `security_runs` table records exact costs per invocation; dogfood evidence will refine M15+'s weekly cap default.

- _Caveat — Phase 1.5 path globs are a starting point, not a final list._ `SECURITY_SENSITIVE_PATTERNS` will miss real security-relevant changes whose paths don't match (e.g., a file named `src/utils.ts` that contains a route handler). The gate is conservative-permissive: the det-prior signal compensates (any ESLint security hit triggers proceed regardless of path), and the M15+ init-time security inventory upgrades precision. False-skip rate is the dogfood metric; M15+ adjusts.

- _Caveat — `readFile` and `grepRepo` have real safety constraints to engineer correctly._ Path-traversal checks must handle symlinks correctly (resolve to canonical path, verify under `repoRoot`). Secret-file deny list must handle filename variations (`.env`, `.env.local`, `.env.production`, etc.). gitignore-honoring must use a parser that handles negations (`!foo/`). 1000-line cap must truncate cleanly with an explicit marker so the LLM knows it received a partial file. These are real engineering risks the implementation must address; smoke tests should cover each.

- _Caveat — boss-decided file batching is a tunable not yet tuned._ The Plan schema allows `files: string[]` per subtask so the boss can batch tightly-coupled files (e.g., `src/auth/handler.ts` + `src/auth/middleware.ts` in one worker). The boss's prompt instructs it to batch when files share state but split when they don't; v0 ships with the instruction and refines based on dogfood. Excessive batching loses parallelism; insufficient batching inflates token spend on shared context.

- _Caveat — `warden security` standalone re-runs det runners not strictly needed._ When `warden security` is invoked, Phase 1 re-runs ESLint security + vuln/OSV (they didn't run in the M8 spine, which wasn't invoked). This is correct behavior but slightly wasteful if the user previously ran `warden review` on the same diff. v0 accepts the duplication; M15+ could cache det runner output keyed on diff hash + det version, but the cost is small and the caching adds complexity not yet justified.

- _Caveat — the Haiku classifier path is structurally implemented but lightly exercised in v0._ The Plan schema allows `worker: 'haiku'` subtasks; the worker dispatcher routes them to `getWorkerCheapModel()`. But Haiku classifiers earn their rent on borderline cases the boss spawns ad-hoc, and v0 dogfood may not exercise that path heavily — the boss may default to Sonnet investigators for everything. v0 ships the surface; M15+ tunes the prompt to push borderline subtasks to Haiku once dogfood reveals what "borderline" looks like in practice.

- _Caveat — `warden review --deep` runs sequentially (M8 then M14), not in parallel._ M14's Phase 1 reads M8's scratchpad as priors; that dependency means M8 must complete first. Sequential execution adds latency (M8's ~30s + M14's ~60s = ~90s wall-clock instead of max(30, 60) = 60s). Acceptable for an opt-in deep tier; M15+ could parallelize by having M14 re-run det priors itself when `--deep` is invoked, trading double det-cost for halved latency. v0 picks correctness + cost over latency.

- _Caveat — slug coverage matches M13 exactly; expansion is dogfood-gated._ The 10-slug vocabulary (`auth-bypass`, `missing-auth`, `rce`, `sql-injection`, `ssrf`, `path-traversal`, `secrets-exposure`, `insecure-crypto`, `xss`, `open-redirect`) is the same set M13 ships. Workers are scoped to this set in their system prompt; the Plan schema's `slugs[]` field uses the same enum. Expansion is M15+ work driven by "every finding the M14 worker emits that _should_ have been a triage hit in M13" — same gating M13 set against itself.

- _Caveat — model IDs are pinned to the M14 ship date._ `claude-opus-4-7` (Anthropic), `gemini-2.5-pro` (Google), `claude-sonnet-4-6` (Anthropic worker strong), `claude-haiku-4-5-20251001` (Anthropic worker cheap) are the v0 selections. When Anthropic or Google ship a successor, the helpers in `@warden/ai/src/models.ts` get a one-line bump per provider per tier. No persistence depends on these IDs at the M14 surface (the `security_runs` table records the model ID per run, so historical cost analysis survives upgrades).

- _Caveat — Phase 4 (Boss Synth) is a different prompt from M4/M8 synthesizers._ The M4/M8 synthesizer prompt (`packages/core/src/llm/prompts/{system,user-template}.md`) is designed to triage findings across every category. M14's Phase 4 synthesizes only `security`-category worker outputs into a final CommentSet; the prompt focuses on security framing, FP suppression, and citation discipline. New file `packages/core/src/security/prompts/synth-system.md` (and matching user template). The same prompts-as-files discipline (ADR-0015) applies.

- _Caveat — design is locked; implementation specifics live in `m14-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0026 → `m11-plan.md`, ADR-0027 → `m12-plan.md`, ADR-0028 → `m13-plan.md`. ADR-0029 is the design commit; `m14-plan.md` is the file-by-file implementation brief. Future agents read both; ADR-0029 is the authority on design questions, `m14-plan.md` on implementation scope (exact module layout, prompt content, smoke harness scope, cost-table values, glob list, secret-deny list).

**Status.** Superseded by ADR-0030 (2026-05-16); preserved-plan path renamed by ADR-0031 (2026-05-16), ADR-0032 (2026-05-16), and the M17 setup reservation (2026-05-19). The grilling pass that produced ADR-0029 informed the M14-security design, but the M14 ship vehicle was redirected to a default-review harness instead — the harness needed to feel right before the deep tier could be layered on top. The 6-phase security pipeline + apex Opus 4.7 tier + `warden security` verb + `warden review --deep` flag + `securityRuns` cost table all remain valid design; they are preserved at `m18-plan.md` and will land under a future ADR once `warden review`'s harness lifecycle gives the deep tier a stable foundation to sit on. 2026-05-17 finalisation amendment: M18 keeps Gemini fallback only for tool-less structured-output call sites (Boss Plan, Boss Synth, no-tool classifier); tool-using investigator workers are Anthropic-only and degrade cleanly with "Gemini fallback skipped (tools required)" until ADR-0033. ADR-0029 should be read as the authoritative pre-existing thinking for that future milestone except for that fallback-boundary amendment; do not re-grill from scratch.

---

## ADR-0030 — M14: default-review harness — Opus 4.6 boss + dynamic dispatch loop + six per-(file, concern-subset) workers + three-phase pipeline

**Context.** Through M13, `warden review` reached default review on six categories (correctness, scalability, consistency, security, committability, leverage). Three of those categories shipped as one-off Haiku sub-agents bolted onto the M8 spine — committability (M7), leverage-libraries (M12), security (M13). Each sub-agent had its own prompt, its own runner file, and its own narrow scope. Copilot reviews on PRs #3 / #5 / #6 / #8 / #14 / #15 surfaced six classes of issue (doc-vs-code drift, scalability regressions, parallelism issues, path safety, silent failures, multi-line snippet bugs) that none of those sub-agents could catch because each sees only its slice. The default review path needed a boss with eyes on the whole diff, not a parallel committee of cheap-tier mini-LLMs.

ADR-0029 designed exactly this shape, but scoped it to a deep security tier with apex Opus 4.7 — the cake-vs-icing framing in `CLAUDE.md`'s M14+ entry. The grilling pass that produced ADR-0030 inverted the priority: the default review path is the cake; the deep security tier is the icing. M14 ships the default review path; M15+ adds the deep tier on top.

**Decision.** M14 implements a **default-review harness** at `packages/core/src/review-harness/` that takes over `warden review` end-to-end. The harness has three phases, one dynamic boss loop, and six worker concerns. The M8 spine retires for review-mode; `warden check` is preserved through a thin reuse of Phase 1.

### 1 — Phase structure: 3 phases, not 6

ADR-0029's 6-phase pipeline (Det Priors → Triage Gate → Boss Plan → Worker Fan-Out → Boss Synth → Citation Verify) assumed static dispatch — the boss planned once, workers executed, the boss synthesized once. With a dynamic boss loop (§4), Plan / Adjudicate / Synth collapse into round-labeled tool calls inside a single LLM session; there is no Triage Gate because the harness always runs when invoked (the M8 spine had no skip path either). The shape is:

1. **Det Priors** (`det-priors.ts`) — `Promise.all` over the existing deterministic runners (TSC, user-config ESLint, M13 ESLint security, jscpd, vuln/OSV, scalability detector, consistency detector, deadcode detector, leverage detector) + M5/M6 selector. Output: `DetPriors = { findings: ToolFinding[], retrievedContext, degraded[] }`. Shared verbatim with `warden check`.
2. **Boss Loop** (`boss-loop.ts`) — single `streamText` tool-use session bounded by `stopWhen: stepCountIs(env.WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS ?? 5)`. The boss reads the diff + det priors + retrieved context, dispatches workers via the `dispatch_worker` tool across rounds labeled `phase: 'plan'|'adjudicate'|'synth'`, then emits final `Output.array(CommentSchema)`.
3. **Citation Verify** (`verifyCitations()`) — unchanged M10/M11 post-pass after the Commit-1 generalization (concat-then-substring-match across all source types, not only `api_def`).

Empty-diff is a one-line early-return at harness entry, not a separate phase: zero LLM calls, zero cost, no scratchpad instantiation.

### 2 — Boss model: Opus 4.6, not 4.7

The boss seat upgrades from Sonnet to Opus for multi-file planning and cross-concern adjudication. 4.6 is chosen over 4.7 for the 1M-context window at the lower price point — 4.7's 1.4× premium is rejected at this milestone (the user's "I can do without that"); if dogfood reveals planning regressions, M15+ revisits. Mapping: `getBossModel()` in `@warden/ai/src/models.ts` flips from `claude-sonnet-4-6` to `claude-opus-4-6`; `getApexModel()` stays at Opus 4.7 against the future deep tier. The Anthropic → retry → Google cascade in `@warden/core/src/llm/cascade.ts` (ADR-0017) is reused untouched.

### 3 — Boss loop dynamism: full dynamic, capped at 5 rounds

ADR-0029's static dispatch (boss plans once → fan-out → synth) cannot adjudicate mid-stream: the boss never sees worker output until synth, by which point its planning decisions are locked. The M14 review pattern (user's framing: "the boss will basically be adjudicating what to do next based on their findings") demands dynamism. The chosen shape is full dynamic with a step-count cap:

- The boss runs `streamText` with one tool (`dispatch_worker`) and `stopWhen: stepCountIs(env.WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS ?? 5)`.
- Within each round the boss may dispatch one or more workers; the AI SDK's tool-use loop supports multi-tool-call rounds, and the dispatch function fans those out via `Promise.all`.
- The boss labels each `dispatch_worker` call with `phase: 'plan'|'adjudicate'|'synth'` for render UX. A missing label defaults to `'adjudicate'`.
- The final round emits `Output.array(CommentSchema)` directly; sources are copied verbatim from worker output (the substring-verifier in Phase 3 is the only citation gate).

The 5-round cap is the chosen cost ceiling. At 10 rounds × 5–20 reviews/day, Opus boss runs ~$7.50–40/day; unacceptable for personal v1. At 5 rounds, ~$0.75–1.00 per review; acceptable. `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS = 1` is valid (clamped to [1,10]) — the boss must plan, dispatch, and synth in one call. Useful for cost-conscious users; smoke-asserted.

### 4 — Worker dimension: hybrid `(file, concern-subset)`

Workers are dispatched by both file selection and concern selection in a single subtask. This is neither pure concern fan-out (vision §3's shape — every concern on every file is wasteful for styling-only files) nor pure file fan-out (misses concern-specificity — a non-security file shouldn't burn a security worker). The boss picks `{ files: string[], concerns: Concern[] }` per dispatch:

- Tightly-coupled files (`src/auth/handler.ts` + `src/auth/middleware.ts`) batch in one worker subtask to share context.
- Independent files split across workers to maximize parallelism.
- A file may earn multiple workers across different concerns (`verify-citations.ts` for correctness + consistency).

Boss-side batching prompt instruction lives in `boss-system.md`; v0 ships the instruction, dogfood refines. Excessive batching loses parallelism; insufficient batching inflates shared context tokens.

### 5 — Six worker concerns + default tiers

Workers run as their own `streamText` sessions; each concern has its own system prompt + tier default. Boss can override tier per call (`tier?: 'sonnet'|'haiku'`).

| Concern          | Default tier | Rationale                                                            |
| ---------------- | ------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `correctness`    | Sonnet       | Subtle bugs (null-deref, off-by-one, async race) — vision §3 mandate |
| `scalability`    | Sonnet       | Perf/memory patterns need reasoning across call sites                |
| `consistency`    | Sonnet       | Multi-file reading (docstring vs impl, README vs schema)             |
| `security`       | Sonnet       | Auth / injection / secrets — vision §3 mandate; M13 Haiku promoted   |
| `committability` | Haiku        | Pattern-matching against anti-patterns — M7 baseline                 |
| `leverage`       | Haiku        | Pattern-matching against library idioms — M12 baseline               |

Three prompts are written fresh (correctness, scalability, consistency); three are seeded verbatim from their M13/M7/M12 sources (security, committability, leverage) and adapted to the tool-use envelope. All prompts live as files in `packages/core/src/review-harness/prompts/workers/` per the prompts-as-files invariant (ADR-0015).

### 6 — Worker tools + per-worker step budget

Every worker has the same three tools and the same step cap:

- `lookupTypeDef` — M11 reuse; the M14 workers become its fourth consumer (after M11 formatter and the retiring M12/M13 sub-agents).
- `readFile({ path, startLine?, endLine? })` — repo-scoped (rejects absolute paths and `..` escapes via `resolveWithinRoot`), secret-deny-listed (`.env`, `.env.local`, `*.pem`, `id_rsa`, `*.key`), gitignore-honoring, capped at 1000 lines with an explicit truncation marker so the LLM knows it received a partial read.
- `grepRepo({ pattern, paths? })` — literal-substring v0 (no regex; avoids ReDoS), capped at 200 results, same secret-deny + gitignore discipline; shells out to ripgrep when available, falls back to a Node walker.

Per-worker budget: `stopWhen: stepCountIs(8)`. Two-tier dynamism: 5 boss rounds × W workers per round × 8 tool calls per worker. `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` (optional positive int) caps total dispatched workers per review; on cap, the dispatch tool returns an error to the boss + emits a `degraded: { kind: 'actionable', topic: 'worker-budget' }` entry.

### 7 — Lane discipline + citation discipline

- **Lane discipline.** The dispatch tool drops worker findings whose `path` falls outside the `files` field of that dispatch call. Aggregate count surfaces as one `info` degraded entry per non-zero drop class.
- **Citation discipline.** Workers emit sources internally; the boss copies them verbatim into the final `Output.array(CommentSchema)`. Substring-verifier (Phase 3) catches drift, but the boss is instructed not to invent or paraphrase sources — every Comment's `sources[]` must trace back to a worker that produced it.

### 8 — Full replacement: M8 spine + M7/M12/M13 sub-agents retire for review-mode

The M8 orchestration spine (`packages/core/src/orchestration/{dispatch,synthesizer,scratchpad}.ts`) is built for static fan-out → synth and cannot host a dynamic boss loop. Wrapping the spine inside the harness preserves complexity without payoff; the harness replaces it outright for review-mode. The three M7/M12/M13 LLM sub-agents collapse into harness workers under unified boss planning (single planning brain, not three parallel cheap-tier mini-LLMs):

- `packages/core/src/runners/security.ts` — deleted; prompt content seeds `review-harness/prompts/workers/security-system.md` (promoted Haiku → Sonnet).
- `packages/core/src/runners/leverage-libraries.ts` — deleted; prompt already lives in `packages/core/src/llm/prompts/leverage-system.md` which seeds the worker.
- `packages/core/src/runners/committability.ts` — LLM half deleted; inline prompt content seeds `committability-system.md`. Detector half (Tier-1 hard-skip) already graduated to M9's `BASELINE_NOISE`.

The `Runner` contract in `orchestration/runner.ts` survives — it remains the right shape for future Phase 1 det-priors additions. `warden check` is preserved by routing through `runDetPriors()` + existing `toComment()` mapping; ADR-0011 invariant ("`check` is deterministic-only, never invokes the LLM") intact.

### 9 — Bug floor: three preconditions, in order, before harness code

The verifier, db migrator, and leverage detector are load-bearing for the harness: workers' citations must verify; the cache must boot on a fresh tree; multi-line constructs from the leverage detector must produce surviving Comments. Three bug-floor commits land before any harness code:

1. **`verify-citations.ts` — generalize concat-then-substring-match across all source types.** M10's per-line `includes()` loop (`verify-citations.ts:177-181`) cannot match a snippet whose `normalizeWhitespace` pass collapses across line breaks; M11's `api_def` branch already had this fix; M14 unifies. Single-line snippets are the 1-line degenerate case of multi-line. Drift constants stay split: `LINE_DRIFT = 5` for general sources, `API_DEF_DRIFT = 30` for `api_def`.
2. **`@warden/db` — auto-migrate on `db()`.** Re-verified at read-time: already shipped (lines 30-31 of `packages/db/src/index.ts`); bug-floor reduces to a regression smoke (`smoke-bugfloor-db-automigrate.mts`) asserting fresh `.warden/cache.sqlite` boots without "no such table" and every M6 schema table queries cleanly.
3. **`leverage.ts` — single-line evidence guard.** Re-verified at read-time: detector already emits `undefined` evidence for multi-line constructs (lines 347-354). Bug-floor reduces to a regression smoke (`smoke-bugfloor-leverage-snippet.mts`) asserting a multi-line `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(...))` survives `verifyCitations()` end-to-end.

Each smoke is independently runnable (`pnpm smoke:bugfloor-*`) and chained under `pnpm smoke:bugfloor`. Commit 1's verifier generalization is the load-bearing change; Commits 2 and 3 are belt-and-suspenders smokes confirming existing guards.

### 10 — Zero schema impact

The harness does not extend `CategoryEnum`, `PRIORITY_ORDER`, `SourceTypeEnum`, or any SQLite schema. Every concern is already in the enum (since ADR-0020 / ADR-0027 / ADR-0028); every worker citation flows through existing `tool` / `api_def` `SourceType` variants. No `reviewRuns` / `harnessRuns` / `securityRuns` table in M14 — cost-tracking deferred per the v1 cost-ceiling-is-small judgment; the harness emits a per-model cost line at render time but does not persist. The cost-table generalisation (`harnessRuns` with a `mode` column) ships in M15+ when the deep tier introduces a second consumer.

### 11 — CLI surface: no new verbs, no new flags
