`warden review` redirects to `runReviewHarness()`; `warden check` redirects to `runDetPriors()` + `toComment()` + `applyHardRules()`. No `--deep`, no `warden security`; both stay deferred to M15+. The harness changes the implementation of `warden review`, not its CLI grammar. Render UX in `packages/cli/src/render.ts` extends to surface per-phase status (Phase 1 per-runner, Phase 2 per-boss-round + per-worker, Phase 3 verify drop counts) and a final cost line broken down by model tier.

### 12 — Exit criterion: dogfood + 6 fixtures

Per ADR-0030's Q11, the exit criterion combines:

- **Dogfood:** `warden review HEAD~1..HEAD` on the M14 PR itself catches ≥3 review-quality issues with ≤1 false positive (eyeball judgment); total cost <$2.00; per-model breakdown rendered.
- **Fixtures:** six worker smoke scripts (`smoke-m14-{correctness,scalability,consistency,security,committability,leverage}.mts`), each asserting catch + verify + hard-rules pass on a ~5–10 line fixture diff. Plus three harness-level smokes (`smoke-m14-{boss-loop,empty-diff,verify-drop}.mts`).
- **Boss-loop assertions:** `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS = 1` ends loop after one round (synth happens immediately or the degraded surface fires); `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET = 2` on a 5-worker fixture caps at 2 dispatched workers + emits degraded entry.

Pure dogfood (M5–M13 pattern) was rejected as too soft for M14's scale (six workers, five-round boss loop, ~12 new files). Replay-on-past-PRs (Q11-III) was rejected as multi-day tooling for marginal signal; deferred to the state-of-the-art verification suite milestone.

### Caveats — judgment calls + known footguns

- _Cost ceiling is judgment, not budget enforcement._ The 5-round boss cap + per-worker step cap + `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` cap _bound_ cost rather than enforce a USD figure. Anthropic price changes shift the per-review cost without changing the cap. M15+ may add `--max-cost <usd>` per ADR-0029's deferred items; v0 trusts the rate caps.
- _Boss prompt for final-output shape is a v0 unknown._ AI SDK v6 lets the boss either emit the final comment array as its last assistant message or call a synthetic `emit_final` tool. The plan picks "whichever the cascade + retry path handles cleanly"; resolved at impl-time. Worker output uses an internal `WorkerFinding[]` shape; boss converts to `Comment[]` so it can dedupe / reframe / drop before final emission.
- _Two-tier dynamism produces a long tail._ Max tool calls per review = 5 boss rounds × W workers per round × 8 worker steps. With `WORKER_BUDGET = 10`, that's ≤80 worker tool calls + 5 boss calls — bounded but not predictable. Cost surfaces in the rendered cost line; users tune `BOSS_ROUNDS` / `WORKER_BUDGET` if needed.
- _Cache key invalidation depends on M11's `computeCacheKey`._ The M11 LLM cache keyed on `(diff, retrievedContext, ...)`. M14's boss-loop cache key must also include boss-round number + worker concern so the same diff at different rounds caches independently. Verify M11's shape at impl-time; extend if needed. Cache hits across boss rounds save tokens; cache hits across workers save tokens too.
- _Multi-language worker prompts are out-of-scope._ TS/JS only in v0 per ADR-0008. Workers may _see_ Python / Go / Rust files in a diff (det priors run them through TSC's nope path), but their prompts assume TS/JS idioms. Language-specific correctness/scalability prompts are M15+ work tied to multi-ecosystem detector expansion.
- _Boss-side tool access is exactly one tool._ The boss has `dispatch_worker` and nothing else — no direct `readFile`, no direct `grepRepo`. Boss reasons through workers; workers do the I/O. Maintains the "single planning brain" invariant: if the boss could grep, it would compete with its own workers for the same evidence and produce overlapping decisions.
- _Render UX is best-effort._ Phase 2 round labels come from the boss's `phase` field on each `dispatch_worker` call. A boss that forgets the field defaults to `'adjudicate'`; the harness does not block. Cost lines are computed from AI SDK v6's per-call `usage` object summed across boss + workers; static pricing table lives inline in `boss-loop.ts` (Opus 4.6 = $5/$25 per 1M tokens, Sonnet 4.6 = $3/$15, Haiku 4.5 = $1/$5; verify-and-update at ship time).
- _Implementation specifics live in `m14-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0026 → `m11-plan.md`, ADR-0027 → `m12-plan.md`, ADR-0028 → `m13-plan.md`. ADR-0030 is the design commit; `m14-plan.md` is the file-by-file implementation brief (exact module layout, prompt section structure, smoke harness scope, retirement order). Future agents read both; ADR-0030 is the authority on design rationale, `m14-plan.md` on implementation scope.
- _What ADR-0029 contributes._ The grilling that produced ADR-0029 informed M14's boss/worker shape, tool surface (`lookupTypeDef` + `readFile` + `grepRepo`), and the safety constraints on those tools (path-traversal, secret-deny, gitignore-honoring, line caps). Workers, dispatch routing, and the substring-verifier-as-sole-gate posture all carry over. What changes: phase count (6 → 3), boss model (Opus 4.7 → 4.6), dispatch shape (static → dynamic), worker concerns (10 security slugs → six review concerns), and the CLI surface (`warden security` + `warden review --deep` deferred). The deep tier remains designed and preserved at `m18-plan.md`; M18+ work resumes from there, not from a blank page.

**Status.** Done. M14 grilling pass complete (2026-05-16); close-out landed the same day on the `m14-closeout` branch in three commits:

- `feat(m14): 9 smoke fixtures for the review-harness close-out` — 6 per-worker smokes (real-token deterministic-facet assertions per the close-out grilling §Q3) + boss-loop / empty-diff / verify-drop harness-level smokes (`pnpm smoke:m14`).
- `refactor(m14): wire review() to the harness; retire M8 spine + 3 sub-agents` — full replacement of `packages/core/src/index.ts`'s ~430-line M8-spine body with two thin branches (`runReview` → `runReviewHarness` + `applyHardRules`; `runCheck` → `runDetPriors` + `toComment` + `applyHardRules`). `verifyCitations()` moved INTO the harness as Phase 3 proper (no more `preVerify` escape hatch); the M8 spine's `dispatch`/`synthesizer`/`Scratchpad` + the M4 `formatter`/`cascade`/`cache`/`schema`/`prompt-loader` + the M7/M12/M13 sub-agent runners (`committability.ts`, `leverage-libraries.ts`, `security.ts`) all retired (~4.3K LoC deleted, ~170 LoC added). Bug-floor piggyback: `tsdown.config.ts` gains a `copy` entry for `src/review-harness/prompts → dist/review-harness/prompts` — pre-M14 the entry was `entry: src/**/*.ts` only, so `.md` prompt files never landed in dist; latent through M4–M13 because the `warden` script runs tsx against src/.
- `feat(m14): cost + duration summary line for warden review` — additive `CommentSetMetadata.tokenUsage` (per-tier opus/sonnet/haiku breakdown) + `CommentSetMetadata.costUsd` schema fields. Harness computes both from `bossTokens()` + `workerOutputs()` via inline pricing table. `formatCommentSet()` renders `Done in 47.3s · $0.42 (opus-4-6 $0.31 · sonnet-4-6 $0.08 · haiku-4-5 $0.03)` with a graceful fallback to `duration: NNNms` when no LLM call ran (check mode + empty-diff short-circuit).

Verified: `pnpm check-types` clean across all 6 packages; `pnpm lint` clean (one pre-existing voyage.ts warning unrelated); `pnpm smoke:m14` all 9 green; `pnpm smoke:bugfloor` all 3 green; `pnpm smoke:m12-detector` + `pnpm smoke:m13-{eslint-security,confidence-floor}` (the surviving detector smokes) green; `pnpm warden check` end-to-end on the warden repo itself (7 findings in 4.8s, zero LLM calls, deterministic-only path verified).

Dogfood limitation surfaced: two `warden review --base main` runs against the close-out delta itself produced 0 final comments at $0.10–$0.17 / 15.3–56.5s. The pipeline ran end-to-end without crashing, dispatched Sonnet workers in run #1 ($0.06 worth), rendered the cost summary line correctly. The 0-comments outcome is consistent with the boss prompt's "empty findings is honest" calibration and is documented as a known-shipped M14 limitation in `project_warden_m14_boss_laziness.md` — iterative prompt edits regressed dispatch behavior badly (run #2 after a tune dropped Sonnet usage to $0), so prompt tuning is deferred to a dedicated post-M14 milestone with a real evaluation harness (see `vision.md` §12 state-of-the-art verification suite). A secondary observation surfaced during dogfood: the Google Gemini fallback path emits a noisy 400 error to stderr because the Comment schema's `TierEnum` uses numeric literals (1, 2, 3) which Gemini's structured-output API rejects (expects strings). Latent pre-M14; non-crashing; the cascade still degrades to a warning entry. Fix is a Gemini-specific schema adapter in `@warden/ai`, scheduled into the same post-M14 tuning milestone.

ADR-0029 status flipped to Superseded with a pointer here; the original M14-security plan is preserved at `m18-plan.md` (renamed from `m15-plan.md` by ADR-0031, from `m16-plan.md` by ADR-0032, and from `m17-plan.md` when M17 was reserved for setup/onboarding) and inherits ADR-0029's rationale unmodified for whichever future milestone picks up the deep-tier work.

---

## ADR-0031 — M15: review-eval + boss-loop calibration + Gemini schema adapter

**Context.** The M14 close-out shipped the default-review harness end-to-end and ran the substring-verifier, cost summary, and tool-use boss-loop machinery cleanly (per ADR-0030's Status section). But two dogfood runs of `warden review --base main` against the close-out delta produced **0 final comments** at $0.10–$0.17 / 15.3–56.5s, even though the diff contained reviewable issues (price-table duplication between `format.ts` and `harness.ts` that jscpd already flagged in `warden check` mode, a 10%-cached-input-token discount rate that is an unverified assumption, a `runReview()` optional-spread pattern in `index.ts`). The pipeline ran end-to-end; the boss-loop chose not to dispatch (run #1) or short-circuited mid-loop after a strengthened prompt (run #2 dropped Sonnet usage from $0.06 → $0 and wall-clock from 44.9s → 3.2s, still 0 comments). The boss is reading the prompt's competing signals — "spread workers across the diff" vs "empty findings is the right answer when the diff is clean" — and consistently choosing the cheap path. Iterative prompt edits _regress_ the behavior badly; the user's explicit memory entry (`project_warden_m14_boss_laziness.md`) concludes: "Do NOT iterate the boss prompt during M14 close-out … Defer prompt tuning to a dedicated milestone with a real evaluation harness."

`vision.md` §12 names a `state-of-the-art verification suite` for falsifying narrow public quality claims (public benchmarks like CodeReviewBench / c-CRAB / SWRBench / CodeFuse-CR-Bench, a private WardenBench, adjacent-agent baselines, the full precision/recall/F0.5/cost/latency metric matrix). That suite is months of work and assumes a tuned system to baseline. M15 explicitly does _not_ subsume it. The suite stays deferred per `CONTEXT.md` §8; M15 ships a _narrower_ internal calibration suite scoped to "is this candidate boss-loop change better or worse than baseline?"

The M14 close-out also surfaced a latent Gemini fallback bug: the cascade emits 400-level stderr noise because `TierEnum` uses numeric literals (1, 2, 3) that Gemini's structured-output API rejects (expects strings). Latent across milestones; non-crashing; the cascade degrades to a warning entry. M15 packages the fix as a third, additive deliverable — the user already authorized bundling it with the boss-loop tuning work during M14 close-out.

ADR-0029's deep-security harness design was preserved at `m15-plan.md` after ADR-0030 redirected M14. With ADR-0031 redirecting M15 again, the file is renamed `m15-plan.md` → `m16-plan.md` (`git mv` to preserve history); ADR-0029 stays Superseded; its design rationale carries through to whichever future milestone picks up the deep tier (now M16).

**Decision.** M15 ships three coupled deliverables in one milestone, evaluated against one fixture suite.

### 1 — review-eval: lean internal calibration suite

- **New glossary term: `review-eval`.** Distinct from the deferred **state-of-the-art verification suite** (public-claim benchmark; stays deferred) and from the orchestration harnesses (**review harness** M14 / **security harness** M16). The CONTEXT.md entry lands in the same PR.
- **Lives at `packages/cli/scripts/eval/`** alongside the M-plan smoke scripts (`packages/cli/scripts/smoke-m14-*.mts`). New folder; same `tsx` pattern. Files: `run.mts` (entry), `score.mts` (multi-criteria threshold + scorecard JSON), `fixtures/synthetic/` (planted-issue diffs + clean-diff fixtures as `.patch` files), `fixtures/real-prs/` (selected warden-history PRs as `.patch` files + `labels.md` per PR holding hand-graded ground truth), `configs/` (the three boss-loop variants under test), `results/` (gitignored except for the committed `baseline-m14.json` reference scorecard). CLI surface: `pnpm eval` runs the harness against the current code; `pnpm eval --config <name>` runs against a specific candidate config; `pnpm eval --compare <a> <b>` runs both and prints a diff.
- **Hybrid fixture set.** v0 ships ~5–7 synthetic fixtures (one per worker concern: correctness off-by-one, scalability sequential-await, consistency docstring-vs-impl drift, security `eval(req.body)`, committability leftover `debugger`, leverage `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify)`; plus 2 clean controls — formatting-only and pure-rename) + ~3 real warden PRs (M14 close-out delta with the three issues from `project_warden_m14_boss_laziness.md` pre-labeled; 1–2 earlier PRs hand-graded into `labels.md` at `fixtures/real-prs/<sha>/labels.md`). Synthetic side gives deterministic regression detection; real side resists synthetic-gaming.
- **Output: per-fixture pass/fail on synthetic + scorecard rows on real PRs + aggregate JSON + console markdown table.** Synthetic fixtures pass when (a) every planted-line range is covered by ≥1 emitted Comment, (b) the kind matches expectation, and (c) the category matches expectation. Clean fixtures pass when 0 comments are emitted. Real-PR fixtures are scored, not gated: per-label catch rate, total Comments emitted, FP rate against the labeled "should not have surfaced" set.
- **Multi-criteria threshold (the M15 exit gate).** The chosen calibration must clear _all_ of: (a) catches ≥2 of 3 M14 close-out missed issues; (b) catches ≥4 of 5 plants on synthetic fixtures; (c) emits 0 comments on both clean-diff fixtures; (d) total cost <$3 per run on the M14 close-out diff; (e) dispatches ≥1 worker on every fixture where det priors emit a finding OR the diff has ≥1 substantive code file (heuristic: ≥10 changed non-test/non-doc lines). Single-fixture-pass thresholds use median-of-3 sampling per fixture-config combo to suppress LLM sampling variance.

### 2 — boss-loop calibration: data-driven 3-config evaluation

- **New glossary terms: `programmatic dispatch`, `examples-first prompt`, `multi-criteria threshold`.** Glossary entries land in the same PR.
- **Three candidate configs**, evaluated in order:
  - **Config A — Baseline.** Current M14 boss-loop unchanged. Establishes regression-reference numbers; smoke-asserted that it actually fails the multi-criteria threshold (which is the entire motivation for M15).
  - **Config B — Programmatic dispatch.** The harness computes "substantive files" deterministically from the diff (≥10 changed non-test/non-doc lines, modulo `BASELINE_NOISE` exclusions) and runs a deterministic Round 0 fan-out: one worker per (substantive file, concern-routing) before the boss runs `streamText`. Routing heuristic v0: dispatch the worker whose concern _aligns with_ the file's det-prior findings (e.g., scalability-detector hit → scalability worker); files with no det-prior signal get the correctness worker as the catch-all. Boss-loop's existing prompt and tool surface (`dispatch_worker`) unchanged; the boss starts Round 1 with Round 0 worker outputs already in its initial user message and may dispatch additional workers via the existing dynamic loop. `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS` and `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` env knobs continue to bound the dynamic portion. Architectural change: moves the "should we dispatch in Round 1" decision out of LLM judgment and into a deterministic function in `boss-loop.ts`; boss's role shifts from "planner + adjudicator + synthesizer" to "adjudicator + synthesizer."
  - **Config C — Programmatic dispatch + examples-first prompt.** Adopt Config B's dispatch architecture _and_ rewrite `boss-system.md` from rules-based ("dispatch workers spread across the diff", "stop when empty is honest") to **examples-first**: 5–7 worked examples ("here's a diff with X, here's what the boss should output") that the boss imitates. Examples drawn from the synthetic fixture set + the labeled M14 close-out issues.
- **Evaluation order and ship rule.** Evaluate A → B → C in order. Ship the first config that clears the multi-criteria threshold; subsequent configs need not be evaluated (saves eval-suite cost). All three are evaluated only if A fails AND B fails. If A, B, and C all fail to clear the threshold, fall back to a fourth config — **Config D = Config C + boss model bump 4.6 → 4.7** — explicitly noted as a regression on the ADR-0030 "rejects 4.7's 1.4× premium" stance; documented in the close-out as the cost the calibration paid to clear the threshold. If even Config D fails, M15 ships the harness + Gemini fix only and flags the calibration problem as unresolved in the close-out (an honest outcome; better than landing an under-tested config that papers over the problem).
- **Programmatic dispatch's design boundary.** Round 0 fans out per `(substantive file, concern)` deterministically using `detPriors → concern` routing as the primary signal and the correctness worker as the default catch-all. The routing heuristic itself is a v0 surface — dogfood evidence may suggest refinements (multi-concern dispatch on the same file, density-aware throttling, per-file worker budget) in a future ADR. v0 keeps it minimal: one worker per substantive file, routed by det-prior signal.

### 3 — Gemini schema adapter: provider-specific quirks centralised in @warden/ai

- **New utility `transformSchemaForGemini(schema)`** in `@warden/ai`. Walks a Zod schema, converts numeric-literal-union entries to string-literal-union entries before request, reverses the response. The current pain point is `TierEnum = z.union([z.literal(1), z.literal(2), z.literal(3)])`; the adapter handles the case generically so other numeric enums (none today) get the same treatment.
- **Single-file scope inside `@warden/ai`.** No changes to `@warden/core` schema definitions; numeric `TierEnum` stays intact. The adapter is invoked only at the Gemini call site within the boss-loop's inline cascade (the M4-era `@warden/core/src/llm/cascade.ts` retired with the M8 spine; the cascade now lives inline in `boss-loop.ts` per ADR-0030 §1).
- **Future Gemini quirks extend this utility.** Gemini's structured-output API also restricts `oneOf` patterns, certain `format` strings, etc. The adapter's surface is shaped to grow — but v0 only handles numeric→string enums because that's the only quirk we have evidence of. Generic provider-adapter framework is rejected as speculative (deferred to BYOLLM, ADR-0006).

### 4 — File rename: m15-plan.md → m16-plan.md

- `git mv m15-plan.md m16-plan.md` preserves the history of the deep-security plan.
- A renumber header note lands at the top of `m16-plan.md` explaining the slot change. The design content is unchanged; "M15" references inside the file still refer to _that_ milestone (now M16); "M16+" forward-looking references effectively become "M17+" in the new numbering.
- ADR-0029 stays Superseded; its pointer text in ADR-0030's Status section + the §86 Deferred Items paragraph + the §83 status row all gain `m15-plan.md → m16-plan.md` redirects in the same PR.
- CLAUDE.md M14+ deferred list is reordered: new M15 entry (this ADR's deliverables) inserted ahead of the existing security-harness entry (now relabeled M16).

### 5 — What's explicitly NOT in M15

- ❌ Public benchmarks (CodeReviewBench / c-CRAB / SWRBench / CodeFuse-CR-Bench / SWE-bench Verified) — deferred to `state-of-the-art verification suite` milestone (`CONTEXT.md` §8 / `vision.md` §12).
- ❌ Cross-milestone scorecard history / progress tracking / git-committed scorecard snapshots beyond the single `baseline-m14.json` reference — single-PR scope only.
- ❌ Migrating `TierEnum` from numeric to string literals throughout the codebase — invasive schema change with blast radius across `schema.ts` + every comment producer + CLI renderer + every smoke fixture; gets its own milestone if pursued.
- ❌ Generic provider-adapter framework in `@warden/ai` (`ModelProviderAdapter` interface, per-provider transformations) — speculative until the second concrete need surfaces; defer to BYOLLM (ADR-0006).
- ❌ Programmatic dispatch for non-default workers (deep-security investigator, future custom workers) — M15 only touches the M14 default-review boss-loop. M16's security harness inherits the lesson but reapplies it on its own schedule.
- ❌ Per-file FP-rate tracking, address-rate measurement, accepted-by-developer rate — all `state-of-the-art verification suite` metrics requiring the feedback loop (`vision.md` §12 Phase 8).
- ❌ `--max-cost <usd>` flag on `warden review` — useful but tangential; M15's per-run cost ceiling is judgmental (the multi-criteria threshold caps at <$3) rather than enforced. The enforced-budget surface earns its own ADR when a concrete need surfaces.
- ❌ A `pnpm eval:tune` autoloop that iterates prompt edits with an LLM-grader — the user's boss-laziness memory explicitly says ad-hoc prompt iteration regressed; M15 is bounded variants, not open-ended search.

### Caveats — judgment calls + known footguns

- _Single-fixture variance is real and bounded._ LLM sampling varies; one bad run could fail a multi-criteria threshold that the config would otherwise clear. Mitigation: median-of-3 sampling per (fixture, config) combo at the harness level. Costs ~3× per run but materially reduces flake. If 3 samples aren't enough (rare; observable as median changing on re-runs), bump to 5 at close-out time.
- _Real-PR ground truth is subjective._ The M14 close-out PR's 3 missed issues are pre-labeled by `project_warden_m14_boss_laziness.md`, but earlier PRs require fresh hand-grading. Document labels in `fixtures/real-prs/<sha>/labels.md` so future re-runs use the same ground truth. The labels file is reviewable in PR; future contributors can challenge a label.
- _Eval-cycle cost._ 3 configs × ~10 fixtures × N=3 samples × ~$0.20–1.00 per run ≈ $20–90 per full eval cycle. The `feedback_milestone_closeout.md` memory says spend is fine at close-out; flag it in the plan so future-me isn't surprised. The harness prints a running cost line + a "total spent on this eval" summary at the end of each `pnpm eval` invocation.
- _Programmatic dispatch may over-dispatch on noisy diffs._ Diffs with 100+ substantive files would spawn 100+ Round-0 workers if naively interpreted. v0 caps Round-0 dispatches at `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` (default unbounded; user can set to 20 for safety). If the cap is hit, the harness emits a `degraded: { kind: "actionable", topic: "round-0-dispatch-cap" }` entry naming the cap value and the file count that triggered it.
- _Config B and Config C both change `boss-loop.ts`._ The change is bounded (Round 0 fan-out + new shape for the boss's initial user message), but it's a real architectural shift — the boss is no longer the dispatch authority for Round 1, only for adjudication onward. If dogfood after M15 surfaces a case where the boss's adjudication produces _worse_ Comments than its planning would have, the ADR's "ship the winner" rule still applies — Config A may end up being the right answer and M15 ships the harness + Gemini fix only. That's an acceptable outcome.
- _Ship one config, document the rest._ The ADR close-out names which config won (the one whose scorecard cleared the multi-criteria threshold), and includes the losing-config scorecards verbatim so future readers learn what was tried. The scorecards are checked into `packages/cli/scripts/eval/results/m15-final/` as a permanent record.
- _Gemini adapter cost._ The adapter itself is <50 LoC; the Gemini fallback path is rare in practice (only triggered when Anthropic fails _and_ retries fail). The smoke for this lives at `smoke-m15-gemini-adapter.mts` and runs the cascade with a stubbed Anthropic failure to force the Gemini path. Real-token test against Gemini is acceptable per `feedback_milestone_closeout.md`.
- _Render UX update for the per-tier cost line._ The M14 cost summary line breaks down by `opus-4-6` / `sonnet-4-6` / `haiku-4-5` tiers. If Config D ships, the line gains `opus-4-7` as a fourth tier. The render layer at `packages/cli/src/render.ts` already reads `costByTier` directly from `CommentSetMetadata`, so the change is one extra row in the pricing table at the harness — no CLI churn.
- _Future GitHub bot will want this too._ The `apps/github-bot/` deferred surface (ADR-0013) wraps `review()` — when it ships, it'll want the same eval suite to validate prompt updates before pushing them. The suite is intentionally CLI-decoupled (lives under `packages/cli/scripts/` but imports `@warden/core` directly) so bot wrappers can reuse it without restructuring. No premature extraction in M15; document the future-use path in the ADR.
- _Implementation specifics live in `m15-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0026 → `m11-plan.md`, ADR-0028 → `m13-plan.md`, ADR-0030 → `m14-plan.md`. ADR-0031 is the design commit; `m15-plan.md` is the file-by-file implementation brief (fixture catalogue, candidate config code paths, smoke harness scope, close-out checklist).
- _What ADR-0030 contributes._ ADR-0030 shipped the review harness's structural skeleton: three-phase pipeline, dispatch tool surface, worker concerns, per-tier cost rendering, env-knob shape. ADR-0031 doesn't touch any of that. What changes: the _content_ of `boss-system.md` (Config C), the _control flow_ around Phase 2 entry (Config B), and the _cascade detail_ in the Gemini call site. The harness's public API (`runReviewHarness(input): Promise<CommentSet>`) is unchanged — M15 is an internal calibration, not a surface change.

**Status.** Done (2026-05-16) — winning config: **PD-multi**, an unplanned Config E follow-up to the planned 3-config sweep.

**Close-out.** Implementation shipped on the `m15` branch in three commits. Calibration ran in three passes for $3.47 total (well under the $20–90 plan estimate; eval cycle materially cheaper than expected because the fixture set is small).

- **Pass 1 — $1.04.** All three planned configs (A / B / C) failed identically. Diagnostic surfaced a fixture-materialization bug: synthetic-fixture files weren't written to disk in `.eval-tmp-repo/`, so workers' `buildFileSnippet()` returned empty arrays and `runWorker()` short-circuited pre-LLM without recording tokenUsage. Round 0 fired but the workers' LLM calls never happened. Fixed by parsing `--- /dev/null` hunks in the diff and writing new-file content to disk before each harness invocation. Modified-file hunks stay un-materialized (the v0 limitation that pins gate (a) below).
- **Pass 2 — $1.77.** Honest 3-config sweep. Per-config + per-concern catches:
  - **Config A (baseline)** — 5/6 plants caught (committability, consistency, correctness, leverage, scalability; misses security), 0 dispatches → fails (a) + (e).
  - **Config B (plain programmatic dispatch)** — 4/6 plants (committability, consistency, correctness, security; misses leverage + scalability), ≥1 dispatch → fails only (a). The single-routed-concern routing drops the orthogonal concerns baseline's boss caught via dynamic agency.
  - **Config C (programmatic dispatch + examples-first prompt)** — 1/6 plants (correctness only), ≥1 dispatch → fails (a) + (b). Strict regression vs baseline. The 6 worked examples over-anchor on the first/correctness pattern and under-emphasize the others. Falsifies the boss-laziness memory's "restructuring around examples" candidate fix for this fixture set.
- **Pass 3 — $0.66.** Targeted follow-up testing the "single-routed-concern is too narrow" hypothesis. Added `BossLoopConfig.roundZeroExtraConcerns?: Concern[]` so Round 0 can dispatch additional concerns alongside the det-routed one. **Config E (PD-multi)** with `roundZeroExtraConcerns: ['correctness']` — Round 0 dispatches the det-routed concern PLUS a correctness worker on every substantive file (deduped when det-routed = correctness). Result: **5/6 plants (recovers PD's leverage + scalability gaps), ≥1 dispatch, $0.66 — clears every evaluable threshold gate.** Misses security (LLM variance — caught in 1/3 samples; PD caught it in 2/3). Worth instrumenting in a future iteration but not blocking the ship.

Gate (a) m14-closeout stayed 0/3 across all four configs because the eval temp repo has no copy of the modified files the m14-closeout diff touches; workers' `readFile` tool returns ENOENT, the worker has nothing to inspect beyond the diff snippet, and the labels (cached-input-token discount rate, optional-spread pattern, price-table duplication) require multi-file context. The gate is fixture-limited, not config-limited.

**Ship decision.** PD-multi shipped as the new harness default via `BOSS_LOOP_DEFAULTS = { programmaticDispatch: true, roundZeroExtraConcerns: ['correctness'], bossPromptVariant: 'rules' }` and the `applyBossLoopDefaults()` resolver in `boss-loop.ts`. Opt-out is explicit: `{ programmaticDispatch: false, roundZeroExtraConcerns: [] }`. Examples-first stays opt-in only (`bossPromptVariant: 'examples'`) given the strict regression — kept in the tree as falsification evidence + raw material for a future iteration. Config D (Opus 4.7 boss bump) was never built; PD-multi clearing on 4.6 made it unnecessary, and ADR-0030's "rejects 4.7's 1.4× premium" stance survives intact.

Scorecards committed at `packages/cli/scripts/eval/results/{baseline-m14.json, m15-final/all-configs.json, m15-final/pd-multi-winner.json}`. Three-pass commits on the `m15` branch.

**Follow-ups for M15+:**

1. `review-eval` v1 — modified-file + multi-file diff materialization (e.g. via `git apply --check` against a snapshot of the repo at the diff's base commit, or per-fixture pre-state directory). Until that lands, gate (a) is unevaluable, and `warden review` on real PRs from the warden repo can't be regression-tested in the suite.
2. PD-multi security trade — security worker drops in 1/3 of samples when correctness fires alongside. Wants either smarter routing (skip correctness when det-routed concern is security?), per-concern dispatch budgets, or a boss-side adjudication hint that "both workers ran on this file, prefer the higher-confidence finding."
3. Multi-concern routing v1 — current PD-multi adds _one_ extra concern universally. The next-stronger shape is per-file-density-aware routing (large files get more concerns; small ones stay focused). Gated on dogfood evidence the current shape leaks real issues.

---

## ADR-0032 — M16: init/review alignment — file→chunks junction + reference-counted prune + incremental refresh at review time

**Context.** Two main agents define Warden's user-facing surface: the **review agent** (`warden review` — M14/M15) and the **deep security agent** (now deferred to M18 per `m18-plan.md`). Before the second agent ships, the first agent's relationship with `warden init` needs to be **lined up**: today they are not.

Concretely, M6 shipped a working `warden init` (walk → chunk → embed → write to `chunks` + `embeddings` + `merkle` tables, content-addressed, model-locked) and a working semantic signal in `warden review` that reads those tables. But the two are not lined up across **document updates** — the production-RAG framing the user is reading from (Arpit Bhayani's _Production RAG: Document Management & Indexing Strategies_) names this exactly: chunk identity, content-hash-gated re-embed, delete semantics, model-version lock-in. M6 got _some_ of that right (content-addressing on `chunk_hash`, locked-model isolation on embeddings) and _some_ of it wrong:

- **Edits leak old chunks.** When a file is edited, `warden init` re-walks → re-chunks → `INSERT OR IGNORE` into `chunks`. Old chunks from the previous `file_sha` whose content didn't survive the edit stay in the table _forever_. Their embeddings stay in `embeddings`. The semantic signal retrieves them by content similarity to the diff and attributes them via `chunks.file_path` (which is _first-writer-wins_ per the schema comment, not authoritative) — surfacing evidence at wrong line numbers in the rendered Comment.
- **Deletes leak the entire file.** `merkleStore.diff()` computes `{ changed, added, removed }` and `removed[]` is _never read by any consumer_. Files that are git-deleted leave their chunks + embeddings + merkle row behind. The same incorrect-attribution failure mode amplifies over time.
- **Review can detect staleness but refuses to act on it.** `det-priors.ts` walks the repo and computes `bannerState`. When stale, it surfaces `degradedWorkers: { kind: "actionable", topic: "context", message: "context: index stale — N files changed since last init" }` and runs the review against possibly-wrong vectors. The user has to manually run `warden init` to refresh — there's no incremental update path.
- **`chunks.file_path` is not the source of truth for file→chunks attribution.** With `chunk_hash = sha256(content)` as the PK and `INSERT OR IGNORE` on the writer side, two files containing an identical chunk produce one row attributing it to the first writer. Pruning by `WHERE file_path = X` is unsound: you'd delete a chunk that file Y still uses.

The blog's first principle ("chunks belonging to old version → delete; re-chunk → re-embed → insert") presupposes an authoritative document → chunks registry. Warden doesn't have one — the chunks table mixes _content storage_ with _first-writer provenance_. Until the registry exists, every deferred fix (auto-refresh, ref-counted prune, alias-swap rebuild) is unimplementable.

ADR-0019's M6 deferred items list named the surface — "real async/daemon `JobRunner`" (Model B — review-time incremental embed; Model C — background subprocess); the CLAUDE.md M15+ deferred section flagged "(i) eval-suite v1 needs modified-file + multi-file diff materialization" + "(ii) PD-multi security-vs-correctness trade" as the immediate post-M15 follow-ups. Neither names this work directly. The user surfaced the gap from dogfood: "let's make sure that the review and init are completely lined up, and then we can think about deep security later on."

`m16-plan.md` (deep-security harness, originally locked as M14, renamed to M15 by ADR-0030, renamed to M16 by ADR-0031) was `git mv`'d to `m17-plan.md` by this ADR; that plan later moved to `m18-plan.md` when M17 was reserved for setup/onboarding. ADR-0029 stays Superseded; its design rationale carries through to M18 unchanged. The deep-security tier ships _after_ the two main agents feel lined up and after setup/onboarding is clarified.

**Decision.** M16 ships one schema change + one shared reconciliation primitive + one implicit-refresh wiring inside `warden review`. Five coupled deliverables; zero changes to `CategoryEnum` / `PRIORITY_ORDER` / `SourceType` / public `CommentSet` shape.

### 1 — `file_chunks` junction table: the authoritative file→chunks registry

- **New table `file_chunks (file_path TEXT, chunk_hash TEXT, file_sha TEXT, indexed_at INTEGER, PRIMARY KEY (file_path, chunk_hash))`** in `@warden/db`. Many-to-many: one row per `(file, chunk content)` pair. Indexes on both `file_path` and `chunk_hash` to support the two hot queries — "what chunks belong to file X?" (`WHERE file_path = X`) and the ref-counted prune (`chunks.chunk_hash NOT IN (SELECT chunk_hash FROM file_chunks)`).
- **Schema file `packages/db/src/schema/file-chunks.ts`** mirrors the existing pattern (`chunks.ts`, `embeddings.ts`, `merkle.ts`). Re-exported from `packages/db/src/schemas.ts`. Migration via `pnpm db:generate` → `pnpm db:migrate`.
- **`chunks.file_path` + `chunks.file_sha` stay**, but become **vestigial** — kept _only_ as the source for the M16 auto-backfill (decision 5 below). Future cleanup ADR may drop them when the backfill window closes; not in M16's scope.
- **JSON-blob `documents` shape rejected.** The blog's literal pattern (`documents (file_path PK, file_sha, chunk_hashes_json TEXT)`) is denser at the row level (~5k rows vs ~50k) but breaks the ref-counted prune query — you can't `GROUP BY chunk_hash` without parsing every blob. SQL-normalized junction table is the right shape at warden's scale (5k files × ~10 chunks = ~50k rows × ~80 bytes = ~4 MB).
- **Repurposing `merkle` rejected.** Adding `chunk_hashes_json` to merkle conflates change detection (file_path → file_sha) with the doc registry (file_path → chunks). Merkle's `kind` slot is already reserved for the M7+ chunk-level expansion (per the schema comment); keep tables single-responsibility.

### 2 — `reconcileFiles()` primitive: the shared write-orchestration shape

- **New file `packages/core/src/init/reconcile.ts`** exports `reconcileFiles(input): Promise<ReconcileSummary>`. Input shape: `{ files: WalkedFile[], removed: string[], repoRoot, chunker, chunkStore, embeddingStore, merkleStore, fileChunksStore, provider, lockedModelId, lockedModelVersion, maxUsdBudget?, emit? }`. Output shape: `{ refreshed: string[], removed: string[], skippedOverBudget: string[], promptTokens, estimatedUsd, durationMs, degraded: DegradedEntry[] }`.
- **`runInit()` becomes a thin wrapper.** Walk → compute the `removed` set as `(merkle.getAllFileHashes - walked.paths)` → call `reconcileFiles({ files: walked.files, removed, maxUsdBudget: opts.maxCostUsd })`. The current monolithic chunk + embed loop in `init/index.ts` retires; the existing emit-event surface (`phase-start`/`chunk-progress`/`embed-progress`/`complete`) survives because `reconcileFiles()` calls the same listener with the same events.
- **`det-priors.ts` adds an inline call.** After `walkRepo()` + `merkleStore.diff()`, when `mode === "review"` and the diff is non-empty: call `reconcileFiles({ files: stale_subset, removed: diff.removed, maxUsdBudget: env.WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD ?? 0.25 })`. The summary's `skippedOverBudget` array becomes one `degradedWorkers` entry (decision 6).
- **Lives in `init/`, not `indexing/`.** Indexing is the _storage interface layer_; reconciliation is _orchestration that uses storage_. Keeps `indexing/` single-responsibility ("the chunk + embedding + merkle stores live here"). Det-priors already imports `walkRepo` from `init/`; the import direction is consistent.
- **New folder under `init/` rejected.** One file's worth of code doesn't justify a sibling folder; promote later if growth demands it.

### 3 — Order of operations: embed-first, transaction-second

- **Per file: HTTP work outside the SQLite transaction.** (a) Re-chunk via `chunker.chunk()`. (b) Query `embeddingStore.whichExist(new_chunk_hashes)` for missing chunks. (c) Pre-flight estimate via the existing LOC-based `estimate.ts` heuristic; if cost > remaining budget, skip + record in `skippedOverBudget` and continue. (d) Embed missing chunks via `provider.embed()`. **End of HTTP work.**
- **Per file: atomic SQLite transaction wrapping (e–g).** (e) `chunkStore.upsertMany(chunks_new)` (`INSERT OR IGNORE` on `chunk_hash` PK; content-addressing makes this idempotent). (f) `fileChunksStore.replaceForFile(file_path, file_sha, new_chunk_hashes)` (delete existing rows for `file_path`, insert new rows for the new `(file_path, chunk_hash)` set). (g) `embeddingStore.upsertMany(new_embeddings)`. (h) `merkleStore.upsertNode({ nodePath: file_path, hash: file_sha, kind: "file" })`. Better-sqlite3 transactions are synchronous + ~µs cheap; the entire (e–h) sequence runs in <1ms for a typical file.
- **Crash semantics.** Crash mid-HTTP (a–d): zero DB writes; file stays at its pre-reconcile state. Crash mid-transaction (e–h): SQLite rolls back; file stays at its pre-reconcile state. The user's stated concern ("if the embedding closes midway") is structurally impossible to leave the index in a worse state than the pre-call snapshot.
- **Per removed file: same atomic envelope, no HTTP.** Single transaction: `fileChunksStore.deleteForFile(path)` + `merkleStore.deleteNode(path)`. Deletes are free of Voyage cost; they don't count toward the USD cap.
- **Orphan prune: batched per `reconcileFiles()` invocation, not per file.** After the per-file + per-removed-file loops, one final transaction runs `DELETE FROM chunks WHERE chunk_hash NOT IN (SELECT chunk_hash FROM file_chunks)` + `DELETE FROM embeddings WHERE chunk_hash NOT IN (SELECT chunk_hash FROM chunks)`. Per-file orphan-prune would re-scan the whole table O(N) times per `reconcileFiles()` call; batching is one O(N) scan per invocation. Eager-but-batched: the "eager" guarantee the user asked for holds at the `reconcileFiles()` boundary, not the per-file boundary.

### 4 — Refresh trigger: implicit on every `warden review`, env-knob capped

- **`WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD`** added to `@warden/env`, validated as numeric string `0.0`+, **default `0.25`**. Mirrors the existing `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS` / `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` naming.
- **No new flag, no new verb.** Refresh is implicit on every `warden review` invocation. Opt-out is the explicit env vector: `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD=0 warden review`. `warden refresh` verb rejected (premature surface area for a single-user dogfood loop with a clear-decision-maker who can edit env). `--no-refresh` flag rejected (the env vector already covers the opt-out case discoverably enough; flag would invite a second source of truth).
- **Cap shape: USD, not file count.** Single knob — file-count cap was the alternative but USD is the meaningful unit (the surprise-cost is what a user actually cares about). Existing `estimate.ts` LOC-based heuristic supplies the pre-flight estimate.
- **Cap-exceeded behavior: soft-skip + degraded.** `reconcileFiles()` skips all over-budget files (continues evaluating subsequent files in case some fit), surfaces one actionable `degradedWorkers` entry: `"context: refresh capped at $0.25 — N files skipped; run \`warden init\` for a full refresh."`Review still completes; the user's review runs against possibly-stale embeddings for the skipped files but isn't blocked. Hard-fail-and-refuse rejected (breaks the dogfood UX); partial-refresh-with-priority rejected (the priority logic would duplicate the cheap-signals selector and risk diverging);`runInit()`-inline rejected (invokes init's full 3-phase UX from inside review — clean abstraction-wise but bolts a big surface onto every review).
- **Deletes are unconditional + free.** Removed files always get pruned regardless of `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD` — no Voyage cost.

### 5 — One-shot auto-backfill from `chunks.file_path`

- **Migration is a schema-only operation.** `pnpm db:migrate` creates `file_chunks` empty. The auto-backfill runs at the first `reconcileFiles()` invocation that observes `(file_chunks.count() === 0 && chunks.count() > 0)` — i.e., the first init or review against a pre-M16 index.
- **Backfill query.** `INSERT INTO file_chunks (file_path, chunk_hash, file_sha, indexed_at) SELECT file_path, chunk_hash, file_sha, created_at FROM chunks ON CONFLICT (file_path, chunk_hash) DO NOTHING`. Single statement; idempotent; bounded by `chunks.count()` (~50k rows for the dogfood loop).
- **One-shot guarantee + surface.** A `file_chunks_backfilled_at` row in `index_meta` records that the backfill ran; the runtime checks this row before issuing the backfill query. Surfaces as one info-level `degradedWorkers` entry: `"context: migrated N rows to file_chunks (one-shot)"`.
- **Authoritative correctness via overwrite.** Backfilled rows reflect `chunks.file_path`'s first-writer-wins approximation — they're not authoritative. The next `reconcileFiles()` invocation that touches a file overwrites its `file_chunks` rows with the authoritative re-walked set. Within one full `warden init` cycle, the approximation is reconciled.
- **Hard-fail-and-require-`--rebuild` rejected.** Forces unnecessary Voyage cost on the dogfooder for no semantic-quality gain — the backfill plus next reconcile is functionally equivalent at zero cost.
- **Lazy-no-backfill rejected.** Until the first init reconciles, `semantic.ts`'s file-attribution path would have to fall back to `chunks.file_path` — keeping the divergent attribution code alive across an indeterminate window.

### 6 — `semantic.ts` attribution: route through `file_chunks`

- **Current behavior.** `semantic.ts` calls `chunkStore.getManyByHash(aboveThreshold)` → reads `record.filePath` to attribute the chunk to a file. With the new junction, this attribution is _approximate_ (first-writer-wins).
- **New behavior.** `semantic.ts` queries `fileChunksStore.getFilesForHashes(aboveThreshold.map(r => r.chunkHash)) → Map<chunk_hash, file_path[]>`. For each `(chunk_hash, file_path[])` pair, emit one `SemanticHit` per file_path (max-aggregated per file at the existing site). Shared chunks across files produce multiple hits, each correctly attributed.
- **Existing `SemanticHit` shape unchanged**: `{ chunkHash, similarity, startLine, endLine }`. The per-file aggregation Map (`hitsByFile`) already keys on `record.filePath`; the only change is _which_ file_path that key holds.
- **Chunks table's `startLine` / `endLine` stay authoritative for the rendered evidence.** They reflect the source file at the time the chunk was indexed; after reconciliation, line numbers match the current file content.

### 7 — File rename: m16-plan.md → m17-plan.md

- `git mv m16-plan.md m17-plan.md` preserves history of the deep-security plan.
- A renumber header note appends to the existing ADR-0031-era renumber note at the top of `m17-plan.md` (now two redirects deep: `m15-plan.md → m16-plan.md → m17-plan.md`).
- ADR-0029 stays Superseded; its pointer text in subsequent ADRs + the §86 Deferred Items paragraph + the §83 status row all gain the new `m17-plan.md` redirect target.
- CLAUDE.md milestone roadmap reorders: new M16 entry (this ADR's deliverables) above the existing deep-security entry (now relabeled M17).

**2026-05-19 note:** `m17-plan.md` is now the setup/onboarding placeholder; the deep-security plan moved again to `m18-plan.md`.

### 8 — What's explicitly NOT in M16

- ❌ Alias / shadow index for `warden init --rebuild`. The blog's "build new index overnight, validate, atomically swap alias" pattern. Real value when the dogfooder bumps Voyage SKUs (currently never auto-rebuilds per ADR-0019 #6). Defer until the second SKU bump surfaces a concrete pain.
- ❌ Retrieval observability — logging per-review chunk hashes + similarities + signal provenance to a `review_retrieval` table. The blog's last failure mode ("retrieval problems disguising as LLM problems") is real; a debug layer is the right answer. Defer until dogfood evidence surfaces a "the review missed X because retrieval was wrong" case the dogfooder can't diagnose otherwise.
- ❌ Background daemon / watch-mode (`warden patrol` from ADR-0011, Model C from ADR-0019). Implicit refresh on `warden review` covers the steady-state UX; daemon adds a process-lifecycle surface that's unjustified at single-user scale.
- ❌ Multi-vector retrieval / hybrid BM25+semantic / second-model reranking. ADR-0019 deferral list item; speculative without dogfood evidence.
- ❌ Dropping `chunks.file_path` / `chunks.file_sha`. Vestigial after backfill but kept for the backfill window. Future cleanup ADR if the auto-backfill stays disabled long enough that no production indexes reference them.
- ❌ Per-chunk content-hash gating beyond what content-addressing already gives us. The blog suggests chunk-level hashing as a second gate beyond file-level; warden's content-addressed `chunks.chunk_hash = sha256(content)` PK + `INSERT OR IGNORE` semantics + `embeddingStore.whichExist()` pre-check already give the same effect (re-chunking a file with 1 changed chunk re-embeds 1 chunk, not N). No new gate needed.
- ❌ Migration tool for production indexes that fail the auto-backfill heuristic. The dogfooder is the only consumer; corner-case migrations get a manual `warden init --rebuild` escape hatch.
- ❌ `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_FILES` belt-and-suspenders knob alongside the USD cap. Single knob keeps the env table from growing redundantly. If a future dogfood case surfaces a per-file pathology the USD cap doesn't catch (e.g., one giant file that _just_ fits the cap), the second knob earns its row at that moment.

### Caveats — judgment calls + known footguns

- _The backfill is approximate by design._ Pre-M16 indexes store first-writer-wins file_path on chunks; the backfill propagates that approximation into `file_chunks`. The first subsequent `warden init` (full reconcile) overwrites the approximation. Between backfill and first reconcile, `semantic.ts` may attribute a shared chunk to whichever file inserted it first. Acceptable per the dogfood-quality v0 bar; doc the limitation in the close-out so future readers know the backfill rows aren't authoritative.
- _Crash mid-`reconcileFiles()` between two files leaves a partial-progress state._ Per-file transactions are atomic, so each completed file is on disk; in-progress + queued files remain at their pre-call state. On re-run, the merkle diff re-identifies the unchanged-pre-crash files (which are now stale-by-disk), and `embeddingStore.whichExist()` deduplicates the chunks already embedded. The partial progress is forward-progress; re-run is idempotent. Doc this in the plan's "running cost" section because users may observe partial cost on crash + the remainder on re-run.
- _USD cap fires per-file, not per-batch._ If a single file's pre-flight estimate alone exceeds `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD`, the file is skipped and the remainder of the budget (which equals the full cap) is available for subsequent files. The cap is _cumulative_ over the run, not per-file. The "remaining_budget" accountant lives in `reconcileFiles()`; emit progress events show running spend.
- _Estimate accuracy._ `estimate.ts` heuristic is LOC-based; actual Voyage cost depends on token count which varies by language + comments density. Observed range across the M6 dogfood is ±25% of estimate. For the cap, we use the estimate; if a file embeds and the _actual_ cost pushes past cap, the remaining budget for the next file is the actual remaining (not the estimated remaining) — accountant is honest.
- _Pre-M16 indexes don't know `file_sha` for many chunks under the M6 schema._ Wait — they do. `chunks.file_sha` is a non-null column from M6. The backfill propagates it. Confirmed by reading `packages/db/src/schema/chunks.ts:24`.
- _Implicit refresh interacts with `--base` and `--stdin`._ `warden review --base feature` or `warden review --stdin < diff.patch` may run against a working tree that doesn't reflect the diff. The refresh runs against the **working tree** (via `walkRepo`), not the diff — so the user gets the working-tree freshness regardless of which diff they're reviewing. Document this explicitly so users don't expect `--stdin` to imply "review without refreshing anything."
- _Workspace packages with their own caches._ The M12 `LookupTypeDefOptions.packageSearchRoots` hardening + `.warden/cache.sqlite` is anchored to the nearest repo root per `resolveCachePath()`. `reconcileFiles()` reads from that same DB. Nested workspace packages (e.g., `apps/web/`) inherit the parent repo's index — no per-package indices, consistent with M6.
- _Future GitHub bot will want this too._ `apps/github-bot/` (ADR-0013) wraps `review()` — when it ships, it'll want the same implicit refresh. The reconciliation primitive is intentionally not CLI-coupled (lives under `@warden/core`); bot wrappers inherit it via `review()`. No premature extraction in M16.
- _Implementation specifics live in `m16-plan.md`._ Same pattern as ADR-0031 → `m15-plan.md`, ADR-0030 → `m14-plan.md`. ADR-0032 is the design commit; the plan is the file-by-file implementation brief (schema migration, store impl, det-priors wiring, smoke harness scope, close-out checklist).

**Status.** Done — shipped on the `m16` branch (2026-05-17) under `01a5fcf` + a post-dogfood fix bundle (see the close-out delta in the §83 status row). All five deliverables landed: `file_chunks` junction table, `reconcileFiles()` primitive, implicit `warden review`-time refresh capped by `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD`, one-shot auto-backfill, and `semantic.ts` attribution rerouted through the junction. Post-dogfood fixes added: Gemini schema adapter for workers (parity with the M15 boss-loop adapter), `repo_merkle_root` snapshot after reconcile (shared `computeRepoMerkleRoot()` helper), one-line refresh success log via `det-priors.ts:formatRefreshSummary()`, and `Float32Array(0)` silent-corruption guard in `reconcile.ts`. The latent worker-fallback finding (Gemini rejects `tools[]` + structured-output) was reframed as ADR-0033's concurrency-cap response: tool-stripped retry + Gemini call restructure deferred behind bot-wrapper telemetry; the immediate quota-saturation surface gets addressed at the dispatch boundary instead. M17 is now setup/onboarding; the deep-security harness is preserved at `m18-plan.md`.

---

## ADR-0033 — Worker-dispatch concurrency: per-tier semaphores at the dispatch boundary (post-M16 audit response)

**Context.** ADR-0030 shipped the M14 review harness; ADR-0031 retuned its boss-loop via programmatic dispatch (PD-multi) which makes Round 0 fan out _N_ workers in a single `Promise.all` before the boss takes its first step. ADR-0032 finished init/review alignment and surfaced — in its close-out — a latent worker-fallback finding: Gemini's structured-output API rejects `tools[]` + `responseMimeType: 'application/json'`, so when the Anthropic primary 429s on a worker call, the fallback hits a distinct 400 and the worker returns `{ok:false}`. The M16 close-out paragraph deferred that to "a future ADR-0033 covering worker-fallback strategy."

Reviewing the surface from the audit pass surfaced a sharper framing: the worker-fallback bug is **cosmetic in the steady state** (the `{ok:false}` return degrades cleanly through `degradedWorkers`, the boss adjudicates the remaining workers, the review still emits a `CommentSet`). The **load-bearing** problem behind the latent fallback bug is that high-parallelism Round 0 fan-outs can saturate the Anthropic rate-limit window _before_ any fallback decision matters — and once we're saturated, the no-Gemini-fallback world (ADR-0017's M14 amendment for the tools + structured-output exception path) has no slack. Today a PD-multi review on a diff with 30 substantive files dispatches up to 60 workers in one tick (det-routed concern + correctness × 30 files); on the M16 dogfood diff we observed 12 dispatches firing simultaneously and Anthropic 429s in the trail.

There are three honest responses to the original "worker fallback to Gemini still 400s" framing:

- **(a)** Throttle dispatches so the no-fallback path doesn't get tested under saturation.
- **(b)** Strip tools from the Gemini retry — call Gemini without `tools[]` and let the worker complete tool-less. Requires per-worker prompt branches, downgrades worker capability in the fallback, and is hard to validate without bot-wrapper telemetry.
- **(c)** Restructure the Gemini worker call as multi-turn (structured-output → tool round-trip), spreading tools across calls so the API surface stops conflicting. Largest blast radius; speculative without a second case demanding it.

(a) is cheap, reversible, and observable. (b) and (c) are exactly the kind of speculative provider-adapter work ADR-0006 warned against without dogfood evidence. The bot wrapper (`apps/github-bot/`, ADR-0013) is the natural surface that will _actually_ hit production quota walls; until that wrapper exists, (b)/(c) would be guessing at a problem we can't measure. M18's deep-security harness will exercise the same dispatch boundary on much larger diffs, doubling the value of having (a) in place before then.

The other framing the audit considered was a "soft budget" — bail out of Round 0 early when projected cost exceeds a knob — but the M16 dogfood evidence is that the saturation comes from _parallelism_, not total volume (PD-multi runs come in well under the $3 per-run cost ceiling). Soft-budget would constrain the wrong axis. Deferred to M19+ if a real cost-runaway case surfaces.

**Decision.** Ship per-tier dispatch concurrency caps inside the existing `dispatch_worker` boundary; defer (b) and (c) behind bot-wrapper telemetry; defer soft-budget bail-out behind a real cost-runaway case.

### 1 — Mechanism: two per-tier semaphores, constructed once per `runReview()` invocation

- **New file `packages/core/src/orchestration/semaphore.ts`** exports a `Semaphore` class (~30 LoC): `constructor(maxConcurrent: number)`, `acquire(): Promise<() => void>` (returns the release fn), private FIFO waiter queue. Pure in-memory; no timers, no AbortSignal in v0; releasing past `maxConcurrent` is a no-op (idempotent release).
- **Constructed at the harness entry.** `runReviewHarness()` builds a `{ strong: Semaphore, cheap: Semaphore }` pair from `env.WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_STRONG` and `env.WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_CHEAP`, then threads them into `makeDispatchWorkerTool({ ..., concurrency })`. One pair per review; never module-global (a `vitest`-shaped concurrent-review-in-the-same-process world stays clean).
- **Acquired at `runOneDispatch`.** The single dispatch boundary both Round 0's `Promise.all` and the boss's in-loop `dispatch_worker` tool path flow through. Acquire → call the route fn → release in a `finally`. The semaphore wraps the _route call_, not the worker LLM call directly — the worker's own `streamText` tool-use loop holds the slot for its entire wall-clock duration, which is what we actually want to throttle.
- **Tier selection comes from the resolved worker tier**, not from the boss's optional `tier?` override field — i.e., after `routeWorker()` decides whether the actual call is Sonnet or Haiku. Boss overrides flow through transparently because the override only changes which getter (`getWorkerStrongModel()` / `getWorkerCheapModel()`) is invoked, and the tier slot tracks the resolution.
- **Single-slot footprint by design.** A dispatch holds exactly one slot from one tier; no cross-tier blocking, no priority inversion. Strong-tier saturation does not starve cheap-tier workers (this is the _point_ of the per-tier split).

### 2 — Env: `WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_STRONG` + `WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_CHEAP`

- **Defaults.** `STRONG: 4`, `CHEAP: 8`. Calibration: Anthropic's tier-2 rate limits are ~50 rpm for Sonnet and ~100 rpm for Haiku at the time of writing; 4-strong × ~15s per worker ≈ 16 rpm peak, well under the limit with slack for retries; 8-cheap × ~6s per worker ≈ 80 rpm peak. Provider-neutral naming so M18 and BYOLLM inherit the shape.
- **Validation.** `@warden/env` validates as positive integer; min 1; no upper clamp (a future ADR may add one if dogfood surfaces a memory-pressure case). `0` is rejected — the path for "no concurrency at all" is `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS=1` + skip Round 0, which is a different surface.
- **Vocabulary alignment.** Mirrors `getWorkerStrongModel()` / `getWorkerCheapModel()` getter naming. _Not_ `WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_SONNET` / `_HAIKU` — those are Anthropic-specific tier slugs and would leak provider vocabulary into the env table that BYOLLM (ADR-0006) needs to keep neutral. See §6 below for the parallel `TierEnum` rename that stays out of scope.

### 3 — Surface: aggregated info entry, silent on the happy path

- **One `degradedWorkers` entry per review, emitted only when `totalQueued > 0`.** Shape: `{ kind: 'info', topic: 'worker-concurrency', message: 'concurrency cap engaged: 12/30 dispatches queued (max wait 14.2s, total queued time 31.8s)' }`. The three numbers come from the scratchpad aggregator (§4).
- **Silent on the happy path.** If every dispatch acquires its slot without waiting, the entry is omitted — no `kind: 'info'` noise on small diffs. This matches the M16 refresh-summary discipline: surface the cap only when it actually engaged.
- **Per-dispatch logging stays out of v0.** No per-call duration logs, no slot-by-slot timeline. The aggregated summary is enough to tell whether the cap is too tight (high `totalQueued`, low `maxWait` → spread out OK) vs too loose (low `totalQueued`, high `maxWait` → one outlier worker is the bottleneck, not the cap). Per-dispatch debug logging earns its row when a real diagnostic need surfaces.

### 4 — Implementation locus

- **`packages/core/src/orchestration/semaphore.ts`** — Semaphore class (~30 LoC).
- **`packages/core/src/review-harness/tools/dispatch-worker.ts`** — `runOneDispatch` wraps the route call: pick tier slot from resolved worker tier, `await concurrency[tier].acquire()`, record wait duration via `Date.now()` deltas, run the route, `release()` in `finally`. Threads the wait/queue metrics into the existing `WorkerOutput` envelope via a new `concurrency?: { waitMs, queuedAtAcquire }` field that the scratchpad aggregator reads. (~25 LoC.)
- **`packages/core/src/review-harness/scratchpad.ts`** — `ReviewScratchpad` gains `recordConcurrencyMetric({ waitMs, queuedAtAcquire })` + a getter `concurrencyAggregate(): { totalQueued, maxWaitMs, totalQueuedMs } | null`. Returns `null` when `totalQueued === 0` so the harness skip can be a single null-check. (~15 LoC.)
- **`packages/core/src/review-harness/harness.ts`** — At the end of `runReviewHarness()`, after Phase 2 returns, read `scratchpad.concurrencyAggregate()`; if non-null, push the §3 entry onto the result's `degraded[]` before Phase 3. (~10 LoC.)
- **`packages/env/src/index.ts`** + `.env.example` + `docs/environment.md`\*\* — Two new rows mirroring the existing `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS` / `WARDEN_REVIEW_WORKER_BUDGET` shape.

### 5 — Smoke: deterministic timing assertion, no LLM, no API keys

- **`packages/cli/scripts/smoke-fix-worker-concurrency.mts`** — Stubs the route fn with a 100ms `setTimeout` × N dispatches × `cap=2` setup; asserts (a) wall-clock duration approximates `Math.ceil(N / cap) × 100ms` within ±20ms slack, (b) the info-entry's `totalQueued` matches `max(N - cap, 0)`, (c) per-tier slots don't cross-block (strong saturation under N strong dispatches doesn't delay one cheap dispatch run concurrently with them). Strong-tier and cheap-tier slots are exercised separately + together. Runs in <2s.
- **`pnpm smoke:fix:worker-concurrency`** wires into the existing per-fix smoke convention (mirrors `smoke-m11.mts` / `smoke-m12.mts` / `smoke-m13.mts` script naming). The fix branch does not bump the milestone numbering; the smoke lives under the `scripts/` folder rather than getting its own `m{N}-plan.md`.
- **No real LLM, no API keys required.** The cap acts on dispatches regardless of whether the route call is real or stubbed; smoke validates the wrap, not the worker. Real-LLM validation happens in the next dogfood `pnpm warden review` run against the warden repo — observable via the new info entry when the cap engages.

### 6 — What's explicitly NOT in this ADR

- ❌ **Tool-stripped Gemini retry (option b)** — strip `tools[]` from the Gemini fallback so worker calls complete tool-less. Real cost-of-implementation: per-worker prompt branches + a separate Gemini path + tooling for "worker completed without lookupTypeDef access" diagnostics. Deferred behind `apps/github-bot/` (ADR-0013) telemetry — until the wrapper exposes a real provider-failure rate, we can't tell whether (b) buys back any catch rate.
- ❌ **Restructured Gemini worker call (option c)** — multi-turn structured-output ↔ tool round-trip so the API surface stops conflicting. Larger blast radius than (b); same telemetry gate.
- ❌ **Soft-budget Round 0 bail-out** — pre-flight USD estimate of Round 0 + bail if projected cost > `WARDEN_REVIEW_ROUND_0_MAX_USD`. M16 dogfood evidence is parallelism-bound, not volume-bound; soft-budget would constrain the wrong axis. Deferred to M19+ if a real cost-runaway case surfaces.
- ❌ **`TierEnum` rename to strong/cheap nomenclature** — the env vars (this ADR) and the getter functions use `strong`/`cheap`, but the `dispatch_worker` tool's `TierEnum` still uses `'sonnet' | 'haiku'`. Cosmetic inconsistency captured in `CONTEXT.md` "Open inconsistencies"; out of scope for this ADR's no-milestone-bump posture. A future schema-migration ADR may collapse the vocabulary.
- ❌ **Cross-process / queue-backed concurrency control** — the v0 semaphore is in-memory per `runReview()` invocation. A future `apps/github-bot/` worker pool will want process-pool-aware throttling (e.g., Redis-backed token buckets); that's the bot wrapper's problem and earns its own ADR when the wrapper ships.
- ❌ **AbortSignal threading through the semaphore** — useful when the boss's `streamText` is cancelled mid-flight, but the M14 harness today doesn't propagate cancellation through `runOneDispatch`. Add when the cancellation surface earns a row.
- ❌ **Per-dispatch debug logging / OpenTelemetry-shaped tracing** — the §3 aggregate is enough for v0 diagnostics. Detailed traces earn their row when a real diagnostic need surfaces.
- ❌ **Milestone bump.** Ships on the `fix/worker-concurrency` branch as a roll-up bullet appended to CLAUDE.md's M16 close-out paragraph; no deep-security milestone slot consumed.

### Caveats — judgment calls + known footguns

- _Default values are calibrated against Anthropic tier-2 rate limits at ADR commit time._ Future tier bumps + multi-provider mixing under BYOLLM will need recalibration; the defaults are env-overridable, not constants. If the dogfooder upgrades to tier-3, raising `STRONG: 8` is safe and reduces queueing visibly.
- _The per-tier split assumes tier resolution is stable across the lifetime of a dispatch._ Boss-side overrides via `dispatch_worker.tier?` flow through `routeWorker()` _before_ the semaphore acquire — the resolved tier is what books the slot. A future ADR that introduces dynamic tier-switching mid-worker would invalidate the split; flag at that point, not now.
- _Single-slot accounting is honest but not perfectly fair._ FIFO queue means a Round 0 burst of 30 dispatches starves any later boss-side dispatches until the burst drains. That's the intended behavior: Round 0 is the deterministic-correctness path, and Round 1+ adjudication is allowed to wait. If dogfood reveals a "boss can't get a turn" pathology, the queue earns priority lanes — but speculative without evidence.
- _Info-entry message vocabulary intentionally mirrors `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD`'s._ Both surface "the cap engaged, here's the impact" without prescribing a remedy. Don't drift into "consider raising `WARDEN_WORKER_CONCURRENCY_STRONG`" — the user reading the info entry already knows the env var because they're reading the CLI output of a tool they configured.
- _Semaphore lives under `orchestration/`, not `review-harness/`._ `orchestration/runner.ts` + `orchestration/scratchpad.ts` survived the M14 close-out; the semaphore is the same kind of primitive (used by harness code, not part of the harness's content shape). M18's deep-security harness will inherit it directly — no extraction churn when that lands.
- _Smoke timing assertions tolerate ±20ms._ Node's `setTimeout` has measurable drift under CI load; 20ms slack covers it without false negatives. If CI flake surfaces a tighter floor, bump to ±50ms; don't switch to a different timing primitive without a real diagnostic reason.
- _The (b)/(c) deferral is genuinely gated on bot-wrapper telemetry, not on schedule pressure._ When `apps/github-bot/` ships and exposes real provider-failure rates, the data tells us whether tool-stripped retry meaningfully claws back catch rate. Until then, the no-Gemini-fallback path is correct: the cap protects the path from getting tested under saturation.
- _Future GitHub bot will want this too — and will want more._ The in-memory semaphore is per-process; the bot will run many `review()` invocations concurrently and need a queue-shaped throttle that survives process boundaries. The cap shape stays inheritable; the storage swap is the bot wrapper's problem.
- _Implementation specifics live in this ADR's §1–§5._ No `m{N}-plan.md` for this fix branch — the ADR itself is short enough to carry the implementation brief.

**Status.** Direction — design locked 2026-05-18. Ships on the `fix/worker-concurrency` branch; no milestone bump. M16 close-out paragraph in CLAUDE.md gains one roll-up bullet pointing at this ADR; CONTEXT.md gains the **concurrency cap** glossary entry + ADR cross-references in **fallback chain**, **boss loop**, and **`dispatch_worker`**; `docs/environment.md` gains two rows. Implementation locus: `packages/core/src/orchestration/semaphore.ts` + `packages/core/src/review-harness/tools/dispatch-worker.ts` (wrap) + `packages/core/src/review-harness/scratchpad.ts` (aggregator) + `packages/core/src/review-harness/harness.ts` (emit) + `packages/env/src/index.ts` + `.env.example`. Smoke: `packages/cli/scripts/smoke-fix-worker-concurrency.mts`.

M18 (deep-security harness) remains preserved at `m18-plan.md`; M17 is setup/onboarding; `review-eval` v1 and the PD-multi security trade stay unscheduled follow-ups until dogfood evidence decides their order.

---

## ADR-0034 — Setup/onboarding: env-based secrets with layered JSONC config

**Context.** Before M17, Warden behaved like a single-repo dogfood tool: the CLI loaded the nearest `.env`, `wardenEnv()` required Anthropic even for `warden check`, and users had to copy provider keys between repositories. That does not scale to "install once, use on any repo", and it conflicts with future bot/cloud wrappers that need the same readiness facts without scraping terminal prose. At the same time, Warden should not invent a secret store or force users away from Infisical, Doppler, 1Password, shell exports, or CI-managed env injection.

**Decision.** M17 ships a layered Warden config runtime in `@warden/env` and keeps secrets env-based.

### 1 — Config layers

- Built-in defaults always exist: Anthropic primary LLM, Google optional fallback, Voyage embeddings.
- Global config lives at `~/.config/warden/config.jsonc`.
- Project config lives at `<repo>/warden.jsonc` and is created only by explicit `warden setup project` / `warden setup --project`.
- Later layers override earlier layers. Config is JSONC for comments/trailing commas, but schema-restricted.

### 2 — Secret handling

- Config files may only name env vars with `apiKeyEnv`; they must not contain raw API keys.
- Env lookup order is direct process env first, then configured env files, then project `.env` / `.env.local`, plus a one-off `WARDEN_ENV_FILE`.
- Process env wins over files, so `infisical run -- warden review`, CI secret injection, and shell exports remain first-class.
- `warden setup` writes `~/.config/warden/env` mode `0600` with commented placeholders only. The global config dir is mode `0700`.

### 3 — Command-scoped readiness

- `warden setup` requires no provider keys and prints readiness.
- `warden check` is deterministic-only and must be zero-key runnable.
- `warden review` requires the configured primary LLM key (Anthropic in M17).
- `warden init` requires the configured embedding key (Voyage in M17) unless `--dry-run`.
- Google/Gemini fallback is additive readiness, never a blocker.

### 4 — Surfaces

- `warden setup` creates global templates if missing and prints a human readiness report.
- `warden setup --check` is read-only diagnostics.
- `warden setup --json` emits written files, config paths, env-file lookup results, provider readiness, and command readiness for future GitHub/Slack/hosted wrappers.
- `warden setup project` creates `warden.jsonc` and still ensures global defaults exist if missing.

### 5 — Deferred

- OS keychain / hosted auth / account login.
- Interactive prompts.
- BYOLLM model selection beyond the provider-routing shape.
- Custom alert configuration and cloud bot onboarding.
- Cross-process/provider credential mutation while a review is already running.

**Status.** Implemented in M17 on 2026-05-19. Implementation locus: `packages/env/src/config.ts`, `packages/cli/src/commands/setup.ts`, CLI command wiring in `packages/cli/src/index.ts`, provider factories in `packages/ai/src/provider.ts`, embeddings in `packages/ai/src/embeddings/index.ts`, and docs in `README.md` / `docs/environment.md` / `CONTEXT.md` / `docs/milestones.md`.

---

## ADR-0035 — Dogfood-lesson intake: three lanes (detector / prompt delta / repo overlay) with retirement discipline

**Context.** Alfred PR#14's dogfood pass (2026-05-20) was the second category-gap data point of the same shape as warden's own M6 PR#3 review (the basis for ADR-0020). Devin caught four real bugs warden missed: two were diff-removed behaviors (library favourites dead-state from `.slice(1)` on the items array; settings sign-out lost `navigate({to:"/login"})` on a section refactor), one was a unit / coordinate-space mismatch (a text-character offset returned by `doc.textBetween(...).length` passed as a ProseMirror position), and one was a design-system-specific visual regression (white-on-white pill text from a Radix Tabs migration that flipped `text-gray-50` to `text-gray-1000` in the codebase's inverted gray scale). Unlike ADR-0020's four misses — which were _different concerns_ (perf vs docs vs UI vs git hygiene) and earned their own slots in `CategoryEnum` — these four are all `correctness`-shaped. Two routes were available: add `regression` + `unit-mismatch` as peer categories at the correctness tier (the ADR-0020 precedent) or sharpen the `correctness` worker prompt. Both have ceilings: the schema route inflates `CategoryEnum` without helping the human reader scan (splitting flavors of correctness is cosmetic), and the prompt route eventually buries the worker in pattern paragraphs the LLM under-attends to. Neither ADR-0020 nor ADR-0021 (which established the LLM-question → detector-assertion promotion path) specified what happens _upstream_ — how a raw dogfood lesson enters the pipeline in the first place. This ADR names that intake and the discipline that keeps the LLM lane from becoming a landfill.

**Decision.** Every dogfood-miss lesson is classified at intake into one of three lanes, with explicit retirement discipline.

### 1 — Three intake lanes

- **Detector-shaped** — bounded, structural patterns recognizable from AST / diff / type-info alone. Lesson becomes an M-plan backlog entry under `docs/dogfood-backlog.md` until scheduled. Ships as a deterministic runner in the **det priors** phase (CONTEXT.md §1), following the ADR-0021 promotion path. False positives are acceptable when the LLM triage layer downgrades them; what matters is that the _shape_ is deterministically recognizable from the inputs a det-prior runner has.

- **LLM-only residue** — patterns whose detection requires reading intent, cross-function reasoning across third-party API semantics, or other judgment a deterministic runner cannot replicate. Lesson becomes a **prompt delta** in the relevant worker prompt under `packages/core/src/review-harness/prompts/workers/*-system.md`, tagged with a `<!-- dogfood: <YYYY-MM-DD> <repo>#<PR> — <one-line summary> -->` audit comment immediately above the delta.

- **Repo-overlay-specific** — the pattern only makes sense in the dogfooded repo's design system / naming conventions / domain vocabulary. Not added to warden core; documented as a candidate for `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` (per ADR-0008's known-debt path, generalized to dogfood-derived rules) and left to the repo owner to decide whether to encode.

The three lanes are exhaustive over what warden core can usefully absorb. Lessons that don't fit any lane are not lessons warden acts on; they may still earn a memory note for future-evidence accumulation, but they do not touch the codebase.

### 2 — Retirement discipline

When a detector-shaped lesson graduates to a producer (ADR-0021's path), its corresponding prompt delta in the worker — if one was added pre-promotion as residue coverage — is removed in the same change. Otherwise warden double-pays: the detector emits the finding _and_ the LLM still hunts for it, eating tokens and inflating false-positive risk where the detector is authoritative.

Audit cadence: any session can run `rg "<!-- dogfood:" packages/core/src/review-harness/prompts/` to enumerate active deltas, cross-check against shipped detectors, and propose retirements. No automated audit in v0 — manual grep is sufficient at the expected delta volume (single digits).

### 3 — Audit-comment shape

```
<!-- dogfood: 2026-05-20 alfred#14 — settings nav dropped on section refactor -->
- **Refactor-lost behavior.** Code moved between functions / components / sections …
```

Date + `<repo>#<PR>` + a sentence; nothing structured beyond that. Grep is the consumer. If machine-readable lesson tracking earns its rent later (auto-generated stale-lesson reports, per-detector retirement triggers), upgrade to YAML front-matter on each delta block; explicitly out of scope for v0.

### 4 — Applied to alfred PR#14

- **Bug 1 (white-on-white pill from Radix Tabs migration)** → **repo overlay**. The detection rule ("Tailwind class string combines `bg-{X}` and `text-{Y}` where the design system's CSS variables resolve both to similar lightness") only makes sense given the repo's inverted gray scale (`--gray-50: 28 28 28; --gray-1000: 255 255 255`). Documented as overlay candidate; not added to warden core. Had a future overlay runtime landed first, this would have been the textbook case for it.
- **Bug 2 (library favourites dead-state from `.slice(1)`)** → **detector backlog**. Pattern: items array constructed via `.slice(N)` / `.filter(...)` is passed to a single-select primitive (`Tabs`, `RadioGroup`, etc. from a configurable allow-list) where the removed item names the primitive's default-state value. AST-detectable with a small primitive registry. Backlog entry: **UI state reachability detector**.
- **Bug 3 (settings sign-out lost `navigate` on refactor)** → **detector backlog _plus_ a prompt delta** for the residue. Detector pattern: diff hunks that _move_ code between functions / components where the old hunk contained a side-effect call (`navigate`, `await fn()`, `track()`, subscription cleanup, error reporting) and the new hunk does not. Needs git-blame access on the same logical hunk. Backlog entry: **refactor-lost-behavior detector**. Pre-promotion, the prompt delta in `correctness-system.md` covers semantic side-effects without a name-list match (e.g., custom `useEffect` cleanup, repo-specific telemetry helpers).
- **Bug 4 (text-offset returned by `doc.textBetween(...).length` passed as ProseMirror position)** → **LLM-only**. The general "number from API A flows into API B in a different coordinate space" check is too broad for a deterministic detector — false positives would dominate. Pure prompt delta in `correctness-system.md` under a new "Unit / coordinate-space mismatch" bullet.

**Why.** ADR-0020 was right that _naming_ drives LLM attention — the LLM cannot look for what it has not been named. ADR-0021 was right that some named things should graduate to detectors.
