What was missing was the intake step that decides _which_ lane a new lesson belongs in, and the retirement step that prevents the LLM lane from accumulating forever. The intake question is short and answerable on the dogfood pass itself: "could a runner recognize this shape from AST / diff / type-info alone?" If yes, M-plan. If no but the residue is general across repos, prompt delta. If no and the residue is repo-specific, overlay. The audit comment makes the LLM lane self-policing without inventing tooling. The intake mirrors warden's own production discipline — citation-grounded findings, deterministic where possible, LLM only for the residue — applied recursively to warden's own growth.

**Alternatives.** (1) **Add `regression` + `unit-mismatch` as peer categories at the correctness tier.** Rejected — both are flavors of `correctness`, and splitting them does not help the human reader scan the output; it inflates `CategoryEnum` and forces priority-order churn for a cosmetic distinction. ADR-0020's four categories earned their split because they named different _concerns_; these do not. (2) **`misc` / wildcard category with confidence-gated comment surfacing + SQLite `misc_findings` table for offline cluster-and-promote.** Rejected — the discovery loop is human-curated at intake (the dogfooder classifies on the spot), not LLM-clustered after the fact. The SQLite table is premature mechanism for a workflow that is still single-digit lessons; memory files + this ADR + `docs/dogfood-backlog.md` are the working backlog until detector M-plan items accumulate enough to earn the table. (3) **Pure prompt extension with no retirement step.** Rejected — exactly the ceiling the dogfood discussion named ("we cannot shove all the wisdom in the world in a prompt"). Without retirement, every dogfood pass adds prompt mass and never subtracts. (4) **Encode lessons as embedded chunks retrieved per-dispatch via the M5/M6 selector.** Rejected as over-engineering for v0 prompt-delta scale; reconsider above ~20 active deltas, alongside the eval-suite ADR named below.

**Caveats.** Lanes aren't watertight — bug 3 demonstrates a hybrid intake (detector for the structural majority + prompt delta for the semantic residue). Intake classifies the _dominant_ lane; residue may also live in another lane, with both audit comments and a backlog entry referencing the same dogfood origin. **"Detector-shaped" is a judgment call.** Err detector-side when the pattern is bounded and structural; err prompt-side when ambiguity dominates. Repeat dogfood evidence on a prompt-delta lesson is the signal to upgrade it to a detector backlog entry (re-classify the lane, write the M-plan ticket, leave the prompt delta in place until the detector ships). **The audit comment is grep-only.** Acceptable at current scale; not acceptable past the threshold above. **Repo-overlay lane is aspirational in v0** — there is no `.reviewbot/overlay.yaml` runtime today (ADR-0008 reserves the path; no consumer exists). Repo-overlay lessons accumulate as documentation candidates until the overlay surface earns its first concrete consumer. **At-scale audit needs measured signal, not manual grep.** Once active deltas pass single digits, or warden's dogfood surface grows past the current set of personal repos, the eval-suite + persistence layer behind it earns its own future ADR — covering fixture provenance, ground-truth labeling, per-detector / per-prompt-delta precision-recall measurement, and the compliance questions a shared corpus of cross-repo diffs raises even at one-user scale. ADR-0035 is the manual-cadence foundation that scaled mechanism builds on, not its replacement.

**Status.** Decision adopted 2026-05-20. Implementation locus: `packages/core/src/review-harness/prompts/workers/correctness-system.md` (two tagged deltas under "What counts as a correctness finding": **Refactor-lost behavior** and **Unit / coordinate-space mismatch**), `CONTEXT.md` §6 (new `dogfood-lesson intake` entry next to `dogfooding`), `decisions.md` Snapshot row, and a new `docs/dogfood-backlog.md` carrying the two detector M-plan candidates (UI state reachability detector + refactor-lost-behavior detector) until they're scheduled into a numbered milestone.

---

## ADR-0036 — Sentry's Warden as prior art: borrow the agent-invocation seam, reject skills-as-platform

**Context.** Sentry shipped `@sentry/warden` (open source: [warden.sentry.dev](https://warden.sentry.dev), [getsentry/warden](https://github.com/getsentry/warden)) under the Seer product line. Sentry's CEO raised it on 2026-05-21, framing this Warden as "less generalized" than theirs and asking how it benches. The site + repo surface four design ingredients worth examining as prior art:

- **Skills as markdown files** following the [agentskills.io](https://agentskills.io) specification. Two ship in-box (`security-review`, `code-review`); arbitrary additional skills are user-authored. The product _is_ the skills runtime, not the checks themselves.
- **Multi-agent post-processing** that merges "same-root-cause" findings across per-skill outputs and validates suggested fixes before surfacing them.
- **Meta-skill** that lets other AI coding agents (Claude Code, Cursor, etc.) invoke Warden as a sub-tool from inside their own loops.
- **GitHub Action + inline PR comments** as the CI surface; JSONL + terminal report locally; `warden.toml` config; BYO API keys (Anthropic or OpenAI).

This ADR fixes Warden's posture toward each ingredient — same template as ADR-0015 used for DeepSec. The "less generalized" framing the CEO offered correctly names the axis (Warden is narrower by design, grounded over generative); this ADR turns that read into explicit borrow / reject / diverge decisions. **Naming overlap (`@sentry/warden`, `warden.sentry.dev`, GitHub org name colliding on the same product category) is acknowledged but explicitly out of scope** here; ADR-0003 owns the rename question.

**Decision.**

- **No borrow needed: same-root-cause merging.** Warden's boss already owns this. `review-harness/prompts/boss-system.md:101` ("If two workers found near-duplicate issues, merge into one Comment with the highest-confidence sources"), `:109` ("Same rule, adjacent lines, same root cause — emit one Comment with a line range; drop the rest"), and `:169` ("Workers do the citing; you do the dedup, the priority sort, the dropping") are the explicit synth-time directives. Sentry's published claim and Warden's current discipline land in the same place; the topology differs (Sentry uses a dedicated post-skill agent; Warden has the boss do it during the synth phase of the boss-loop per ADR-0030) but the outcome is the same. Ratify the existing design. If post-synth duplicates show up in dogfood, ADR-0035's three-lane intake handles the residue — prompt delta if LLM-only, dedicated post-boss consolidation runner if structurally recognizable.

- **No borrow needed: output / config surfaces.** `--json` already ships (ADR-0010); GH inline PR comments are scheduled under the bot roadmap (ADR-0013); env + layered JSONC config exists (ADR-0034). `warden.toml`-style TOML config is a duplicate surface for no current gain.

- **Borrow (defer to bot milestone).** **Agent-skill invocation seam.** Ship a `@warden/agent-skill` artifact (location: a new `apps/agent-skill/` package) compatible with whatever invocation contract Claude Code / Cursor settle on — `agentskills.io` is the current candidate but the contract, not the spec name, is what matters — so other agent loops can call Warden as a sub-tool, running the deterministic phase + boss-loop + citation-verify under their orchestration. Zero `@warden/core` impact: it consumes the existing I/O-pure review pipeline through the same entry point the future GitHub Action and VS Code wrapper will use (ADR-0013). This is distribution, not a new capability. Deferred until the bot milestone gets scoped; the architectural commitment is "the seam is reachable from `@warden/core`'s public surface," which ADR-0013 already enforces.

- **Reject.** **Skills-as-markdown extensibility for Warden's own checks**, and any conformance to `agentskills.io` as the format Warden uses to define its own concerns. Warden's six review concerns (correctness, scalability, consistency, security, committability, leverage — per ADR-0027 + ADR-0028 + ADR-0030 + ADR-0035) are hand-crafted because the value bet is grounded-and-narrow. Letting users author arbitrary markdown skills inverts that bet — each user-authored skill is unverified LLM prompt mass, and the citation discipline (ADR-0008, ADR-0015) does not survive arbitrary skill content. Independent of the spec question: adopting `agentskills.io` as Warden's _own_ check format would tie Warden's roadmap to Sentry's, with no offsetting gain. _Note: rejecting the spec for our own checks is independent of producing a sub-tool that's invocation-compatible with the spec — see the previous bullet._

- **Diverge.** **Fix-suggestion validation.** v0 surfaces no patches. If patch-surfacing ever ships, the validation gate is deterministic — the patch parses, TSC remains clean, no new ESLint errors, no regression in pre-existing diagnostics — rather than LLM-validated as Sentry does. Same shape of divergence as ADR-0015's diff from DeepSec: prefer external / deterministic oracles over LLM-as-judge for trust-load-bearing checks.

**Why.** Sentry's design optimizes for _coverage breadth via user-authored skills_. Warden's design optimizes for _finding trust via citation discipline_. These are coherent product bets, not severities on the same axis. The CEO's "less generalized" framing names the right axis; the right response is not to widen toward Sentry's surface but to make the narrow surface measurably more trustworthy. The one genuinely missing piece in Warden's design — riding other agents' invocation surfaces as a distribution path — is a borrow that doesn't compromise the wedge, so it's adopted but deferred behind the bot roadmap. Everything else is either already shipped (consolidation, output formats, config) or actively rejected (skills-as-platform). The split mirrors ADR-0015's "borrow shape, reject grounding model" template — same posture applied to different prior art.

**Near-term constraint.** None load-bearing. The synth-time merging directive in `boss-system.md` stays as-is; no audit-tagged delta is added under ADR-0035 because the behavior already lives in the prompt. If a dogfood pass shows post-synth duplicates the boss should have merged, file a backlog entry under `docs/dogfood-backlog.md` — promote to a dedicated post-boss consolidation pass _only_ once at least two cases land, per ADR-0035's three-lane promotion path.

**Alternatives.**

1. **Adopt `agentskills.io` for Warden's own checks.** Rejected as the core divergence — erases the grounding discipline that justifies the project. The "every finding is citable" guarantee is the wedge.
2. **Skip the prior-art read entirely.** Rejected for the same reason ADR-0015 rejected ignoring DeepSec: shared-shape prior art is too useful to leave unexamined, and the explicit divergence list sharpens the wedge for future contributors and for the project's own public framing.
3. **Ship the agent-invocation seam now (skip the bot-milestone defer).** Rejected — distribution work before the review loop is dogfood-stable inverts ADR-0002. The seam earns rent when the contract it exposes is stable; the synth output is still calibration-tuned post-M15 (ADR-0031 close-out flagged ≥1 known limitation seed for M15+ follow-ups).
4. **Add a dedicated Haiku post-boss consolidation pass now.** Rejected as premature mechanism. The boss already directs same-root-cause merging; a dedicated pass earns rent only when dogfood evidence of boss merge-failures accumulates, per ADR-0035's promotion path.
5. **Build a `warden.toml`-style config surface.** Rejected — duplicate of ADR-0034's env + layered JSONC. Two config surfaces double the failure modes for the same set of user-tunable knobs.
6. **Treat Sentry as a feature-roadmap-parity competitor and bench head-to-head.** Rejected — the product bets are non-comparable on a single axis. A bench has rent only if both tools claim the same thing; Sentry claims coverage-breadth-via-skills, Warden claims findings-with-citable-evidence. A bench that scores both on "findings caught per diff" buries the disagreement instead of naming it. The honest artifact is a methodology document that names the divergent claims and measures each tool against its own; that is downstream of this ADR, not part of it.

**Caveats.** **Naming is out of scope here.** ADR-0003 owns the rename question; this ADR makes no commitment to a rename regardless of how the name overlap evolves. **The "no borrow needed" ratification assumes the boss's merge directive is actually working in production.** If dogfood shows it's not, the answer is the three-lane intake (ADR-0035), not a retroactive amendment of this ADR. **Sentry may evolve.** Their roadmap is private; if `agentskills.io` becomes a cross-vendor spec adopted by multiple agent vendors (not just Sentry), the agent-invocation seam may be cheap enough to pull forward of the bot milestone. The reject of _checks-as-skills_ stands regardless of spec adoption. **CEO framing is a data point, not a directive.** "Less generalized" is the CEO's mental model of the axis we sit on; this ADR treats it as a useful one-sentence framing, not as a product-strategy commitment.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-05-21. No code lands at ADR commit time. Implementation: the agent-invocation seam (`apps/agent-skill/`) stays in ADR-0013's bot-milestone backlog; the dedicated post-boss consolidation pass stays in the conditional-on-dogfood-evidence backlog (ADR-0035). Snapshot row + Status row added to `decisions.md`. No `CategoryEnum`, `PRIORITY_ORDER`, `SourceType`, or SQLite schema impact.

---

## ADR-0037 — Format-check runner safety: read-only, diff-scoped, mutation-guarded

**Context.** A future setup/onboarding path can plausibly discover a repo's formatter and run a format signal near the beginning of `warden check` / `warden review`. That signal is useful only if it behaves like review infrastructure. The dangerous failure mode is a configured formatter command that rewrites the real working tree before Warden computes its findings, especially if it formats a large number of unrelated files. That would pollute the diff, bury the user's actual change, and violate the same trust boundary that makes Warden's deterministic runners acceptable: review may inspect and report, but it must not silently edit.

**Decision.** Any format-check runner is read-only, diff-scoped, and mutation-guarded.

### 1 — Read-only by default

Warden must prefer native non-mutating formatter modes: `prettier --check`, `biome check`, `dprint check`, or equivalent. A command that writes in place is not valid as a `check` / `review` runner. Patch-producing behavior, if it ever ships, belongs behind an explicit future surface such as `warden fix`; this ADR does not create that surface.

### 2 — Diff-scoped output

Formatter diagnostics are only actionable review comments when they intersect the diff's touched files and line ranges. Formatting drift outside the diff is repository hygiene, not a PR finding. If the formatter reports many untouched files, Warden emits at most one `degradedWorkers` entry with topic `format-check`, e.g. "formatter reported 312 untouched files; comments limited to touched files." It does not fan out comments over unrelated files.

### 3 — Mutation guard

The runner snapshots the working tree before invoking the formatter and checks it again afterward. The implementation can start with `git status --porcelain` plus file hashes for touched files; a later version can widen the hash set if dogfood finds gaps. If the real tree changes, Warden fails fast with an actionable misconfiguration message and does not continue on the mutated diff. The user fixes the formatter command or runs their formatter explicitly outside Warden.

### 4 — Write-only formatter escape hatch

If an otherwise useful formatter has no check mode, Warden runs it in a temp copy of the repo or of the relevant files. It then compares the temp result back to the original and reports only diff-scoped diagnostics. The real repository remains untouched.

### 5 — Runner placement

The format-check runner, if built, belongs in **Det Priors** alongside TSC, ESLint, and other deterministic producers. It can run early for fast feedback, but its output is still subject to the same noise-filter and hard-rule discipline as every other runner. It has no LLM-specific behavior and no new schema category unless dogfood proves formatting needs a distinct category; the default mapping should reuse `style` or degraded metadata.

**Why.** Review tools must preserve the user's working tree. A formatter that rewrites unrelated files changes the object under review and produces misleading downstream signals: `git diff` grows, workers read formatted churn as if it were user intent, and Warden's own comments become entangled with side effects it caused. Read-only check mode is the simple path. The mutation guard is the belt-and-suspenders defense against misconfigured scripts, wrapper tools whose semantics change across versions, or repo-specific commands named "format:check" that still write.

**Alternatives.**

1. **Run the repo's existing `format` script directly.** Rejected. Script names are conventional, not semantic. `format` usually writes, and even `format:check` is only trustworthy after mutation guarding.
2. **Let Warden auto-format before review.** Rejected for `check` / `review`. Auto-formatting may be useful as an explicit fix command later, but silently changing code before analysis violates the CLI's one-shot review contract.
3. **Report all formatter drift, including unrelated files.** Rejected. Warden reviews the current diff. Existing repo-wide drift should not drown the change under review.
4. **Disable formatter support entirely.** Rejected as too blunt. Formatting is a useful deterministic signal when scoped and non-mutating; the risk is side effects, not the signal itself.

**Caveats.** A line-range-accurate format diagnostic may require formatter-specific parsing; a v0 runner can conservatively attach file-level comments only for touched files. Temp-copy execution has cost on large repos; first implementation should prefer native check mode and reserve temp copies for configured write-only tools. Formatter discovery/config earns its own implementation plan so Warden does not guess command semantics from package names alone.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-01. No code lands at ADR commit time. Implementation backlog: formatter command discovery/config; read-only runner in Det Priors; temp-copy execution for write-only tools; mutation-guard smoke tests proving unrelated files are not changed or commented on. No `CategoryEnum`, `PRIORITY_ORDER`, `SourceType`, or SQLite schema impact.

---

## ADR-0038 — Review intensity profiles: medium / high / xhigh as the user-facing cost-quality knob

**Context.** The M14/M15 review harness has enough knobs to shape cost and depth: boss rounds, Round 0 programmatic dispatch, extra concerns, worker budget, worker concurrency, refresh budget, confidence gates, and eventually M18's deep-security harness. M17's config runtime also introduced `modelPolicy.profile: "standard"` as a placeholder. Exposing all of those independently makes Warden powerful but awkward: users think in terms of "catch the P1/P2 bugs" vs "go all the way on this refactor," not in terms of `WARDEN_REVIEW_BOSS_ROUNDS=3` plus a worker cap plus a provider reasoning setting. Provider model surfaces are also moving: some vendors expose stronger code/reasoning modes that can push sub-agent quality up at high token cost. Warden should be able to use those for high-stakes runs without making the default path expensive or tying the CLI to a provider marketing name.

**Decision.** Add a future **review intensity profile** surface. Profiles are product-level presets that resolve to low-level harness/model/cost controls.

### 1 — Profile names and UX

The user-facing profiles are:

- **`medium`** — cost-aware review targeting P1/P2 bugs. Best for ordinary PR hygiene, pre-merge checks, or "tell me if this is dangerous."
- **`high`** — balanced default. This preserves the current Warden promise: deterministic priors + calibrated boss/worker review for substantive code changes.
- **`xhigh`** — explicit expensive mode. Best for risky migrations, legacy-code refactors, security-sensitive rewrites, or "spend the tokens; I want depth."

CLI shape: `warden review --profile medium|high|xhigh`. Config shape: project/global default under `review.profile` or the existing `modelPolicy.profile` slot if the implementation keeps that name. An env override may exist for CI, but the CLI flag wins over config and env. `warden check` remains deterministic-only; it does not become a cheap alias for `medium`.

### 2 — What a profile controls

A profile owns these axes together:

- **Bug-depth target** — which tiers/categories Warden optimizes for.
- **Short-circuit gates** — when the pipeline can stop after Det Priors, skip Round 0, skip semantic refresh, skip workers, or skip M18 deep-security.
- **Worker fan-out** — Round 0 enabled/disabled, extra concerns, per-file grouping, worker budget, concurrency, and follow-up dispatch allowance.
- **Model/reasoning policy** — which boss/worker model tier and provider reasoning/code mode to use, if the configured provider supports it.
- **Cost posture** — default max-cost/soft-budget behavior and how loudly Warden reports that a profile's budget changed the path.
- **Output surface** — max comments, Tier 3 surfacing, and whether low-confidence exploratory findings are allowed.

Low-level env vars stay available as escape hatches, but they should not be the normal UX. The profile resolver produces an explicit, inspectable resolved plan so JSON/bot surfaces can say which phases ran and which were skipped.

### 3 — Initial semantics

| Profile  | Intent                            | Short-circuit posture                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Worker/model posture                                                                                                                                                | Output posture                                                                |
| -------- | --------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `medium` | Catch likely P1/P2 issues cheaply | Stop after Det Priors when the diff is docs-only, config-only, formatting-only, or has no substantive code plus no det-prior signal. Skip semantic refresh when over the small refresh budget. Run no workers on clean/no-signal diffs. | Lower boss rounds, smaller worker budget, Round 0 only for substantive files with det-prior signal or security-sensitive paths. Prefer standard model settings.     | Tier 1/2 only by default; Tier 3 only with `--verbose`.                       |
| `high`   | Default balanced review           | Current M15 PD-multi behavior, with existing no-op short-circuits for empty/docs-only diffs and M16 refresh budget.                                                                                                                     | Current boss/worker tiers and calibrated Round 0 + correctness extra.                                                                                               | Current output rules.                                                         |
| `xhigh`  | Spend for depth                   | Avoid cheap no-signal exits on substantive code. Allow larger refresh budget and wider context. If M18 exists, run deep-security automatically on security-sensitive diffs or when requested by config.                                 | More boss rounds, higher worker budget, wider concern fan-out, larger file groups for cross-file reasoning, and provider high-reasoning/code modes when configured. | Allow more comments and Tier 3 exploratory findings, still citation-verified. |

The table is a starting contract, not final numeric tuning. Exact budgets should be calibrated through `review-eval` plus dogfood traces, not guessed.

### 4 — Cost-saving without UX damage

Every short-circuit must be explainable. If `medium` skips workers because Det Priors saw no substantive code, the CLI prints a concise phase line and JSON includes a structured `degradedWorkers` or metadata entry naming the gate. Silent savings are fine only when the result is indistinguishable from doing the work (e.g. empty diff). For visible user intent, Warden should say "skipped expensive worker phase under `medium`; use `--profile high` or `--profile xhigh` for deeper review."

Short-circuiting is allowed to save cost only when it preserves the profile promise. `medium` may skip deeper reasoning on low-signal diffs because its promise is P1/P2 coverage. `xhigh` should not skip a substantive refactor merely because Det Priors are quiet; that is exactly the case the expensive profile exists to cover.

### 5 — Provider reasoning/code modes

Provider-specific high-reasoning or code-specialized modes are implementation details behind the profile resolver. Warden should not expose a CLI flag named after a provider's current product label. Instead:

- Profile says desired reasoning effort: `standard`, `elevated`, or `max`.
- Provider adapter maps that to Anthropic/OpenAI/Google-specific request fields when supported.
- Unsupported providers degrade to the nearest available model tier and report the downgrade in metadata.
- The default `high` profile stays cost-controlled even if a provider introduces a new expensive reasoning feature.

This lets `xhigh` use premium code/reasoning behavior for users who explicitly asked for it while keeping default review predictable.

### 6 — Relationship to existing verbs

`warden check` stays deterministic and keyless. `warden review --profile medium` is not the same command: it may still use LLMs when the profile's gates decide the diff deserves them. `warden security` remains the focused deep-security verb. `warden review --profile xhigh` may include the security harness for security-sensitive diffs after M18, but the focused verb still exists for users who want security-only output.

**Why.** Profiles match how users actually decide to spend review budget. A legacy migration and a routine UI copy change should not run the same LLM topology. At the same time, making users tune individual harness internals is the wrong abstraction and will age badly as providers add reasoning controls. A profile resolver gives Warden one stable user promise and one internal place to evolve cost/depth policy.

**Alternatives.**

1. **Keep only low-level env knobs.** Rejected. It is powerful but poor UX, and bot/CI users need a stable intent label they can put in config.
2. **Separate verbs for every depth.** Rejected. `check` / `review` / `security` already carry semantic differences. `medium-review`, `deep-review`, etc. would fragment the CLI without improving the core decision.
3. **Default everyone to the most expensive reasoning mode.** Rejected. It burns user budget on ordinary diffs and makes Warden feel unpredictable.
4. **Never use provider premium reasoning modes.** Rejected. Some users explicitly want maximum depth for high-risk refactors; Warden should support that as an opt-in.
5. **Make `xhigh` just mean "run more workers."** Rejected as too narrow. Depth comes from model/reasoning policy, context refresh, security harness inclusion, follow-up allowance, and output policy together.

**Caveats.** Profile names must be validated in `review-eval` before implementation ships; this ADR locks the shape, not the numeric thresholds. Provider-specific reasoning fields are temporally unstable and must be read from current official provider docs at implementation time. `xhigh` can still emit zero comments when citation-verified evidence does not support a finding; expensive mode buys more search, not permission to speculate. Cost reporting becomes more important: the CLI should show profile + actual spend in the final summary.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-01. No code lands at ADR commit time. Implementation backlog: config schema expansion; CLI `--profile`; profile resolver; resolved-profile metadata in JSON; phase-level short-circuit gates; provider reasoning-policy mapping; per-profile eval thresholds and smoke fixtures. No `CategoryEnum`, `PRIORITY_ORDER`, `SourceType`, or SQLite schema impact expected.

---

## ADR-0039 — Product identity: Warden becomes a hosted platform (reopens ADR-0001, amends ADR-0024)

**Context.** Through M17, every ADR assumed the ADR-0001 frame: single user, local-first CLI, OSS-quality bar, no multi-tenant scaffolding. ADR-0024 leaned on that frame to declare the naming-collision question (`@sentry/warden`, bare `warden` taken on npm) _dormant_ and to size the public surface as "personal-portfolio-grade, won't renew the domain." The owner has now decided to take Warden hosted — a Greptile-class product: web dashboard, accounts, a server-side index, and eventually the ADR-0013 PR/Slack bots as first-class surfaces rather than deferred wrappers. That decision changes the cost calculus ADR-0024 relied on and reactivates three dormant questions at once (naming, multi-tenancy, hosted infra).

**Decision.** Warden's north star moves from "elaborate solo CLI" to "hosted code-review platform with a local-first CLI as one client."

1. **Two coordinated surfaces, one core.** `@warden/core` stays the I/O-pure review engine (the ADR-0004 / ADR-0013 constraint upheld — this is what makes the pivot cheap). The CLI is one client; a hosted service (`apps/api` + worker pool) and a web dashboard (`apps/dashboard`) are new clients of the same `review()` entry point. No review logic moves into the server; the server orchestrates, persists, and fans out.

2. **Multi-tenant from the storage seam down, not the review logic up.** ADR-0016's storage interfaces (content-addressed, model-versioned, portable, queue-decoupled) already anticipated a non-SQLite backend; a hosted Postgres/pgvector (or managed vector DB) implementation of the same interfaces is additive. Tenancy (org/repo/user scoping) lives in the storage + API layer, never in `@warden/core`. The local CLI keeps its SQLite backend unchanged.

3. **Dashboard is in scope (Phase 4).** Greptile-class surfaces: repo/index status, review feed, per-finding detail with citation evidence, cluster (linked-repo) management, settings, usage/cost. Build on the design system lifted from `-dimension-ai-legacy` (Next 15 / Tailwind / Radix — transactional dashboard DNA, has tables/teams/settings); build fresh the review-specific surfaces (diff viewer, findings panel) neither dimension codebase carries. ADR-0024's static `apps/web` marketing site and ADR-0014's interactive-triage surface both fold into the dashboard's identity — they stop being separate deferred apps.

4. **Naming is now blocking.** A hosted, discoverable product competes for SEO, npm namespace, and brand against `@sentry/warden` (same category, same name). ADR-0024 §1 and ADR-0036 both parked this explicitly on the solo-project framing; that framing is gone. ADR-0040 reopens ADR-0003's rename question as a hard prerequisite to any public launch.

5. **Sequencing preserves the wedge.** The hosted pivot does not change _what_ Warden finds (grounded, citation-verified, narrow per ADR-0008 / ADR-0036). Phases 1–3 (chunk quality, breadth, clusters) ship locally first and are cloud-compatible by construction; the dashboard + hosted API land last, after the core is best-in-class. We do not build the platform on top of a mediocre engine.

**Why.** The pivot is cheap _because_ of accumulated discipline: an I/O-pure core (ADR-0013), interface-shaped storage (ADR-0016), provider-routing config (ADR-0034), and JSON output (ADR-0010) already separate "what Warden decides" from "where it runs." Going hosted is mostly new clients + a tenancy layer + a vector-backend swap, not a rewrite. The strategic reason to do it now: a CLI-only tool can't compete with Greptile/Sentry on the surface developers actually live in (the PR). The wedge — trust via citation — is more valuable embedded in a PR feed than behind a manual `warden review`.

**Alternatives.** (1) Stay local-first CLI (rejected by owner — ceiling too low against PR-native competitors). (2) Hosted-first, deprecate the CLI (rejected — the CLI is the dogfood loop, and the local-first / data-residency story is a differentiator vs cloud-only tools; keep it a first-class client). (3) Build the dashboard now, before chunk quality (rejected — a dashboard over a six-language raw-text-embedding engine showcases the weakness; depth first).

**Caveats.** This reopens ADR-0001 (single-user) and ADR-0024 (solo-portfolio framing) — both are amended, not deleted; the OSS-quality bar and local-first CLI survive. Hosted infra reintroduces everything ADR-0024 §2 listed as the reason to stay static (secrets, queues, abuse mitigation, per-user state, SOC2-adjacent expectations) — those become real backlog, not hand-waves. Data-residency posture (code travels to embed/review providers per ADR-0019) becomes a contractual concern at multi-tenant scale, not just a doc note — BYO-key and self-host tiers move up the roadmap.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-11. No code at commit time. Gates ADR-0040 (naming) before any public launch. Amends ADR-0001 + ADR-0024.

---

## ADR-0040 — Name resolution under the hosted pivot (reopens ADR-0003)

**Context.** ADR-0003 chose distribution as `npx warden`; the bare `warden` npm name is already taken, and Sentry ships `@sentry/warden` / `warden.sentry.dev` in the exact same category (AI code review) with brand momentum and a CEO who has publicly compared the two (Sentry CEO signal, 2026-05-21). ADR-0024 and ADR-0036 both deferred this to ADR-0003 under the solo-project framing. ADR-0039 removed that framing. A hosted, discoverable product cannot launch into a same-name same-category collision with a well-funded incumbent.

**Decision.** Reopen the name. This ADR fixes the _criteria_ and _candidate directions_; the final pick is the owner's call and is recorded here once made.

Criteria: (a) npm + GitHub org + domain available together; (b) no same-category collision with an incumbent; (c) survives a hosted brand (memorable, sayable, ownable); (d) minimizes churn against the existing `warden` / `wrdn.beauty` mental model.

Candidate directions (not final):

- **Keep "Warden", scope + differentiate.** Ship as `@<brand>/warden` or a product name where "warden" is descriptive; lean on the citation-discipline differentiator. Cheapest internally; loses on criterion (b) — still colliding with Sentry on the word that matters.
- **Rename the public product, keep "warden" internally.** New public brand; `@warden/*` package scope and `.warden/` cache dir stay as internal monorepo identifiers. Preserves all code/doc references; only the public surface rebrands. **Recommended direction.**
- **Full rename.** New brand end to end, including package scope, cache dir, and `WARDEN_*` env vars. Cleanest brand, highest churn.

**Recommendation.** Direction 2 — rename the public product, keep `@warden/*` and `.warden/` internal. It clears (a)/(b)/(c) at the cost of a docs/marketing rebrand only, leaving the internal `@warden/*` references, env-var prefixes, and cache-dir contract untouched.

**Why.** The collision is load-bearing only on the _public_ surface; internal package scope is invisible to users and carries no SEO/brand cost. Decoupling public brand from internal scope is standard practice (products routinely ship under a name different from their npm org). It keeps the dogfood loop and every existing ADR cross-reference stable while the brand question resolves on its own timeline.

**Alternatives.** Covered as candidate directions above. Pure "keep warden everywhere" is rejected on criterion (b). Pure full-rename is deferred unless the owner wants the internal churn.

**Caveats.** `.warden/` cache-dir and `WARDEN_*` env vars are a compatibility surface; Direction 3 would need a migration shim. The owner must supply the actual name; until then this ADR blocks ADR-0039's public launch but **not** Phases 1–3 (local engine work is brand-neutral).

**Status.** **Open — reopened 2026-06-11; awaiting name selection.** Reopens ADR-0003.

---

## ADR-0041 — Homegrown chunker: Rust core via napi-rs (supersedes ADR-0019 #2)

**Context.** ADR-0019 #2 took the depend-don't-build call: chunking via `code-chunk` (npm, MIT, pinned), six languages, with documented fork triggers. Two facts now push past that. (1) The sibling `-dimension-ai-code-indexing-rust` project carries a 43-language / 80-extension tree-sitter registry (`src/helpers/language.rs`) that is owned and directly portable as data. (2) `code-chunk`'s breadth is capped at six and its semantic extraction (scope chains, signatures, sibling context) is the expensive per-language work — exactly what "perfect reviews in the major langs" (ADR-0039's quality bar) needs more of. The owner has decided to build Warden's own chunker in Rust, exposed to the Node CLI via napi-rs, reusing the dimension registry + tree-sitter plumbing while adding the semantic extraction `code-chunk` pioneered.

**Decision.**

1. **New crate `crates/warden-chunk`, exposed via napi-rs.** A native addon (`@warden/chunk-native`) consumed behind the _existing_ `Chunker` interface at `packages/core/src/context/chunker.ts` — the single import seam ADR-0019 #2 established stays the only thing `@warden/core` knows about. `CodeChunkAdapter` is replaced by `NativeChunkAdapter`; no other consumer changes.

2. **Semantic parity is the bar, not just AST-boundary splitting.** The dimension indexer's chunking is purely size-based (`text_splitter::CodeSplitter`, ~1024 chars, zero metadata) — porting _that_ would be a quality regression. The new crate reuses dimension's language registry and tree-sitter setup but implements `code-chunk`-equivalent extraction: scope chain, entity signatures, sibling context, imports, and a contextualized embedding string (see ADR-0042). Per-language tree-sitter queries are the real work, written tier-by-tier.

3. **Tiered language coverage.** Tier A (semantic-complete: TS, JS, Python, Rust, Go, Java — the current six) ships first at parity-or-better with `code-chunk`. Tier B (major langs earning breadth: C#, Ruby, PHP, Kotlin, C/C++, Swift — picked by dogfood/demand) adds full semantic queries incrementally. Tier C (the long tail of the 43) is admitted via a **size-windowed fallback** (dimension's text_splitter approach) so any registered language is at least indexable, explicitly flagged as shallow. The walk filter (`init/walk.ts` `SOURCE_EXT_RE`) widens in lockstep with whichever tier is enabled (Phase 2 work).

4. **Distribution: prebuilt platform binaries + wasm fallback.** napi-rs prebuilds per (os, arch) published as optional-dependency packages (the `@napi-rs/cli` standard), with a `code-chunk`-style wasm build as the universal fallback when no prebuild matches. This **amends ADR-0003's "no platform-binary-matrix" stance** — the matrix is now accepted, justified by the quality ceiling and bounded by napi-rs tooling that automates the release matrix.

**Why.** Owning the chunker converts language breadth from "wait on an upstream solo-maintainer" into a registry-data + query-writing task we control, and it lets chunk quality (ADR-0042's contextualized embeddings, future symbol-graph extraction) evolve on our schedule. Rust is the right host: the tree-sitter ecosystem is native-first, the dimension registry is already Rust, and chunking is CPU-bound batch work where native beats wasm meaningfully at `init` scale. napi-rs keeps it a transparent dependency of the TS CLI.

**Alternatives.** (1) Fork `code-chunk` in TS, add langs + wire contextualizedText (rejected by owner; lower ceiling — but noted as the cheaper path and the fallback if the Rust build/distribution burden proves not worth it). (2) Port dimension's Rust chunker as-is (rejected — size-based splitting is a quality regression; we want its registry, not its chunking). (3) Rust CLI sidecar over stdio instead of napi (rejected for steady-state per-call process overhead and a worse install story than optional-dep prebuilds). (4) wasm-only, no native (rejected — gives up the native perf that motivated Rust; kept only as the fallback tier).

**Caveats.** The platform-binary matrix is real maintenance ADR-0003 deliberately avoided — CI release infra (per-target builds, prebuild publishing, wasm-fallback wiring) is a prerequisite, not free. Per-language semantic queries are non-trivial and are the actual cost; Tier A must reach measured parity with `code-chunk` on the eval harness (ADR-0031 review-eval + retrieval metrics) **before** `code-chunk` is removed — no big-bang swap. The `Chunker` interface seam keeps the migration reversible: if the Rust path underdelivers, `CodeChunkAdapter` is one adapter away.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-11. No code at commit time. Supersedes ADR-0019 #2 (the `code-chunk` dependency) on completion; amends ADR-0003 (binary-matrix). Pairs with ADR-0042.

---

## ADR-0042 — Embed contextualized chunk text; revisit content-addressed dedup key (revises ADR-0019 #3)

**Context.** ADR-0019 #3 set `chunk_hash = sha256(raw chunk content)` as both the dedup key and the embedding-row key, so identical code in two files collapses to one embedding row. But the corpus side currently embeds the _raw_ chunk text (`chunker.ts:120` stores `content: c.text`; `init` embeds that), while `code-chunk` ships a `contextualizedText` field built specifically for embeddings — it prepends file path, scope chain (`# Scope: Class > method`), entity signatures (`# Defines: …`), imports (`# Uses: …`), and sibling/overlap context. Warden embeds none of it, and silently inherits `code-chunk`'s `overlapLines: 10` default, which _only_ affects `contextualizedText` — so it pays for a feature that does nothing. The semantic signal embeds the unified diff as the query (`semantic.ts:74`) and retrieves these document chunks; prepended symbolic context plausibly aligns better with a diff's own path/symbol structure. Adopting it collides with ADR-0019 #3's dedup key.

**Decision.**

1. **Embed contextualized text, not raw.** The corpus-side embedding input becomes the contextualized string (path + scope + signatures + imports + sibling/overlap context), assembled by the new Rust chunker (ADR-0041) at parity with `code-chunk`'s `formatChunkWithContext`. The raw chunk text is still stored verbatim for display and citation line-ranges; only the _embedding input_ changes.

2. **Dedup key moves to `sha256(contextualizedText)`.** Because contextualized text embeds file path + scope, identical code in two files now embeds differently and must not collapse — keying on the contextualized text is the correct content-address for the thing actually embedded. This **revises ADR-0019 #3**: cross-file dedup savings shrink (identical snippets in different files become distinct rows), accepted as the cost of correct per-location embeddings. The raw-content hash is retained as a separate column for provenance/display dedup. The `file_chunks` authoritative attribution (ADR-0032) is unchanged.

3. **Eval-gated, not assumed.** Whether contextualized embeddings improve diff→chunk retrieval is empirical (the query is a whole diff, not natural language). Before flipping the default, A/B both embedding inputs on the `review-eval` real-PR fixtures (ADR-0031), scoring selector recall against the files each PR actually touched (the `*-misses-*` fixtures already in the working tree are direct ground truth). Ship whichever wins; record the number.

4. **Cost is surfaced.** More embedding rows (less dedup) + larger embedding inputs (context headers) raise `init` token cost. The pre-flight estimate (ADR-0019 #5) accounts for both. The locked-model + `--rebuild` machinery (ADR-0019 #6) carries the re-embed when the default flips.

**Why.** Warden is leaving its embedding provider's primary quality lever unused while paying for an inert overlap setting — the cheapest credible quality win in the indexing layer. Keying on the embedded artifact (contextualized text) rather than a substring of it (raw content) restores the content-addressing invariant ADR-0016 cares about: the hash names exactly what was embedded. The eval gate prevents trading a measured property (dedup savings) for an assumed one (retrieval lift).

**Alternatives.** (1) Keep raw-content keying but embed contextualized text anyway (rejected — first-writer-wins makes a shared chunk carry one file's context arbitrarily; the embedding no longer matches its key). (2) Keep embedding raw text, improve quality elsewhere (rejected — leaves the provider's main lever unused; retained as the safe fallback if the A/B shows no lift). (3) Embed both and store two vectors per chunk (rejected — doubles cost/storage for a marginal hybrid-retrieval gain that is a separate future ADR).

**Caveats.** The dedup-savings loss is real on monorepos with heavy duplication — measure it on a dogfood repo before the flip. The A/B must use median-of-N sampling (ADR-0031 discipline) given LLM/embedding variance. If the lift is within noise, the default stays raw and #1/#2 do not ship — only the inert-overlap cleanup does.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-11. Pairs with ADR-0041; gated on the eval A/B before the default flips. Revises ADR-0019 #3 on adoption.

---

## ADR-0043 — Cross-repo clusters: linked-repo config + cross-repo retrieval (de-defers ADR-0019 / ADR-0026 sibling-repo)

**Context.** Cross-repo awareness has been deferred since ADR-0019 (the M10+ list) and narrowed by ADR-0026 to `.d.ts` lookup-on-demand only — sibling-repo indexing and `node_modules/<pkg>/src` retrieval stayed out. Greptile shipped this as "clusters": a `greptile.json` listing related/pattern repos (frontend+backend, shared libraries, microservice deps) pulled into a review's context. Warden's own context-selection principle (diff is the target; repo + cross-repo deps are adjudication context) always intended this. ADR-0039's hosted pivot makes multi-repo first-class. This ADR de-defers it.

**Decision.**

1. **`warden.jsonc` gains a `cluster` block** (additive to ADR-0034's layered schema — no break to existing configs):

   ```jsonc
   cluster: {
     repos: [
       { name: "api",    path: "../backend", ref?: "main" },      // local sibling
       { name: "shared", git: "git@…:org/shared.git", ref?: "…" } // remote (hosted)
     ],
     mode?: "context" | "review"  // default "context"
   }
   ```

   `context` (default): linked repos are indexed and retrievable as _adjudication context_ — the review target stays the current repo's diff, but the selector and workers can pull chunks/types from linked repos. `review` (cross-repo diff review) is reserved and out of scope here.

2. **Linked repos index into the same content-addressed store, cluster-scoped.** ADR-0016's interfaces make this a storage concern, not a review-logic one. Each chunk/embedding row carries its source-repo identity; the local SQLite backend indexes sibling paths, the hosted backend (ADR-0039) indexes cluster members server-side. Cross-repo chunks are retrieved by the existing semantic + cheap signals, scoped to the active cluster.

3. **Retrieval, not just lookup.** For clustered repos this supersedes ADR-0026's `.d.ts`-only narrowing: linked-repo _source_ is chunked and embedded (ADR-0041 / ADR-0042), so a finding can cite a symbol's real implementation in a sibling repo, not just its `.d.ts`. `.d.ts` lookup remains the path for unlinked third-party packages.

4. **Bounded by cost + explicitness.** Cluster indexing is opt-in via config and surfaced in the `init` pre-flight estimate (each linked repo is a cost line). No implicit cross-repo crawl; only declared cluster members are indexed.

**Why.** Cross-repo context is the highest-value retrieval gap for real teams — microservice + shared-lib topologies are where single-repo review misses most — and it's the feature Greptile is actively marketing. Warden's storage discipline (ADR-0016) and the homegrown chunker (ADR-0041) make it an index-scope + config-schema change rather than a new subsystem. Declared clusters (not auto-discovery) keep cost legible and honor ADR-0019's "gate cross-repo on a real consumer" caveat — the consumer is now the hosted product.

**Alternatives.** (1) Auto-discover linked repos from lockfile/workspace topology (rejected for v0 — cost spikes + surprise indexing; declared clusters are explicit and bounded; auto-discovery is a later additive layer). (2) Keep `.d.ts`-only (ADR-0026) and never index sibling source (rejected — `.d.ts` gives types but not implementation/behavior, which is where cross-repo bugs live). (3) Per-review ad-hoc cross-repo embedding (rejected — re-embedding linked repos every review is cost-prohibitive; index once, refresh incrementally per ADR-0032).

**Caveats.** Stale linked-repo indexes need the M16 refresh story extended across cluster members (per-member Merkle + budget). Remote (git) cluster members in the local CLI need a clone/fetch story the local tool lacks today — local sibling-path members ship first; remote members are a hosted-side concern (ADR-0039). Tenant isolation of cluster indexes is a hosted-security requirement, not a v0 local concern.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-11. De-defers the ADR-0019 M10+ / ADR-0026 sibling-repo retrieval items. Extends ADR-0034 config schema. No code at commit time.

---

## ADR-0044 — Sourced vs reasoned findings: demote the universal citation gate to a per-claim-type discipline; split `evidence` from `sources[]`; observability as the trust spine

**Context.** Warden's founding thesis (ADR-0008) was citation discipline: _the LLM cannot author findings without a tool source; it only triages and formats what deterministic runners produced._ ADR-0021 hardened it into "LLMs ask, never assert" — LLM output routed to the `questions[]` lane. That thesis caps recall: real bugs an LLM can reason about but cannot cite to an external authority (refactor-lost-behavior, unit/coordinate-space mismatch, subtle races — the exact class the `*-misses-*` dogfood fixtures and the `project_warden_review_category_gaps` / `project_warden_alfred_pr14_misses` memories document Copilot/Devin catching and Warden missing) get suppressed or softened to questions.

But the M14 review harness (2026-05-16) already broke the thesis without admitting it. The `correctness` worker — a Sonnet LLM doing pure judgment — emits `kind: "assertion"` findings (`review-harness/prompts/workers/correctness-system.md`), and `WorkerFindingSchema` (`workers/finding-schema.ts:35,40`) _requires_ `sources[].min(1)`, satisfied by a **self-quoted** `{path, line, snippet}` triple the worker tags `type: "tool", id: "correctness-worker"`. The substring-verifier confirms the quoted line _exists_; it never confirms the _claim_. So:

- The glossary already lies: **finding** = _"tool-verified defect from a deterministic runner"_ (`CONTEXT.md` §2) and `schema.ts:54` = _"assertions (claims grounded in tool/CVE evidence)"_ — both false since M14.
- Two epistemically opposite things wear `type: "tool"`: a TSC/ESLint/AST detector that _produced_ the finding (authority = the tool) and an LLM's self-quote (authority = none; anti-fabrication only). That single overloaded label makes an honest audit trail impossible.

This ADR ratifies the reality M14 created and makes it honest, rather than writing aspirational discipline the code contradicts on day one.

**Decision.**

1. **Charter: ratify + make honest, don't pretend it's net-new.** Warden findings are judgment-capable and have been since M14. ADR-0044 documents that, fixes the lying glossary/schema entries, and introduces a provenance taxonomy where _how a finding was produced_ is legible. The "demote citations" framing is precise: citation discipline stays the thesis for claims that _rest on an external authority_; it was never appropriate for claims that rest on reading the diff.

2. **Split the locator from the citation (`evidence` vs `sources[]`).** `WorkerFinding` and `Comment` gain an `evidence` field — the self-quoted, substring-verified `{path, line, snippet}` locator — distinct from `sources[]`, which now carries **only external/deterministic citations** (`cve`, `advisory`, `tool`, `api_def`, `repo_convention`, `documentation`, `changelog`, `web`). `evidence` is **mandatory** on every finding (anti-fabrication floor). `sources[]` becomes **optional** and may legitimately be empty. This honors the split the glossary already drew (§2 **evidence** vs **sources[]**, line 57) that the M14 worker path collapsed. `type: "tool"` reverts to deterministic-runner output only; LLM self-quotes never wear it.

3. **The source-mandatory gate is per-claim-type, not per-concern.** A non-empty `sources[]` is required _iff the finding's truth rests on an external authority that exists_:

   | Claim's truth rests on…                | Required in `sources[]`        | Enforcement                                                                                              |
   | -------------------------------------- | ------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
   | a published CVE/advisory               | `cve` / `advisory` (OSV)       | **hard** — no OSV record → drop (unchanged from M3)                                                      |
   | a library API's shape/behavior         | `api_def` (`lookupTypeDef`)    | **soft** — prompt-required; verifier validates cited-but-wrong; uncited slips (ADR-0026 §7, generalized) |
   | a written repo convention / doc        | `repo_convention`              | soft, same shape                                                                                         |
   | **judgment about the diff's own code** | none — `evidence` locator only | n/a                                                                                                      |

   Concern is the wrong axis: `security` is _both_ a hard-gated ESLint detector and a `reasoned` Sonnet worker; `leverage` is _both_ a deterministic detector and an `api_def`-citing worker. The gate keys on the claim, not the worker.

4. **Invariant: no mechanism ever drops a finding solely for empty `sources[]`.** That is the recall cap this ADR removes; re-imposing it by concern would reinstate it through the back door. Mechanical gating survives only where the authority is deterministic (OSV-drop, detector-by-construction, `api_def` structural verify). Everything else is prompt-discipline + anti-fabrication on `evidence`.

5. **Vocabulary (active language refinement).**
   - **finding** — redefined: _any producer's raw pre-synthesis output_ (detector or worker), carrying `evidence` + optional `sources[]` + `kind` + `confidence`. Provenance leaves the word and lives in the sources.
   - **sourced** / **reasoned** — new provenance adjective on findings/comments. **sourced** = carries ≥1 external/deterministic `sources[]` entry. **reasoned** = `evidence`-only, `sources[]` empty. The three legitimate shapes are now nameable: _sourced assertion_ (detector/OSV/api), _reasoned assertion_ (LLM, confident), _reasoned question_ (LLM, ambiguous). `kind` (assertion|question) is orthogonal to provenance. `sourced`/`reasoned` is **derived** (presence of external sources), not a stored field.
   - **citation discipline** — rewritten: _every quoted snippet (in `evidence` or `sources[]`) must be substring-verifiable; claims resting on an external authority must cite it; reasoned claims need not. The discipline is anti-fabrication + cite-the-authority-when-one-exists — not no-LLM-assertions._
   - **substring-verifier** — rewritten: verifies the `evidence` locator on _every_ finding (anti-fabrication) **and** the `{path, line, snippet}` triples in `sources[]` (`tool` / `api_def`). One algorithm, two fields.

6. **Confidence sets `kind`; it never drops.** The control for the `reasoned` lane is a deterministic post-pass in `applyHardRules()` (no second LLM — **ADR-0015 reaffirmed, not reopened**):
   - `reasoned` + confidence ≥ category threshold → **assertion**; `reasoned` + confidence < threshold → **question** (degrade, not drop — preserves recall, is the M4 **clarification question** posture).
   - `sourced` findings: confidence never gates `kind` (authority makes them assertions); confidence stays the sort key.
   - **Tier-1 bypass redefined**: from _"Tier-1 always posts as asserted"_ to _"Tier-1 never drops"_ — a low-confidence Tier-1 reasoned finding still degrades to a question (surfaces, doesn't assert; a 0.5-confidence "you have an auth bypass" is the worst false positive a reviewer can hit).
   - `CATEGORY_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR`'s action changes from drop → degrade-to-question for `reasoned` findings (`security: 0.8` sub-threshold findings become questions, not silence). Noise floor handled by the **volume cap** + the degrade; an optional hard-drop floor (~0.3) defaults off.

7. **Observability trace as the trust spine — descriptive, never a gate.** A per-review **review trace**: a read-model derived from `ReviewScratchpad` at the end of `runReviewHarness()`, not new instrumentation (the data already exists there — `detPriors`, `workerOutputs[]` with `tier` + `toolCalls`, `bossTokens`, `degraded[]`). Records the _deterministic pipeline facts_ — det-priors fired, context retrieved, dispatches `(file, concern, tier, toolCalls[])`, per-finding `{provenance, confidence, kind, evidenceVerified, sources[].type}`, and the deterministic transforms that changed the output (confidence→kind degrades, verifier drops, volume-cap discards, lane-discipline drops). It does **not** record the boss's free-text reasoning (LLM prose, expensive, low-trust, re-imports the LLM-judges-LLM smell). **Invariant: the trace records how a review was produced; it never decides what posts.** Persisted to a local `reviewRuns`-shaped table in `.warden/cache.sqlite` (mirroring `securityRuns`), cloud-compatible by construction via ADR-0016 interfaces; a compact summary rides `CommentSet.metadata`. Dashboard _rendering_ deferred to ADR-0039 Phase 4. Wedge: "phenomenal reviews you can audit," not "we cite."

**Why.**

- _Ratify, don't aspire._ ADR-0008 and ADR-0021 are already contradicted by shipping code. Writing more aspirational discipline repeats the exact failure this grill caught. The honest move is to name what M14 did and give it the discipline it shipped without.
- _Recall is the goal; the gate was the cap._ The dogfood evidence (`*-misses-*` fixtures, the category-gaps memories) is bugs Warden _reasoned about but couldn't cite_. Demoting the universal gate is the direct lever on that recall; `evidence` + confidence + degrade-to-question are the precision controls that keep it honest.
- _Provenance must be legible for the trust spine to exist._ You cannot build an auditable dashboard on a `sources[]` field that calls "the LLM pointed here" and "OSV confirmed this CVE" the same word. The `evidence`/`sources[]` split and the `sourced`/`reasoned` adjective are the minimum vocabulary the trace needs.
- _Per-claim-type over per-concern._ `security` and `leverage` each contain both a deterministic detector and a reasoned worker; a per-concern gate gets one of them wrong. The claim, not the worker, knows whether an authority exists.
- _Decide the shape now, defer the surface._ Same MO as ADR-0015 (prompts-as-files) and ADR-0016 (storage interfaces): the `evidence` field, the `reviewRuns` shape, and the descriptive-not-gating invariant are cheap now and expensive to retrofit; the dashboard is Phase 4.

**Ripple (doc + ADR sweep, to land with implementation).**

- **ADR-0008** — amended: the universal "LLM cannot author findings" thesis narrows to the per-claim-type gate (#3). Citation discipline survives for `sourced` claims.
- **ADR-0021** — edited: "LLMs ask, never assert" is relaxed — a confident `reasoned` finding may be an assertion; the committability-sub-agent-emits-questions shape was the conservative prototype.
- **ADR-0015** — reaffirmed: confidence is self-reported by the worker, never adjudicated by a second LLM; the degrade and the verifier are deterministic. Judgment mode ≠ DeepSec's two-agent revalidation.
- **ADR-0026 §7** — generalized: the accepted epistemic floor (prompt-required + structural-verify-what's-cited + uncited-slips) extends from `api_def` to every `reasoned` producer.
- **CONTEXT.md §2** — rewrite `finding`, `citation discipline`, `substring-verifier`, `sources[]`; add `evidence` (as a Comment/finding field), `sourced`/`reasoned`, `review trace`; resolve the "Open inconsistencies" `finding`-vs-`comment` entry.

**Alternatives.** (1) Keep the universal gate, accept the recall cap (rejected — it's the founding constraint the dogfood evidence falsifies, and the code already abandoned it). (2) Relabel only — add `type: "judgment"` to the source enum, keep the locator inside `sources[]` (rejected — relabels the conflation instead of removing it; every future LLM producer would re-cram locators as fake sources; `Comment` is the wrapper API and there are zero shipped wrappers, so the clean break is free now and expensive later). (3) Per-concern gate (rejected — §3: `security`/`leverage` are each both modes). (4) Drop low-confidence reasoned findings (rejected — reinstates the recall cap at a different threshold). (5) Record the boss's per-finding reasoning in the trace (rejected — LLM prose, expensive, re-imports LLM-judges-LLM).

**Caveats.** Precision risk is real: demoting the gate spends false positives to buy recall. The control is confidence + degrade-to-question + volume cap + the verifier on `evidence` — and it must be _measured_, not assumed. Phase 1's `review-eval` A/B must score `reasoned`-assertions-on vs -off against the `*-misses-*` fixtures on **both** recall and the precision it costs; if recall doesn't move on real misses, the gate demotion isn't worth the ADR-0008 reopening. The `evidence`-field migration touches the public `Comment` schema, `WorkerFindingSchema`, all six worker prompts, `to-comment.ts`, the verifier, and the renderer — one concentrated schema change. `sourced`/`reasoned` is a derived property (presence of external sources), not a stored enum — compute it, don't persist a field that can drift from `sources[]`.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-11. Reopens ADR-0008; reaffirms ADR-0015; edits ADR-0021; generalizes ADR-0026 §7; revises CONTEXT.md §2. Closes the §7.1 open item in `docs/platform-pivot-handoff.md`. Eval-gated per the Caveats before the `reasoned`-assertion default ships. No code at commit time.

---

## ADR-0045 — Backend & full-stack review coverage: reuse `react-doctor` as the deterministic detector corpus + a reasoned checklist lane, classified through ADR-0035

**Context.** The owner maintains a 20-review-deep full-stack TypeScript review checklist (the `review-prompt.md` gist), already named in-scope as a **custom rule** at `docs/platform-pivot-handoff.md` §6 Q1 ("N+1, timeouts, the Promise.all-over-billable-calls trap, library-leverage, TS patterns, a11y…"). It is not one feature request; it is a _corpus of review lessons_ spanning backend data-access (N+1, transactions, pagination, parameterized SQL), security (per-route validation, authZ-ownership, rate-limiter coverage, webhook HMAC, secret-in-log hygiene, HTTP status codes), resilience (fetch/LLM timeouts, idempotency, `Promise.all`-over-billable-calls, env-config), library leverage (Drizzle relational/prepared/`onConflict`, Elysia `guard`/`onError`/TypeBox, AI SDK v6 `maxOutputTokens`/`inputSchema`/`Output`), TS patterns (exhaustive-switch-`never`, guards-over-`as`, no-`any`), and a frontend/a11y half. The question this ADR answers: how does warden absorb that corpus without forking a lint engine, inflating `CategoryEnum`, or re-litigating the citation thesis.

Three facts decide it. (1) A classification pass over the corpus (~80 discrete items) splits it cleanly: roughly half are statically decidable from a single-file AST; roughly half need cross-file or intent judgment (idempotency, ownership-authz, rate-limiter `categorize()` coverage, status-code correctness) and are _not_ statically lintable. (2) The sibling OSS repo `react-doctor` (`~/Developer/oss/react-doctor`) is a mature **386-rule** oxc-based lint engine — 344 single-file oxlint visitor rules plus a **42-rule** project-level `scan()` SAST suite (SQL/NoSQL injection, secret leaks, webhook-signature absence, mass assignment, path traversal, command injection), with `server`/`nextjs`/`correctness`/`js-performance` families — that already covers most of the checklist's security and _all_ of its frontend/re-render/a11y half. It ships an ESLint mirror `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` (which wraps the _full_ `oxlintPlugin.rules` registry; the `scan()`/`ScanFinding` SAST rules ride along only as inert no-op visitors and are filtered out of every mirror preset via `!isScanRule`, so the mirror functionally exposes the single-file **visitor rules** only) and a programmatic `@react-doctor/api` `diagnose()` (which additionally runs those project-level `scan()` SAST rules — call path `diagnose → … → checkSecurityScan`), plus a 3-stage rule-authoring pipeline (`rule-research → rule-writing → rule-validate`) whose validate stage runs the `rde-eval` corpus (the `react-doctor-evals` harness over ~8.4k OSS repos). It has **no TypeScript type checker** — syntactic + scope/CFG heuristics only. (3) Warden already has every home this corpus needs: ADR-0035 defined the three-lane intake (**detector** / **LLM-residue** / **repo-overlay**), ADR-0044 just created the **reasoned** lane (`evidence`-only, `sources[]` optional) the judgment items require, ADR-0036 (§6 Q1 amendment) put custom rules in scope, and ADR-0041 establishes a Rust + tree-sitter + napi seam (`crates/warden-chunk`). This ADR routes the corpus into those homes and resolves the one open seam — _what runs the deterministic half_.

**Decision.**

1. **Intake the whole checklist through ADR-0035's three lanes — this is the first corpus-scale application of that intake, not a single dogfood miss.** Each item answers ADR-0035's question ("could a runner recognize this shape from AST / diff / type-info alone?"): **yes** → detector lane (#2–#3); **no, but general across repos** → reasoned/residue lane (#4); **no, and repo-specific** → overlay/custom-rule lane (#5). The lanes and their retirement discipline are ADR-0035's; the novelty is intaking a curated external corpus at once rather than one PR-miss at a time.

2. **Detector lane: reuse `react-doctor` as the deterministic corpus behind the existing `ToolFinding` Runner seam — do not hand-port rules.** Two new det-prior producers slot into the `Promise.all` in `packages/core/src/review-harness/det-priors.ts`, following the ADR-0028 precedent that already loads ESLint plugins via the Node API (`packages/core/src/runners/eslint-security.ts`, `createRequire`-loaded pinned plugins):
   - **`react-doctor-lint`** — loads `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` through the existing ESLint Node-API path; maps its visitor-rule diagnostics to `ToolFinding`.
   - **`react-doctor-scan`** — invokes `@react-doctor/api` `diagnose()` for the project-level `scan()` SAST rules absent from the ESLint mirror; maps its diagnostics to `ToolFinding`.

   Both emit `kind: "assertion"`, `confidence: 1`, a new `ToolFinding.source = "react-doctor"` (extend the union at `packages/core/src/runners/types.ts`, add a branch in `runners/to-comment.ts`'s `mapSeverity` and in `boss-loop.ts`'s `routeFindingToConcern` so PD-multi's Round-0 dispatch routes them), and populate the **mandatory `evidence` locator** (ADR-0044) from each diagnostic's node range. They run in `warden check` (zero LLM, the recall floor) and are `sourced` findings that sail through every ADR-0044 gate. **Coverage discipline:** before authoring _any_ warden detector, dedupe against react-doctor — it already fires on SQL/NoSQL injection, secret/client-bundle leaks, webhook-signature absence, mass assignment, the full React re-render surface (both missing- _and_ over-memoization), effect cleanup, derived state, list keys, ARIA, and dead code (the last as a whole-project reachability check — DeadCode/knip via the `diagnose()`/scan producer, not a registry rule in the lint mirror). Warden authors nothing react-doctor already covers; it consumes.

3. **Author the genuinely-new backend rules UPSTREAM in `react-doctor`, not in warden.** The ~12 lintable white-space rules — `ai-sdk-v6-no-deprecated-options`, `ai-sdk-v6-tool-input-schema`, `ai-sdk-call-without-timeout-or-abort`, `no-db-query-in-loop` (N+1; react-doctor's `async-await-in-loop` deliberately allowlists `query`/`execute`, so this is a true gap), `no-raw-error-object-in-log`, `fetch-without-timeout-signal`, `no-billable-call-in-promise-all`, `prefer-exhaustive-switch-never-guard`, `no-filter-result-as-cast`, `webhook-hmac-over-reserialized-body`, `elysia-route-missing-validation`, `drizzle-imprecise-column-type` — go through react-doctor's rule pipeline + `rde-eval` corpus and reach warden for free via the `react-doctor-lint` producer. **react-doctor stays the rule factory; warden is a consumer.** (Items react-doctor does not ship, consistent with its no-type-checker / v1 scope — `no-any`, `no-non-null-assertion`, `no-console`, `no-magic-numbers` — warden does not re-ship either; the omission is verified, the _intent_ inferred.)

4. **Reasoned lane: the non-lintable items become tagged worker prompt deltas (ADR-0035 §1 residue), riding ADR-0044's `reasonedFindingMode`.** Idempotency-on-retried-writes, authZ-ownership (not merely authN), rate-limiter `categorize()` coverage, HTTP-status correctness, missing DB indexes, safe-migration shape, the library-leverage prose (Drizzle relational/prepared, Elysia `guard`/`onError`, AI-SDK `Output`), and the interval-billing-resolver class are `correctness`/`security`/`scalability`-shaped judgment. They become `<!-- dogfood/checklist: 2026-06-16 review-prompt — <summary> -->`-tagged deltas in the existing `packages/core/src/review-harness/prompts/workers/*-system.md` (NOT a new concern — ADR-0035 §1 + ADR-0020 prefer prompt deltas over `CategoryEnum` inflation; several, e.g. `Promise.all`-over-billable and refactor-lost-behavior, are _already_ in `correctness-system.md`). They post as `reasoned` findings (`evidence`-only, `sources: []`), degrading to questions below the confidence floor per ADR-0044. **Retirement discipline (ADR-0035 §2):** when one of these graduates to a react-doctor detector (e.g. `no-db-query-in-loop` ships), its prompt delta is removed in the same change so warden doesn't double-pay.

5. **Overlay / custom-rule lane: the checklist itself is the first concrete artifact for ADR-0036's custom-rule amendment.** The full `review-prompt.md` is the owner's review-guidance document; it graduates ADR-0035's reserved repo-overlay lane into the auto-detected repo file + hosted Custom-Context page resolved at handoff §6 Q1. Warden core ships the _generally-true_ subset (lanes #2–#4); the _repo-specific residue_ — a project's own rate-limiter `categorize` list, design-system color inversions, naming/domain vocabulary — stays user-authored guidance, never core. This is the disposition ADR-0035 §4 gave alfred PR#14 bug 1, applied to the whole corpus.

6. **Detector-lane evolution stays open behind the `ToolFinding` Runner seam (resolves the "native runners vs dimension/tree-sitter" question).** Near term, react-doctor reuse (#2) is the call — it is the maximal corpus at zero hand-port cost, and it is TS/JS-only, which is warden's v0 ecosystem (Snapshot row "v0 ecosystem"). It is **not** a permanent commitment: (a) **native warden TS-AST runners** (the ADR-0023/0027 `runners/scalability.ts`/`leverage.ts` pattern, `import ts from "typescript"`) remain the right home for _warden-specific_ signals react-doctor won't host, or where warden's `typescript`-AST gives type access react-doctor's oxc heuristics lack; (b) **tree-sitter `.scm`-query rules on the `crates/warden-chunk` napi seam** (ADR-0041) are the long-horizon _multi-language_ home once breadth past TS/JS matters. The `-dimension-ai-code-indexing-rust` repo is explicitly **not** that backend — it is a closed NATS→chunk→embed→TurboPuffer pipeline with no AST/symbol/query surface and no Node binding; its only reusable asset, the 43-language tree-sitter registry, is already being copied into `warden-chunk` per ADR-0041. As with ADR-0041's `Chunker` seam, the `ToolFinding` Runner contract keeps all three producers swappable without `@warden/core` changes — the migration is reversible by construction.

**Why.**

- _Reuse-before-build at corpus scale._ 386 FP-tuned rules incl. a SAST suite is years of detector work; the ESLint-plugin mirror + `diagnose()` are exactly the two seams warden's ADR-0028 ESLint path already accommodates. Hand-porting forks the corpus and re-pays react-doctor's false-positive tuning for no gain.
- _The checklist already bisects along warden's seams._ Lintable → ADR-0035 detector lane = `sourced`, confidence 1, sails through ADR-0044's per-claim-type gate. Judgment → ADR-0035 residue lane = ADR-0044's `reasoned` lane = exactly the recall the `*-misses-*` fixtures chase. The two prior ADRs were built for this intake; this ADR is their first joint exercise.
- _Single source of truth._ Authoring new backend rules where the rule pipeline + `rde-eval` already live (react-doctor) and consuming via the plugin keeps warden out of the rule-maintenance business and lets both products improve together — the same depend-don't-duplicate logic ADR-0019/0041 applied to chunking.
- _Don't inflate `CategoryEnum` or mint a concern._ ADR-0035 §1 + ADR-0020: naming drives LLM attention, but _flavors_ of correctness/security belong as prompt deltas, not peer categories. A `backend` concern is the cosmetic split ADR-0035 already rejected.
- _Honor the checklist as a product feature, not just internal config._ §6 Q1 already resolved custom rules in scope; the gist is the canonical first instance, and treating it so de-risks the Custom-Context surface with a real artifact.

**Ripple (doc + ADR sweep, to land with implementation).**

- **ADR-0008 / ADR-0028** — the deterministic-detector set grows beyond `tsc` + `eslint-security` to the two `react-doctor` producers; the ESLint-Node-API pattern (ADR-0028) generalizes to a second plugin source + a programmatic-API source.
- **ADR-0035** — first corpus-scale application of the three-lane intake; note that curated external checklists intake identically, and the retirement discipline now also governs checklist-delta ↔ upstream-react-doctor-rule pairs (a cross-repo retirement edge).
- **ADR-0036** — the custom-rule amendment gets its first concrete artifact (`review-prompt.md`); cross-reference from §6 Q1.
- **ADR-0044** — the `reasoned` lane gains its first non-dogfood population source.
- **ADR-0041** — record `warden-chunk` as the eventual tree-sitter-query rule host (#6b); not a near-term dependency.
- **CONTEXT.md** — §5 (Runners) add the `react-doctor-lint` / `react-doctor-scan` producers + the `react-doctor` `ToolFinding.source`; §6 add a **review-guidance / checklist** term and resolve it against **custom rule** (Q1).
- **`docs/dogfood-backlog.md`** — the ~12 new rules become upstream (cross-repo) authoring entries; the reasoned-lane items become tagged prompt-delta entries.
- **`packages/core/package.json`** — add pinned `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` + `@react-doctor/api`, behind a capability gate that no-ops when absent.

**Alternatives.** (1) **Hand-port the rules as native warden TS-AST runners** (rejected near-term — forks a 386-rule corpus and its FP tuning; warden re-pays years of work and diverges; retained only as the home for _warden-specific_ signals, #6a). (2) **Build the detector lane on the `warden-chunk` tree-sitter/napi seam now** (rejected — `warden-chunk` isn't written; tree-sitter `.scm` queries lack scope/type resolution — a _worse_ envelope than react-doctor's already-no-type-checker one for these rules; multi-language breadth isn't warden's v0 need; revisit per #6b). (3) **Use `-dimension-ai-code-indexing-rust` as the AST backend** (rejected — closed pipeline, no AST/query/IPC surface, no Node binding; only its language registry is reusable and ADR-0041 already claims it). (4) **Put the whole checklist in worker prompts (LLM-only)** (rejected — wastes the deterministic floor; the lintable half is cheaper, citable, and FP-controlled as detectors; ADR-0035's "could a runner recognize the shape?" answers _yes_ for half the corpus). (5) **Expand `react-doctor` itself into a backend product / score backends** (rejected at the react-doctor end — its score is category-blind, computed as 100 minus a flat penalty per _distinct_ violated rule key; a backend-only repo trips few react-doctor rules and so scores misleadingly high. Accessibility is one of five display-only diagnostic buckets, not a score input, so the inflation is the sparse-violation mechanism, not a category that "cannot fire." react-doctor stays a rule factory, warden is the review product). (6) **Add a `backend` worker concern + `CategoryEnum` entry** (rejected by default — ADR-0035/0020: flavors of existing concerns are prompt deltas; revisit only if checklist volume buries the correctness/security prompts past ADR-0035's ~20-delta threshold).

**Caveats.** Precision is the real risk: react-doctor is FP-tuned for React repos, so on backend/non-React TS some rules may mis-fire or simply not apply (its capability gate drops React/a11y rules when no React dep is present, but the generic families still run). Every `react-doctor` producer must clear warden's eval clean-fixture "0 unlabeled comments" gate (ADR-0031 gate c) before default-on, gated per-rule-family if needed. **Two eval gates:** new upstream rules clear react-doctor's `rde-eval`; the warden integration clears `review-eval` (recall on `*-misses-*` + the precision it costs) per ADR-0031/0044 discipline.
