The ESLint mirror is **visitor-rules-only**; the SAST `scan()` suite needs the `diagnose()` runner — two producers, and `diagnose()` is a whole-tree walk, so it is review-scoped and budgeted (the `WARDEN_REVIEW_REFRESH_MAX_USD` posture), not necessarily in the fast `warden check` floor. react-doctor has **no type checker** (syntactic + scope/CFG only); rules needing resolved types ("is this really a `Promise` / a typed ORM query") are out of its envelope and stay in the reasoned lane — do not expect detector coverage there. **Supply chain:** `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` / `@react-doctor/api` are external sibling-OSS deps — pin and gate. **Retirement debt:** every checklist prompt delta that later graduates to a react-doctor rule must have its delta removed (ADR-0035 §2), now across two repos. **Upstream-scope risk:** react-doctor is React/frontend-only today (24 React-facing families, no backend/ORM family), so authoring `elysia-route-missing-validation` and `drizzle-imprecise-column-type` upstream presumes a backend/ORM scope expansion it has not yet made; if upstream declines, those two fall back to warden-native TS-AST runners (#6a) rather than the `react-doctor-lint` producer.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-16. Applies ADR-0035 (three-lane intake) at corpus scale; populates ADR-0044's reasoned lane; gives ADR-0036's custom-rule amendment its first artifact; references ADR-0041 (`warden-chunk`) as the deferred tree-sitter-query rule host. Implementation locus: two producers in `packages/core/src/review-harness/det-priors.ts` (`react-doctor-lint` via the ADR-0028 `runners/eslint-security.ts` path + `react-doctor-scan` via `@react-doctor/api`), `ToolFinding.source = "react-doctor"` in `runners/types.ts` + `to-comment.ts` + `boss-loop.ts` routing, tagged prompt deltas in `review-harness/prompts/workers/*-system.md`, the ~12 new rules authored in the `react-doctor` repo's rule pipeline, and pinned deps in `packages/core/package.json`. New external deps + reasoned-lane deltas are capability-gated and eval-gated (ADR-0031 clean-fixture + `*-misses-*`) before default-on. No code at commit time. **Verified 2026-06-16** — every react-doctor claim above was independently checked against the source tree (`~/Developer/oss/react-doctor`) by a 31-agent adversarial verify→refute pass. Thesis holds; factual corrections applied: SAST count 66→**42** (per `rule-registry.test.ts`), 386 split into 344 visitor + 42 scan, ESLint-mirror phrasing (wraps full registry, scan rules inert + preset-filtered), pipeline 3-stage (rde-eval inside `validate`), Alt-5 rationale → category-blind score, "deliberately"→omission-verified/intent-inferred. All 12 upstream-rule gaps confirmed genuine (incl. the `async-await-in-loop` `query`/`execute` allowlist sub-claim); `diagnose()→scan()` disjointness, no-type-checker, and the React/a11y capability gate all confirmed.

---

## ADR-0046 — Backend-coverage implementation seam: consume `react-doctor` via the published CLI subprocess (amends ADR-0045 §2)

**Context.** ADR-0045 (2026-06-16) located its detector lane in two `det-priors.ts` producers: `react-doctor-lint` (loads `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` in-process via the ADR-0028 `createRequire` path) and `react-doctor-scan` (imports `@react-doctor/api` `diagnose()` for the project-level `scan()` SAST suite), with "pinned `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` + `@react-doctor/api`" deps. Implementation reconnaissance (2026-06-16) falsified that dependency shape: `@react-doctor/api` and `@react-doctor/core` are `private: true` and **not published** to npm (`npm view` → not found). The published `react-doctor` package does expose a public `react-doctor/api` subpath with `diagnose()` and `JsonReport` types, but `DiagnoseOptions` exposes only engine inputs like `includePaths`, not the CLI's `scope` / baseline-delta controls; adding `react-doctor` as a dependency would also bring the same oxc native binding + `@sentry/node` transitive weight into Warden's install tree. ADR-0045's direct `@react-doctor/api` producer cannot be built as written, and the importable subpath does not buy the coherence lever this iteration needs. This ADR re-seats the detector lane on the public surface that carries the full corpus **and** the scope semantics: the `react-doctor` CLI's `--json` report.

**Decision.**

1. **One det-prior producer that subprocesses the published `react-doctor` CLI — not two in-process producers.** A single `react-doctor-cli` producer slots into `det-priors.ts`, runs the CLI with `--json --json-compact --no-telemetry --blocking none`, and parses the report through a local minimal Zod schema into `ToolFinding[]`. The local schema follows the public `react-doctor/api` `JsonReport` / `Diagnostic` shape (`schemaVersion`, `ok`, `diagnostics[]`, `summary`, optional `baseline`) but Warden does **not** import `react-doctor` at runtime. One call yields 344 visitor rules **+** the 42-rule `scan()` SAST suite and, when a base ref is threaded (`--base`, see §R1 below), the base-vs-head finding **delta** — collapsing ADR-0045's two-producer split into one. **It does NOT yield dead-code (§R1):** react-doctor's whole-project checks run only at `--scope full`, which is mutually exclusive with the delta/lines scopes warden uses — so warden drops react-doctor dead-code and relies on its own `deadcode` detector; `--scope full` is deferred to ADR-0038 `xhigh`. This is the **TSC / `npm audit` precedent**, not a reversal of ADR-0028: `runners/_shared.ts:spawnCapture` already shells out for `tsc.ts` and `audit.ts`, and CONTEXT.md §5 defines a **detector** as deterministic analysis via "AST traversal … structured comparison … _or process execution (vuln, jscpd)_." ADR-0028's in-process `createRequire` was an _ESLint-plugin-specific_ choice, never a blanket "detectors must be in-process" rule.

2. **Scope discipline: changed-file parity first, introduced-only only when baseline metadata exists.** The runner writes Warden's already-pruned `changedPaths` to a temp file and passes the CLI's hidden `--changed-files-from <file>` flag so react-doctor scans the same file set Warden decided was in scope. In `check`, invoke `--scope lines` to match Warden's current changed-line behavior. In `review`, invoke `--scope changed` **only** when Warden can also thread a git-resolved base into react-doctor's expected env (`REACT_DOCTOR_BASE_SHA` preferred when available; `GITHUB_BASE_REF` otherwise). Without that base metadata — especially stdin diffs — fall back to `--scope lines` and do not claim introduced-only semantics. This keeps the base-vs-head finding delta as the marquee coherence win without making it a false promise; generalizing introduced-only delta to _all_ Warden findings remains deferred to its own coherence ADR.

3. **Scan overlap: `react-doctor` wins; warden retires its 3 overlapping M13 ESLint-security rules.** The CLI's `scan()` families subsume three M13 `eslint-security` rules — `command-execution` ⊃ `detect-child-process`, `artifact`/`repository-secret-leak` ⊃ `no-secrets/no-secrets`, `path-traversal` ⊃ `detect-non-literal-fs-filename` — and add four net-new (`raw-sql`, `nosql`, `webhook-signature`, `request-body-mass-assignment`). Warden **removes** those three rules from `eslint-security.ts` (keeping the other five: `detect-eval-with-expression`, `detect-non-literal-regexp`, `detect-pseudoRandomBytes`, `detect-buffer-noassert`, `detect-disable-mustache-escape`) so `react-doctor` is the single source per family — no double-reporting, the coherence requirement that motivated this ADR.

4. **Runtime: npx-on-demand, pinned version, telemetry disabled, cached — not a bundled dependency.** The producer invokes `npx --yes --package react-doctor@<PIN> -- react-doctor …`; Warden adds **no** `react-doctor` entry to any `package.json`, even though `react-doctor/api` is technically importable. Consequence (a): the oxc native binding never enters Warden's install tree, so **ADR-0003's no-binary-matrix stance stays intact — no amendment needed** (contrast ADR-0041, which _does_ amend it for `warden-chunk` prebuilds). Consequence (b): the published CLI carries `@sentry/node` telemetry, so the producer **always** passes `--no-telemetry` and `--blocking none` (findings must not turn the subprocess exit code into a runner failure). Consequence (c) — the accepted cost: on an offline or cache-cold run the producer cannot fetch, so `warden check` loses the three retired security families until the cache is warm. The producer is **capability-gated and never hard-fails `check`**; absence emits one loud `degradedWorkers` actionable entry ("react-doctor unavailable — N security families skipped; cached after first online run").

5. **Schema: extend `ToolFinding.source`, no `CategoryEnum`/schema ripple.** Add `"react-doctor"` to the `ToolFinding.source` union (`runners/types.ts`), a `mapSeverity` branch (`to-comment.ts`) routing scan families to `{category, tier}`, and a `routeFindingToConcern` branch (`boss-loop.ts`) so PD-multi's Round-0 dispatch routes them. Each diagnostic maps `plugin/rule` to `ruleId`, `filePath` to a repo-relative `file`, and `line`/`column`/`endLine`/`endColumn` to the existing locator fields. The CLI does not supply snippets; the runner may populate optional `ToolFinding.evidence` by reading the cited source line, but tool-only sources remain valid if it leaves `evidence` undefined. `confidence` stays a **`Comment`** field (CONTEXT.md §2), assigned at the `to-comment` layer — ADR-0045's "confidence:1" was shorthand for "sourced assertion, no demotion," needing no `ToolFinding.confidence` field.

6. **Sequencing: Iteration-0 ∥ Iteration-1, independent.** The react-doctor producer emits **sourced** findings that fit warden's _current_ glossary (`finding` = tool-verified, carries a source) — it has **zero dependency on ADR-0044's unbuilt machinery** (no `evidence` field, per-claim-type gate, deterministic degrade, or `reviewRuns` table, none of which PR #26 shipped). So it ships in parallel with **Iteration-0**, the wired-but-un-run ADR-0044 `reasoned-assertions` vs `programmatic-dispatch-multi` A/B (ADR-0044's own prescribed eval gate, ~$20–90). Only the **reasoned-lane** half of ADR-0045 (§4 prompt deltas) depends on ADR-0044, and is gated on the A/B's recall/precision result.

**Why.**

- _The named dependency seam is impossible; the chosen one is the most-precedented._ `@react-doctor/api` is private; the importable `react-doctor/api` subpath does not expose the CLI's `scope` / baseline contract and would force the heavy package dependency anyway. The CLI `--json` output is the public contract that carries the report Warden needs. Subprocessing it is the exact `tsc` / `npm audit` pattern Warden already runs.
- _One call, whole corpus, plus the coherence lever when base metadata exists._ The CLI returns visitor + scan + dead-code in a single invocation and can return introduced-only diagnostics when it can resolve the baseline. The two-producer in-process split would miss scan/delta with the original package names, and the importable `react-doctor/api` subpath still lacks the CLI's scope controls.
- _npx keeps warden light and keeps ADR-0003 intact._ No native binary in warden's tree, no install-weight regression for a CLI whose only caller is a subprocess.
- _Single source per family is the coherence bar._ Two security producers firing on the same line is precisely the incoherence this iteration exists to remove.

**Ripple (doc + ADR sweep, to land with implementation).**

- **ADR-0045** — §2 superseded: the two in-process producers (`react-doctor-lint` + `react-doctor-scan`) become one CLI-subprocess producer; §Ripple's "`@react-doctor/api`" dep and §Status's implementation locus are corrected; the reasoned/overlay lanes (§4–§5) are unchanged.
- **ADR-0028** — generalized: the ESLint-Node-API detector pattern is joined by a second _subprocess_ detector; the in-process choice was plugin-specific, not a rule.
- **ADR-0008 / M13** — `eslint-security.ts` trims to five rules; CONTEXT.md §5's **ESLint security detector** rule list updates; the three retired families are now react-doctor-sourced.
- **ADR-0003 / ADR-0041** — explicitly _untouched_: npx-on-demand keeps the oxc binary out of warden's tree, so no binary-matrix amendment is incurred here.
- **CONTEXT.md** — §5 adds a **react-doctor CLI runner** detector + the `react-doctor` `ToolFinding.source`, and trims the **ESLint security detector** list; §6 nuances **provider-readiness** (the offline-cold-start gap for react-doctor-sourced families).
- **`docs/dogfood-backlog.md`** — the upstream-authored backend rules (ADR-0045 §3) are consumed through this one producer, not a `react-doctor-lint`/`-scan` pair.

**Implementation sequence (tightened).**

1. **Contract smoke first.** Pin `REACT_DOCTOR_CLI_VERSION = "0.5.6"` and add a smoke that runs `npx --yes --package react-doctor@0.5.6 -- react-doctor --json --json-compact --no-telemetry --blocking none --scope lines --changed-files-from <tmp>` against a no-React fixture and a tiny React fixture. Assert the top-level JSON envelope (`schemaVersion`, `ok`, `diagnostics[]`, `summary`) and that `projects: []` is a clean zero-finding result.
2. **Runner module.** Add `packages/core/src/runners/react-doctor.ts`: write a newline-delimited temp changed-file list from Warden's pruned `changedPaths`; spawn via `spawnCapture` with a **60s timeout** and **per-verb npx (§R2): `review` → `npx --yes`, `check` → `npx --no-install`** (cache-only, fail-fast — keeps the fast floor offline-friendly, `tsc --no-install` precedent); parse stdout with the local Zod schema; translate diagnostics to `ToolFinding` (`source: "react-doctor"`, `ruleId: "${plugin}/${rule}"`, repo-relative file, locator range); collect `projects[].skippedChecks` into warning degraded entries; parse mismatch / unavailable npx becomes one actionable `react-doctor` degraded entry, not a throw.
3. **Scope metadata.** Extend `ResolvedDiff` / `ReviewInput` / `DetPriorsInput` with optional baseline metadata from `resolveDiff()` before enabling `--scope changed`. Until that metadata is present, `review` uses the same `--scope lines` path as `check`; no code should claim introduced-only react-doctor results for stdin or unknown-base diffs.
4. **Wire and route.** Add the runner to `runDetPriors()`'s `Promise.all` (gated on `WARDEN_REACT_DOCTOR`, default off), append findings/degraded, add `"react-doctor"` to `ToolFinding.source`, and map react-doctor's coarse `category`: **Security→`{security, tier 1}`** (all Security tier-1 per ADR-0028 §7, eval-gated per family), **Bugs→`{correctness, tier 2}`**, **Performance→`{scalability, tier 2}`**, **Maintainability + Accessibility→`{clarity, tier 3}`** (no `CategoryEnum` ripple; unknown category → `clarity`/3). **Drop dead-code findings (§R1).** Route Security → the `security` worker in `boss-loop.ts`; `clarity` findings post but drive no worker dispatch.
5. **Retire overlap at the default-on flip — NOT while the producer is default-off (§R3).** Trimming `security/detect-child-process`, `security/detect-non-literal-fs-filename`, and `no-secrets/no-secrets` from `eslint-security.ts` before react-doctor is default-on would strip three security families from the _default_ config (producer off **and** ESLint rules gone). So the trim lands in the **same change that flips `WARDEN_REACT_DOCTOR` default-on** (after Step 6's gate), with a smoke proving those rules no longer emit and the families are react-doctor-sourced. In the eval window (producer manually on, ESLint rules still present) the three families double-report — tolerable.
6. **Eval gate.** Before default-on, run `pnpm check-types`, `pnpm lint`, parser/runner smokes, the relevant `review-eval` clean fixtures, and at least one `*-misses-*` fixture that should benefit from a react-doctor family. Gate per family if the clean fixture shows FP volume.

**Alternatives.** (1) **In-process `eslint-plugin-react-doctor` only** (visitor rules; rejected — forfeits the 42-rule scan SAST _and_ delta-scoping, reopening both later anyway). (2) **Hybrid: in-process visitor in `check` + CLI scan in `review`** (rejected — two producers that double-report visitor rules unless deduped; the unification the CLI gives for free is the point). (3) **Depend on `react-doctor` and import `react-doctor/api`** (rejected — `DiagnoseOptions` lacks the CLI's `scope` / baseline controls, and the package dependency drags the oxc native binding + `@sentry/node` into every Warden install). (4) **Publish `@react-doctor/api` / `@react-doctor/core` upstream and consume in-process** (rejected — forces react-doctor to expose + semver-commit APIs it deliberately marked `private`; cross-repo release coupling; and the CLI `--json` is already the stable contract Warden needs). (5) **Hard-pin `react-doctor` as a required dependency just for its exported types** (rejected — same install-weight / ADR-0003 problem for type sugar; use a local minimal schema instead). (6) **Keep both security producers, dedup post-hoc by `(path,line)`** (rejected — two sources of truth; a `(path,line)` merge mis-collapses two distinct real findings on one line). (7) **Vendor react-doctor's scan rules into Warden** (rejected — forks a FP-tuned corpus, the exact reuse-don't-duplicate logic ADR-0045 exists to honor).

**Caveats.** _Contract coupling:_ Warden depends on the CLI's JSON shape and flag surface — pin the version, Zod-validate the parsed report, and degrade (not crash) on a parse mismatch. The visible flags are `--json`, `--json-compact`, `--scope`, `--no-telemetry`, and `--blocking`; `--changed-files-from` is hidden in 0.5.6, so the smoke test must fail loudly if it disappears. _Baseline coupling:_ `--scope changed` is only a true introduced-only filter when react-doctor receives a usable base via the verified **`--base <ref>` flag** (`resolve-scope.ts` reads `flags.base` → merge-base delta). There is **no** `REACT_DOCTOR_BASE_SHA` / `GITHUB_BASE_REF` env path — that earlier claim was falsified against the source (2026-06-16 plan grill). Warden threads the ref from `resolveDiff()` through `ReviewInput` (§R-base / plan Decision 1); when no base resolves (stdin / unknown-base diffs) `review` falls back to `--scope lines` and makes no introduced-only claim. _Offline floor gap:_ the three retired security families silently miss on a cache-cold offline `check`; the loud `degradedWorkers` entry is the only mitigation (no Warden-native fallback — the M13 rules are deleted, per Decision 3). _False positives:_ react-doctor is React/FP-tuned, so on backend/non-React TS some families mis-fire; every family clears Warden's `review-eval` clean-fixture "0 unlabeled comments" gate (ADR-0031 gate c) before default-on, gated per-family. _Telemetry:_ always `--no-telemetry`; treat any future CLI flag drift as a supply-chain review item. _npx fragility:_ resolution/version pinning across package managers and proxies needs a smoke test.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-16, via a `/grill-with-docs` pass over ADR-0045's implementation seam (decisions confirmed by the owner: CLI-subprocess seam, RD-wins overlap retirement, npx-on-demand runtime). Follow-up tightening on 2026-06-16 verified the public npm surface: `react-doctor@0.5.6` and `eslint-plugin-react-doctor@0.5.6` publish; `@react-doctor/api` / `@react-doctor/core` 404; `react-doctor` exposes `react-doctor/api` but without CLI `scope` / baseline controls. Amends ADR-0045 §2/§Ripple/§Status; generalizes ADR-0028; trims M13's `eslint-security.ts`; leaves ADR-0003/0041 untouched; revises CONTEXT.md §5/§6. Implementation locus: one `react-doctor-cli` producer in `packages/core/src/runners/react-doctor.ts` wired from `packages/core/src/review-harness/det-priors.ts` (via `runners/_shared.ts:spawnCapture`, temp `--changed-files-from`, local Zod report parse), `"react-doctor"` in `runners/types.ts` + `to-comment.ts` + `boss-loop.ts` routing, optional baseline metadata threaded from `diff/source.ts` through `ReviewInput` before enabling true `--scope changed`, the 3-rule trim in `runners/eslint-security.ts`, a pinned `REACT_DOCTOR_CLI_VERSION` constant, and the capability-gate + `degradedWorkers` surface. Iteration-1 ships in parallel with the Iteration-0 reasoned A/B; eval-gated (ADR-0031 clean-fixture + `*-misses-*`) before default-on. No code at commit time. **Implementation plan + refinements (2026-06-16, Iteration-1 `/grill-with-docs`):** full brief at `react-doctor-iteration-1-plan.md`. Refinements layered on the sequence above: **§R1** — the single call excludes dead-code (`--scope full`-only; dropped in favor of warden's `deadcode` detector, `--scope full` deferred to ADR-0038 `xhigh`); **§R2** — per-verb npx (`--yes` in `review`, `--no-install` cache-only in `check`); **§R3** — the 3-rule ESLint trim rides the default-on flip, not Iteration-1 (avoids a default-config security-floor gap); base ref threads via the verified **`--base` flag** (the `REACT_DOCTOR_BASE_SHA`/`GITHUB_BASE_REF` env claim was falsified against source); category→`{category,tier}` mapping locked (Security/1, Bugs/2, Perf/2, Maint+a11y→clarity/3, no `CategoryEnum` ripple); ships behind `WARDEN_REACT_DOCTOR` (default off).

---

## ADR-0047 — Reasoned-finding precision controls: false-positive traps, refutation context, proof-bearing evidence, and an ADR-0015 carve-out path

**Context.** On 2026-06-17, Warden dogfooding on `99Yash/alfred#131` produced 12 findings, and the user refuted 8 as false positives by reading the code. The misses were not random. The cited line was real in every case, so the current substring-verifier did exactly what it was designed to do: anti-fabrication, not soundness. Follow-up mapping of the fixture labels to the pinned PR diff showed two precision failures. Four comments targeted lines outside added hunks and should have been dropped deterministically by the review surface. Four comments were on changed hunks, but the claim failed because a second piece of code refuted it:

1. `classify.ts` second-pass mutation — same-function control flow: `working = secondPass` happens only after the second pass succeeds; the catch path still sees `firstPass`.
2. `reasoning-section.tsx` boolean threshold — pure boolean misread: below both thresholds is `!(len || dur)`.
3. `sender-context.ts` no-reply case bypass — caller invariant: `parseFromHeader` lowercases `localPart`.
4. `approval-card.tsx` busy state — runtime lifecycle: Replicache removes the successful card from the queue, unmounting it.
5. `sanitizeAssist` length check — intent: the resolved text is what renders, so the post-resolution length is the bounded value.
6. `dry-run-triage-backfill.ts` nullable sender — callee contract: `resolveSenderRelationship` guards null internally.
7. `sender-relationship.ts` null metadata — callee contract: `parsePersonEntityMetadata` does `safeParse(raw ?? {})`.
8. `user-authored-brief.ts` transcript omission — executor contract: transcript is updated only when `result.transcript !== undefined`.

Four of the eight are out-of-diff comment-scope failures (`classify` x2, `approval-card`, `user-authored-brief`). Four are changed-hunk reasoned-soundness failures (`reasoning-section`, `sender-context`, `dry-run-triage-backfill`, `sender-relationship`). This is a precision failure in the reasoned lane ADR-0044 expands, not a recall failure and not a detector-lane gap, but the cheapest first lever is deterministic diff scoping before deeper refutation-context injection.

**Decision.** Tighten the reasoned lane before making reasoned assertions the default.

0. **LLM comments are scoped to added diff lines.** Detector findings already use `scopeToDiff()` before becoming comments. LLM-authored worker/boss comments now get the same range-overlap rule after citation verification: keep a comment only when `[lineStart,lineEnd]` overlaps an added line in the diff for `file`; drop out-of-diff comments and surface an info-level degraded entry. Workers may still read caller/callee context outside the diff, but the rendered review surface stays anchored to introduced code.

1. **`review-eval` gains first-class false-positive traps.** Fixture labels may now use `expect: absent`; a matching comment is a forbidden hit, not a caught recall label. The aggregate threshold gains a zero-hit false-positive trap gate with max/any-sample semantics, not median semantics: a known false positive recurring in 1 of 3 samples is still a failure. Seed it with `packages/cli/scripts/eval/fixtures/real-prs/alfred-pr131-falsepos-9349d565`, the eight PR#131 refutations above. This gives ADR-0044's "measure precision it costs" clause a concrete mechanism instead of relying on clean fixtures only. The fixture records the mixed hunk anchoring and needs a keyed baseline run to record per-trap reproduction before it becomes load-bearing calibration data.

2. **Inject deterministic refutation context into worker prompts.** Do not make workers discover the obvious callee/caller bodies by optional `readFile`/`grepRepo` calls. Promote ADR-0018's deferred "AST-verified symbol-ref signal" from "if dogfooding shows precision is too low" to scheduled reasoned-lane work. Start with a bounded TS implementation behind the worker prompt assembly: same-file containing function, directly-called function bodies from the hunk, and callers of changed exported functions when cheap to resolve. Widen only when the changed-hunk false-positive traps prove the narrower module is shallow.

3. **Reasoned assertion `evidence` must be proof-bearing.** ADR-0044 split `evidence` from `sources[]`, but PR#131 shows that "quote the suspicious line" is not enough. A reasoned assertion's evidence must include the code that proves the bug: source and sink, missing guard and callee contract, assignment order and catch path, caller raw input and callee expectation. When the worker can locate only a suspicious line but not the proof, it emits `kind: "question"` or nothing. This is still deterministic anti-fabrication plus worker judgment; it is not a universal source gate.

4. **ADR-0015 keeps its sourced-finding rule, but reasoned findings get a carve-out path.** ADR-0015 rejected DeepSec's second-agent revalidation because sourced findings have a real oracle: re-fetch OSV, re-run the tool, re-query `.d.ts`. A reasoned finding has no such external oracle; the judgment is the artifact. If refutation context plus proof-bearing evidence does not clear the PR#131 false-positive fixture, Warden may add a grounded adversarial refutation pass for reasoned findings only. That pass must use the same repo-scoped tools (`readFile`, `grepRepo`, `lookupTypeDef`), default to refuting unless the bug is provable from quoted code, and record its transform in the review trace. It must never revalidate sourced detector/CVE/tool findings.

**Why.**

- _The current controls do not constrain the rendered review surface._ `verifyCitations()` confirms the quoted snippet exists anywhere in the repo tree, but it does not ensure the comment is anchorable to an added line. Detector findings had this guard; LLM comments did not.
- _The current controls do not look at the refuting code._ Once a comment is on a changed line, substring verification still only proves the cited line exists; self-reported confidence cannot catch a worker confidently missing a callee; volume cap is orthogonal.
- _More det-priors and react-doctor do not address the changed-line class._ React-doctor's deterministic corpus improves sourced coverage; it does not make a reasoned claim survive caller/callee contracts.
- _Context injection is the deepest module change._ The current worker interface exposes a tiny diff-window plus optional tools, making every worker re-solve context discovery. A deterministic refutation-context module concentrates that complexity once and gives every worker the same locality and leverage.
- _The second-judge carve-out is narrower than DeepSec._ The pass is permitted only for reasoned findings, only after deterministic controls are measured, and only as a refutation pass over quoted code. It does not become a general LLM-judges-LLM correctness gate.

**Implementation sequence.**

1. Land LLM-comment added-line scoping, eval support, and the PR#131 false-positive fixture.
2. Run `pnpm eval --fixture alfred-pr131-falsepos-9349d565 --config reasoned-assertions --samples 1` once with keys to capture the current failure shape, then repeat with the current default config for baseline noise. Record per-trap forbidden counts; traps that never reproduce are regression guards, not calibration data.
3. Prototype deterministic refutation-context injection in the worker prompt assembly, not in individual worker prompts. Keep the first module TS-only and bounded to one-hop caller/callee/same-function context.
4. Re-run the PR#131 fixture and compare forbidden hits, cost, and dispatch count. Only widen the context module if the fixture still fails for the changed-line structural cases.
5. Implement ADR-0044's real `evidence` field and update worker prompts so assertions must cite proof-bearing evidence. Re-run the `*-misses-*` and `*-falsepos-*` fixtures before flipping reasoned assertions on by default.
6. If the false-positive fixture still fails after steps 3-5, design the reasoned-only adversarial refutation pass as a separate implementation ADR section before coding it.

**Non-goals.**

- No new `CategoryEnum` slot for "false positive" or "refutation"; this is evaluation and harness control, not output taxonomy.
- No prompt-only fix. Prompt guidance may help, but the failure was missing context at the worker interface.
- No detector-lane reshuffle. Sourced findings keep ADR-0015's source re-verification model.
- No broad SOTA suite. This stays inside `review-eval`; the public benchmark milestone remains deferred.

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-17. LLM-comment added-line scoping (`scopeCommentsToDiff()`), eval support for `expect: absent` labels with max/any-sample gate semantics, and the `alfred-pr131-falsepos-9349d565` fixture landed with this ADR. A keyed baseline run has not yet been recorded. Refutation-context injection, proof-bearing `evidence`, and the reasoned-only adversarial refutation pass are implementation follow-ups gated by the fixture results.

---

## ADR-0048 — Observability layer: a live OTEL→self-hosted-Langfuse dev surface, durable review-run identity, and dropped-candidate trace events (operationalizes ADR-0044 §7)

**Context.** Iterating on recall — the `diligent` worker variant, ADR-0044's reasoned lane, ADR-0047's refutation context, levers B/C in `to-issues/` — is blind. The CLI surfaces only the final `Comment[]`, cost, and `degraded[]`. Nothing shows, per worker, which files it `readFile`'d, what it `grepRepo`'d, how many steps it spent, or which candidate findings it dropped before citation (the `project_warden_recall_is_agency_gap` memory: a worker that never grepped a caller and one that grepped and cleared it look identical in the output). The `project_warden_pr235_openai_headhead` head-to-head — Warden 2 findings (one FP) vs an OpenAI staff-prompt harness's 5 substantive on the same diff — is the standing evidence that recall is the bet, and recall iteration needs instrumentation.

Warden has had a deliberate **defer-hosted-observability** posture (ADR-0017's invariant is _cascade-transition_ observability via `FormatterEvent`/`DegradedEntry`; ADR-0032 deferred retrieval observability "until dogfood evidence"; the `review-observability` to-issue recommended local-trace-first). This ADR overrides that posture for the development surface specifically: making Warden the best code-review agent now depends on seeing _how_ a review was produced, end to end, and comparing that across eval runs.

ADR-0044 §7 already designed half of this and must not be reopened by accident. It specs a **review trace** — a read-model derived from `ReviewScratchpad` at the end of `runReviewHarness()` — persisted to a `reviewRuns`-shaped table mirroring `securityRuns`, recording the deterministic pipeline facts (dispatches `(file, concern, tier, toolCalls[])`, per-finding `{provenance, confidence, kind, evidenceVerified, sources[].type}`, and the deterministic transforms that changed the output: confidence→kind degrades, verifier drops, volume-cap discards, lane-discipline drops). That trace is **the trust spine: local, descriptive, prose-free, and never a gate** — it explicitly excludes the boss's free-text reasoning to avoid re-importing the LLM-judges-LLM smell, with dashboard rendering deferred to ADR-0039 Phase 4. Alfred (`../alfred`) ships a working precedent: a `metered()` chokepoint that opens a Langfuse span per billable call, gated on keys, grouping by `runId`, with `LANGFUSE_CAPTURE_IO` PII gating and a self-hosted Docker stack. Warden has **no `metered()` chokepoint** — it routes all AI SDK through `@warden/ai`, makes `streamText` calls directly in `boss-loop.ts` / `workers/run-worker.ts` / `workers/dispatch.ts`, and computes cost _post-hoc by tier_ in `harness.ts:computeCosts`. A verbatim port does not fit.

**Decision.** Add a live, development-time observability surface alongside ADR-0044 §7's persisted trust-spine trace, and give both a durable run identity.

1. **Two surfaces, one run identity — complements ADR-0044 §7, does not reopen it.** ADR-0044's review trace stays THE trust spine: local, descriptive, prose-free, never gates, persisted. ADR-0048's **Langfuse surface** is a _separate, non-authoritative, dev-time_ debugging + cross-run-diffing surface. Both hang off the same `reviewRuns` row + run-id. Langfuse never becomes the audit artifact; the audit read-model never depends on Langfuse being up.

2. **Run identity — operationalizes ADR-0044 §7's `reviewRuns` table, with a split key.** Ship the `reviewRuns` table now (`.warden/cache.sqlite`, Drizzle, cloud-compatible via ADR-0016 interfaces). `reviewRuns.id` = random `createId("run")` — the durable run identity and the Langfuse trace-grouping key (mirrors `securityRuns.id`). Additionally `reviewRuns.input_hash` = content-addressed hash over `(diff_hash, resolved config, sorted model-set)` — the dedup/resume lookup key. The split is deliberate: a random id keeps two genuine re-runs of the same diff as distinct rows (cross-run diffing needs that history), while `input_hash` lets a future resume path recognise "same review." Run-id is minted once in `runReviewHarness()` and threaded to workers via `dispatch_worker` and to the eval harness (which tags traces by config/fixture/sample).

3. **Substrate is OTEL-native; `core` stays Langfuse-agnostic.** The AI SDK's `experimental_telemetry: { isEnabled, functionId, metadata: { runId, role, concern, tier, file } }` is set on the three `streamText` sites. It auto-emits OTEL spans for every LLM call **and every tool call** (`readFile` / `grepRepo` / `lookupTypeDef` appear as child spans with their args) — the exact per-worker investigation signal recall iteration needs, for near-zero per-call code. The OTEL bootstrap (a `NodeSDK` + span exporter) lives **only in `@warden/ai`** (the package boundary that already owns every AI-SDK touchpoint); `@warden/core` sets telemetry metadata but never imports Langfuse or an exporter. Export target is a self-hosted Langfuse instance via an OTEL `SpanExporter` (the `langfuse-vercel` `LangfuseExporter`, which maps AI-SDK span conventions to Langfuse generations, or raw OTLP to Langfuse's OTel endpoint — exact package settled at implementation). Because the CLI is a short-lived process, the exporter is **force-flushed on exit** (mirrors alfred's `flushLangfuse`), or spans are lost.

4. **Dropped-candidate events reuse ADR-0044 §7's read-model — same data, two sinks.** The deterministic transforms ADR-0044 §7 already enumerates are emitted as OTEL **span events** under the active worker/boss span: lane-discipline path drops (`run-worker.ts:84`), uncited-finding drops (`run-worker.ts:235`, `droppedUncited`), off-hunk / non-patch-line scope drops (`comment-scope.ts:32`, `droppedCount`; ADR-0047 §0 `scopeCommentsToDiff()`), volume-cap discards, and confidence→kind degrades. There is one source — the scratchpad read-model — and two sinks: the persisted trust-spine trace (ADR-0044) and the live Langfuse span events (this ADR). This closes the gap that generic OTEL tool-spans cannot: a dropped candidate never becomes a tool call, so we emit it explicitly.

5. **Per-call cost is warden-computed.** Attach a per-call `costUsd` span attribute computed from `@warden/ai`'s model-catalog prices for the served model. Do not rely on Langfuse's own pricing config (it may not carry `claude-opus-4-8` etc.). Warden's post-hoc tier summary (`harness.ts:computeCosts`) stays the source of truth; the spans mirror it at per-call granularity so a single worker's cost is legible.

6. **Scope: self-hosted only; capture I/O ON; prose carve-out from ADR-0044 §7.** v0 binds to a local Docker Langfuse stack — **no Langfuse Cloud**, because the diff and repo source flow into prompts and a code-review tool must not ship other people's source off-box. I/O capture (full prompt/completion bodies, **including boss reasoning prose**) defaults **ON** when keys are present, gated by env (`WARDEN_LANGFUSE_CAPTURE_IO`) so a future CI/cloud run can flip it off. The carve-out is explicit: ADR-0044 §7's _prose-free_ invariant binds the **persisted trust-spine trace only**. Langfuse is non-authoritative dev tooling on a self-hosted box; capturing prose there for debugging violates nothing ADR-0044 protects, because that prose never enters the audit read-model and never decides what posts.

7. **Emission gating: keys-present = on, else total no-op.** Absent `LANGFUSE_PUBLIC_KEY` / `LANGFUSE_SECRET_KEY` (CI, local dev without the stack) → the exporter is never constructed and `experimental_telemetry` stays off; the call path is branch-free and unchanged. Identical posture to alfred's lazy-noop client.

8. **Resume is designed-but-deferred (no code this ADR).** `reviewRuns.input_hash` plus a per-worker content-addressed sub-key `(concern, sorted dispatched files, prompt-hash, model)` is the natural cache/resume key. The contract: cache completed _worker outputs_; on resume of a matching `input_hash`, replay completed workers and re-enter the boss loop; boss-round checkpointing is a later layer. This **supersedes the dead `llm_review_cache` (ADR-0007)** as the resume substrate — that table was wired to zero consumers and predates the M14 boss/worker harness. No resume code ships here; it is a scheduled follow-up the run identity unblocks.

**Why.**

- _Recall is the bet, and the bet is blind without this._ Every open lever (diligent, B/C, ADR-0047's refutation context) is a hypothesis about worker behaviour the current output can't show. The head-to-head memory is the evidence; per-worker traces + cross-run diffing are the instrument that turns "diligent scored ~1/5" into "diligent's day_shape worker grepped the caller, PD-multi's didn't."
- _OTEL over a Langfuse-SDK port keeps the package boundary._ AI SDK telemetry auto-instruments tool calls (the signal we want) for a flag, and OTEL leaves `core` Langfuse-agnostic with a swappable backend — honoring the `@warden/ai`-owns-the-SDK boundary. Porting alfred's `metered()` would mean hand-rolled spans at three sites and a `langfuse` dep in `core`, for a chokepoint warden's post-hoc cost model doesn't have.
- _Complement, don't reopen._ ADR-0044 §7 paid for the hard part (the read-model, the `reviewRuns` shape, the never-gates invariant). This ADR operationalizes that table and adds the live surface 0044 deferred — the two-surface split is what lets prose capture coexist with the prose-free trust spine.
- _Self-hosted is non-negotiable for a code-review tool._ Source in prompts means the box must own the trace store. That single constraint also makes capture-ON safe, which is what "investigate everything" needs.
- _Decide the run identity now, defer resume._ Same MO as ADR-0015/0016/0044: the run-id + `input_hash` shape is cheap now and expensive to retrofit once traces and a cache key off it; full resume is a separable build.

**ADR-0005 note.** ADR-0005's single-SDK invariant governs the _LLM_ SDK (the AI SDK). OpenTelemetry is telemetry infrastructure, not an LLM provider SDK, and the Langfuse exporter is isolated to `@warden/ai`; adding `@opentelemetry/*` (+ a Langfuse exporter) does not violate the AI-SDK-only rule. Flagged so the dep addition isn't read as a breach.

**Alternatives.** (1) Local-first JSON `--trace` dump, defer Langfuse (the to-issue's original recommendation) — rejected for v0: it can't do the cross-run/eval diffing and flame-graph inspection that recall iteration needs, and ADR-0044 §7's read-model already covers the local-audit case. (2) Port alfred's `metered()` chokepoint with the `langfuse` SDK — rejected: warden has no per-call chokepoint, it would put a Langfuse dep in `core`, and it duplicates cost logic warden computes post-hoc. (3) Langfuse subsumes ADR-0044's local trace (one surface) — rejected: couples the trust spine to a dev tool and contaminates the prose-free audit invariant. (4) Capture spans/tokens but no prose, even in Langfuse — rejected: defeats "investigate everything" on a self-hosted box where prose is the most diagnostic signal; the carve-out makes prose safe. (5) Support Langfuse Cloud via `LANGFUSE_HOST` — rejected for v0: ships source off-box. (6) Random-only or content-only run id — rejected: random loses dedup/resume, content-only collapses run history needed for cross-run diffing; the split keeps both.

**Caveats.** OTEL + AI-SDK-telemetry → Langfuse span mapping is the implementation risk: the AI SDK emits its own semantic conventions, and the exporter (`langfuse-vercel` vs raw OTLP) must map them to Langfuse generations/cost correctly — verify with a real review before declaring it works. Short-lived-process flush is a sharp edge (unflushed spans vanish). Capture-ON means a self-hosted Langfuse volume holds reviewed source; the Docker stack secrets are local throwaways and must never be reused for any hosted deploy (per alfred's compose warning). When the `reviewRuns` migration lands it must follow `db:generate` → `db:migrate`; the row should be written best-effort and must never block or fail a review. Per-call cost depends on the model-catalog price for the _served_ model being current.

**Relationships.** Operationalizes ADR-0044 §7 (`reviewRuns` table, dropped-candidate signals from the review-trace read-model). Complements, does not reopen, ADR-0044 §7's prose-free trust-spine invariant (§1, §6 carve-out). Overrides the defer-hosted-observability posture of ADR-0017 / ADR-0032 / the `review-observability` to-issue for the dev surface specifically. Supersedes ADR-0007's `llm_review_cache` as the resume substrate (§8). Cloud-compatible by construction via ADR-0016 storage interfaces. Dashboard rendering stays ADR-0039 Phase 4. Adds glossary terms to CONTEXT.md §2 / a new observability section (**review run**, **run-id**, **input-hash**, **dropped-candidate event**, **observability surface** vs **review trace**).

**Status.** Direction adopted 2026-06-21. **Wired 2026-06-22** (issue #32): the `reviewRuns` table + run-id mint/thread + best-effort persistence (§2), the OTEL bootstrap + `LangfuseExporter` isolated to `@warden/ai`/`observability.ts` (§3), `experimental_telemetry` on both review `streamText` sites (boss-loop + run-worker — `workers/dispatch.ts` routes, it does not call `streamText`) grouped by `langfuseTraceId`=run-id (§3), dropped-candidate span events at the lane/uncited/off-hunk sites (§4), keys-present-else-no-op gating (§7), capture-IO default-on (§6), and CLI force-flush on exit (§3). Verified by the keys-absent no-op + `reviewRuns` round-trip smoke (`smoke:adr-0048-observability`) and a keys-present bootstrap→telemetry→flush run without a live collector. **Still deferred:** the live span→Langfuse mapping against the Docker stack + a real review (the eval/cross-run-diff acceptance signal — _not_ a fixture gate), per-call cost on spans (§5), per-worker output cache + resume (§8, issue #33), Langfuse Cloud support, and dashboard rendering (ADR-0039 Phase 4).
